i turn them into two and threedimensional pieces and sculptures and installations .	我把它們變成二維立體的零件 , 雕塑和裝置藝術 。
upon working with the plastic , after about the first eight years , some of my work started to fissure and break down into smaller little bits of plastic .	在大約八年後 , 我開始用塑膠工作 , 我的工作開始變得裂縫 , 分解成更小的塑膠塊 。
and i thought , " great .	我心想: 「 太好了 ,
it's ephemeral just like us . "	它和我們一樣短暫 。 」
upon educating myself a little further about plastics , i actually realized this was a bad thing .	在我對塑膠的教育進一步了解之後 , 我發現這是件壞事 。
it's a bad thing that plastic breaks down into smaller little bits , because it's always still plastic .	塑膠被分解成小塊的壞東西因為它總是被塑膠分解
and what we're finding is that a lot of it is in the marine environment .	我們發現 , 很多都在海洋環境裡 。
i then , in the last few years , learned about the pacific garbage patch and the gyre .	接著 , 在過去幾年 , 我了解到太平洋垃圾帶和垃圾漩渦 。
and my initial reaction and i think this is a lot of people's first reaction to learning about it is , " oh my god !	而我的初始反應──我認為這是很多人第一次學到這個的反應──就是: 「 我的天 !
we've got to go out there and clean this thing up . "	我們必須去那裡清理這些東西 。 」
so i actually developed a proposal to go out with a cargo ship and two decommissioned fishing trawlers , a crane , a chipping machine and a coldmolding machine .	所以 , 我真的開發了一個提案 , 用一艘貨船和兩艘退休的漁船拖網、一座起重機、一座磨碎機 , 和一台冷模機出去 。
and my intention was to go out to the gyre , raise awareness about this issue and begin to pick up the plastic , chip it into little bits and cold mold it into bricks that could potentially be used as building materials in underdeveloped communities .	而我的意圖便是去到垃圾漩渦那裏 , 喚起大家對此議題的認知 , 開始把塑膠撈起來 , 一塊一塊一小塊碎片 , 冷塑成磚以後可能被用作建築材料的磚塊 , 在未開發的社區內 。
i began talking with people who actually had been out to the gyre and were studying the plastic problem in the marine environment and upon doing so , i realized actually that cleaning it up would be a very small drop in the bucket relative to how much is being generated every day around the world , and that actually i needed to back up and look at the bigger picture .	我開始跟實際去過垃圾漩渦並且研究海洋環境裡的塑膠問題接著我發現把塑膠清理乾淨原理相較於全世界每天製造的量 , 我需要重新檢視並檢視更大的圖像
and the bigger picture is: we need to find a way to turn off the faucet .	更大的情況是:我們需要找到一種方法來關掉水龍頭 。
we need to cut the spigot of singleuse and disposable plastics , which are entering the marine environment every day on a global scale .	我們需要削減單次使用及丟棄的塑膠 , 這些塑膠每天以全球的規模進入海洋環境中 。
so in looking at that , i also realized that i was really angry .	所以 , 看著這一點 , 我發現我真的很憤怒 。
i wasn't just concerned about plastic that you're trying to imagine out in the middle of the pacific ocean of which i have learned there are now 11 gyres , potentially , of plastic in five major oceans in the world .	我擔心的不只是塑膠你試著想像在太平洋中間我學到了有11個塑膠垃圾漩渦 , 可能是世界上五大洋的塑膠垃圾 。
it's not just that gyre of plastic that i'm concerned about it's the gyre of plastic in the supermarket .	我關心的不只是塑膠垃圾的漩渦而是超級市場裡塑膠的漩渦
i'd go to the supermarket and all of my food is packaged in plastic .	我會去超市 , 我所有的食物都是塑膠包裝 。
all of my beverages are packaged in plastic , even at the health food market .	我所有的飲料都是用塑膠包裝的 , 即使是在健康食品市場也一樣 。
i'm also concerned about the plastic in the refrigerator , and i'm concerned about the plastic and the toxins that leach from plastic into us and into our bodies .	我也很關心冰箱裡的塑膠還有從塑膠流入我們體內的毒素
so i came together with a group of other people who were all looking at this issue , and we created the plastic pollution coalition .	所以我和一群其他的人一起 , 他們都在研究這個議題 , 我們成立了 「 塑膠污染聯盟 」 。
we have many initiatives that we're working on , but some of them are very basic .	我們有許多倡議 , 其中有一些是非常基本的 。
one is: if 80 to 90 percent of what we're finding in the ocean of the marine debris that we're finding in the ocean is plastic , then why don't we call it what it is .	其一是:如果我們在海裡找到的海洋碎片中有80%到90%都是塑膠那麽我們就稱之為 " 海洋碎片 " 。
recycling everybody kind of ends their books about being sustainable and greening with the idea of recycling .	回收每個人這類型的書 , 都是以永續經營及綠化的觀念來結尾再利用資源回收的概念 。
you put something in a bin and you don't have to think about it again .	把東西放進一個桶子裡 , 再也不用想了 。
what is the reality of that ?	那樣的現實真貌是什麼 ?
in the united states , less than seven percent of our plastics are recycled .	在美國 , 塑膠回收的比率不到7%
and if you really look into it , particularly when it comes to plastic bottles , most of it is only downcycled , or incinerated , or shipped to china .	如果你真的去研究它 , 特別是當談到塑膠瓶時 , 大部分只會被降級回收 , 或是燒掉 , 或是運到中國去 。
it is downcycled and turned into lesser things , while a glass bottle can be a glass bottle again or can be used again a plastic bottle can never be a plastic bottle again .	它被降下 , 轉變成更小的東西 , 而玻璃瓶卻可以再次成為玻璃瓶 , 或是再次使用一個塑膠瓶 , 永遠不會再被當作塑膠瓶 。
so this is a big issue for us .	所以這對我們來說是個大問題 。
another thing that we're looking at and asking people to think about is we've added a fourth r onto the front of the " reduce , reuse , recycle , " three r's , and that is refuse .	我們在看的另一件事是叫大家想一想我們在 " 減量、再利用、回收 " 的前面再加上了第四個r " , 那就拒絕了
whenever possible , refuse singleuse and disposable plastics .	無論何時 , 拒絕單次使用和丟棄的塑膠品
alternatives exist ; some of them are very oldschool .	替代方案是存在的 ; 有些是很老派的 。
i myself am now collecting these cool pyrex containers and using those instead of glad and tupperware containers to store food in .	我自己現在在收集這些很酷的pyrex容器 , 用它們來代替glad和tupperware存放的容器 。
and i know that i am doing a service to myself and my family .	我也知道 , 我在為自己和家人服務 。
it's very easy to pick up a stainlesssteel bottle or a glass bottle , if you're traveling and you've forgotten to bring your stainlesssteel bottle and fill that up with water or filtered water , versus purchasing plastic bottled water .	要拿起一個不銹鋼瓶或玻璃瓶 , 很容易就可以拿起 , 如果你在旅行中 , 而你已經忘了帶上一個不鏽鋼瓶裝水 , 或裝滿水 , 而不是用來買塑膠瓶裝水 。
i guess what i want to say to everybody here and i know that you guys know a lot about this issue is that this is a huge problem in the oceans , but this is a problem that we've created as consumers and we can solve .	我猜我想在這裡對大家說的──我知道你們都知道這個議題──這個議題在海洋中是很大的問題 , 但這是我們身為消費者所創造的問題 , 且我們能解決的問題 。
we can solve this by raising awareness of the issue and teaching people to choose alternatives .	我們能解決這個問題 , 做法是提高人們對議題的意識 , 並教導人們選擇替代方案 。
so whenever possible , to choose alternatives to singleuse plastics .	所以 , 若可能的話 , 可以選擇用單一用塑膠的替代品 。
we can cut the stem tide the stem of this into our oceans and in doing so , save our oceans , save our planet , save ourselves .	我們可以把這份資料的根源切割成我們的海洋 , 也因此 , 拯救我們的地球 , 拯救我們自己 。
this demo from pattie maes' lab at mit , spearheaded by pranav mistry was the buzz of ted . it's a wearable device with a projector that paves the way for profound interaction with our environment . imagine " minority report " and then some .	這位在麻省理工學院的帕蒂•馬斯實驗室的展示 , 由帕納•密特里所帶領 , 成為了可穿戴的裝置 , 能夠為我們的環境做深度互動 。 想像 「 關鍵報告 」 , 然後一些 。
demo , design , interface design , technology	示範、設計、界面設計、科技、
pattie maes and pranav mistry demo sixthsense	pattiemaes和panavmitry關於第六感 。
i've been intrigued by this question of whether we could evolve or develop a sixth sense a sense that would give us seamless access and easy access to metainformation or information that may exist somewhere that may be relevant to help us make the right decision about whatever it is that we're coming across .	我一直對這個問題很有興趣:我們能否進化出或發展出第六感 。 這種感覺會讓我們無縫接觸、容易獲取資訊 , 或現存的資訊 , 可能可以協助我們做出正確的決定 , 決定我們要面對的是什麼 。
and some of you may argue , well , don't today's cell phones do that already ?	你們有些人可能會爭辯說 , 嗯 , 不是現今的手機已經在做了嗎 ?
but i would say no .	但我會說不 。
when you meet someone here at ted and this is the top networking place , of course , of the year you don't shake somebody's hand and then say , " can you hold on for a moment while i take out my phone and google you ? "	當你在ted與別人會面時──這可是這一年最佳的網路場所──當然 , 你不會和某人握手 , 然後問: 「 你能不能在我拿出手機和google查詢你一下 ? 」
or when you go to the supermarket and you're standing there in that huge aisle of different types of toilet papers , you don't take out your cell phone , and open a browser , and go to a website to try to decide which of these different toilet papers is the most ecologically responsible purchase to make .	或是當你到超級市場 , 站在那一大排那一大排的不同種類的衛生紙 , 你不會拿出手機 , 打開瀏覽器 , 去瀏覽一個網站 , 試著決定各種不同的衛生紙中哪個購買選擇是最環保的 。
so we don't really have easy access to all this relevant information that can just help us make optimal decisions about what to do next and what actions to take .	所以 , 我們真的無法很容易取得所有這些相關的資訊 , 這些資訊能夠協助我們做出最佳決策 , 決定下一步要做什麼 , 以及要採取什麼行動 。
and so my research group at the media lab has been developing a series of inventions to give us access to this information in a sort of easy way , without requiring that the user changes any of their behavior .	所以 , 我在媒體實驗室的研究小組正在研發一系列的發明 , 讓我們能輕鬆地取得這些資訊 , 且不需要使用者改變他們的行為 。
and i'm here to unveil our latest effort , and most successful effort so far , which is still very much a work in process .	我在此向各位揭露我們最新的努力 , 目前為止最成功的努力 , 這在過程中仍是個大工程 。
i'm actually wearing the device right now and we've sort of cobbled it together with components that are off the shelf and that , by the way , only cost 350 dollars at this point in time .	現在我正穿著這個裝置我們將它和架子外的零件結合在一起順便一提 , 這個裝置現在的價格只有350美元
i'm wearing a camera , just a simple webcam , a portable , batterypowered projection system with a little mirror .	我戴著一台攝影機 , 只是一個簡單的網路攝影機 , 一個攜帶電池電力的投影系統 , 配上一個小鏡子 。
these components communicate to my cell phone in my pocket which acts as the communication and computation device .	這些元件在我口袋裡的手機交流 , 扮演著溝通和運算裝置的角色 。
and in the video here we see my student pranav mistry , who's really the genius who's been implementing and designing this whole system .	在影片中 , 我們看到我的學生帕納•米特里 , 他真的是實施和設計這整個系統的天才 。
and we see how this system lets him walk up to any surface and start using his hands to interact with the information that is projected in front of him .	我們看到這個系統讓他走到任何平面前 , 用他的雙手開始與他面前投射的資訊互動 。
the system tracks the four significant fingers .	系統會追蹤這四隻重要的手指
in this case , he's wearing simple marker caps that you may recognize .	在這個例子中 , 他戴著你可能認得的簡單標記帽
but if you want a more stylish version you could also paint your nails in different colors .	但如果你想要比較時髦的版本你也可以把指甲塗上不同顏色 。
and the camera basically tracks these four fingers and recognizes any gestures that he's making so he can just go to , for example , a map of long beach , zoom in and out , etc .	攝影機基本上能追蹤這四隻手指並且能辨識出他的任何手勢舉例來說 , 他能直接去看長灘的地圖 , 放大和縮小等等 。
the system also recognizes iconic gestures such as the " take a picture " gesture , and then takes a picture of whatever is in front of you .	這個系統還能辨識出具象徵性的手勢 , 例如 「 拍照 」 的手勢 , 然後在你面前拍照 。
and when he then walks back to the media lab , he can just go up to any wall and project all the pictures that he's taken , sort through them and organize them , and resize them , etc . , again using all natural gestures .	接著 , 當他走回媒體實驗室時 , 他可以走到任何一面牆前 , 投影出他拍攝的所有照片 , 分類並整理它們 , 等等 , 再次使用自然的手勢 。
so , some of you most likely were here two years ago and saw the demo by jeff han or some of you may think , " well , doesn't this look like the microsoft surface table ? "	你們有些人可能在兩年前到這裡看到傑夫•漢做的示範或許有些人會想: 「 這不是很像微軟的平面電腦嗎 ? 」
and yes , you also interact using natural gestures , both hands , etc .	沒錯 , 你也用自然的手勢來互動 , 雙手都如此 。
but the difference here is that you can use any surface , you can walk to up to any surface , including your hand if nothing else is available and interact with this projected data .	但差別在於 , 你可以用任何表面 , 你可以走到任何表面上 , 包括你的手 , 如果沒有其他表面可用 , 並和這些投影資料進行互動 。
the device is completely portable , and can be . . .	這裝置完全可攜帶 , 可以變成...
so one important difference is that it's totally mobile .	所以一個重要的不同點是它完全是流動的 。
another even more important difference is that in mass production this would not cost more tomorrow than today's cell phones and would actually not sort of be a bigger packaging could look a lot more stylish than this version that i'm wearing around my neck .	另一個更重要的不同點是:在量產時 , 量產的成本不會比現在的手機更高 , 看起來會比我脖子上戴的版本更時髦 。
but other than letting some of you live out your fantasy of looking as cool as tom cruise in " minority report , " the reason why we're really excited about this device is that it really can act as one of these sixthsense devices that gives you relevant information about whatever is in front of you .	但除了讓你們其中一些人活出你的幻想之外 , 在《關鍵報告》中 , 湯姆•克魯斯的《關鍵報告》中 , 我們之所以會對這個裝置感到興奮 , 是因為它真的可以扮演第六感的裝置之一 , 給你關於你面前事物的任何資訊 。
so we see pranav here going into the supermarket and he's shopping for some paper towels .	所以我們看到帕納進入超級市場 , 準備購買一些紙巾 。
and , as he picks up a product the system can recognize the product that he's picking up , using either image recognition or marker technology , and give him the green light or an orange light .	當他拿起一樣產品--這個系統可以辨識出他撿到的產品 , 用的是影像辨識或是標記技術 , 給他綠燈或橘燈 。
he can ask for additional information .	他可以要求額外的資訊
so this particular choice here is a particularly good choice , given his personal criteria .	所以 , 基於他個人的標準 , 這是個特別好的選擇 。
some of you may want the toilet paper with the most bleach in it rather than the most ecologicallyresponsible choice .	有些人可能會想要有最多漂白劑的衛生紙 , 而不是最環保的選擇 。
if he picks up a book in the bookstore , he can get an amazon rating it gets projected right on the cover of the book .	如果他在書店裡拿起一本書 , 他就可以取得亞馬遜書局的評分 , 它會直接投影在書的封面上 。
this is juan's book , our previous speaker , which gets a great rating , by the way , at amazon .	這是胡安的書 , 我們之前的講者 , 順便說一句 , 在亞馬遜 , 取得很好的評分 。
and so , pranav turns the page of the book and can then see additional information about the book reader comments , maybe sort of information by his favorite critic , etc .	所以 , 帕納翻閱這本書的頁面 , 可以看到更多關於這本書的資訊--讀者評論 , 可能是他最喜歡的評論家等等--
if he turns to a particular page he finds an annotation by maybe an expert of a friend of ours that gives him a little bit of additional information about whatever is on that particular page .	如果他翻到特定的一頁他能找到我們朋友的註解並給予他與那一頁內容相關的額外資訊
reading the newspaper it never has to be outdated .	閱讀報紙時 , 它不必過時 。
you can get video annotations of the event that you're reading about you can get the latest sports scores etc .	你可以收到關於你閱讀事件的影片註解──你可以取得最新的體育比賽分數等等 。
this is a more controversial one .	這個比較有爭議性 。
as you interact with someone at ted , maybe you can see a word cloud of the tags , the words that are associated with that person in their blog and personal web pages .	當你在ted與某人互動時 , 也許你能看到一團團的標籤 , 那些與那個人相關的字來自他們的部落格和個人網頁 。
in this case , the student is interested in cameras , etc .	在這個案例中 , 學生們對攝影機感興趣等等
on your way to the airport , if you pick up your boarding pass , it can tell you that your flight is delayed , that the gate has changed , etc .	在你去機場的路上 , 如果你拿起你的登機證 , 它可以告訴你飛機誤點了 , 登機門已經變了 , 等等 。
and , if you need to know what the current time is it's as simple as drawing a watch on your arm .	而且 , 如果你需要知道現在的時間 , 就跟在你手臂上畫個手錶一樣簡單 。
so that's where we're at so far in developing this sixth sense that would give us seamless access to all this relevant information about the things that we may come across .	所以這就是我們發展出第六感的地方 , 讓我們可以接觸到和我們可能遇到的事物有關的重要資訊 。
my student pranav , who's really , like i said , the genius behind this .	我的學生帕納 , 像我說的 , 他是這背後的天才 。
he does deserve a lot of applause because i don't think he's slept much in the last three months , actually .	他確實應該得到很多掌聲因為我認為過去三個月他睡得不多
and his girlfriend is probably not very happy about him either .	他的女朋友大概也不太高興他 。
but it's not perfect yet , it's very much a work in progress .	但目前它還不完美 , 還在進行中 , 非常大量的工作 。
and who knows , maybe in another 10 years we'll be here with the ultimate sixth sense brain implant .	誰知道呢 ? 也許十年後我們會帶著植入腦內的終極第六感來這裡 。
phyllis rodriguez and aicha elwafi have a powerful friendship born of unthinkable loss . rodriguez' son was killed in the world trade center attacks on september 11 , 2001 ; elwafi's son zacarias moussaoui was convicted of a role in those attacks and is serving a life sentence . in hoping to find peace , these two moms have come to understand and respect one another .	phyllisrodriguez和aichaelwafi有一個強而有力的友誼-是出自於無法想像的損失 。 rodriguez的兒子在世界貿易中心被殺害了 , 2001年9月11日 , 埃爾瓦菲的兒子•莫薩伊被判了一個角色 , 被判了在那些攻擊事件中被判 , 並為此所服務 。 希望找到和平 , 這兩位母親得以此來彼此相互理解 。
culture , global issues , politics	文化、全球議題、政治、
9/11 healing: the mothers who found forgiveness , friendship	9/11治癒:那些找到寬恕、友情的媽媽們 ,
phyllis rodriguez: we are here today because of the fact that we have what most people consider an unusual friendship .	phyllisrodriguez:我們今天來到這裡是因為我們擁有大多數人所認為的不尋常的友誼 。
and yet , it feels natural to us now .	然而 , 現在我們覺得很自然 。
i first learned that my son had been in the world trade center on the morning of september 11th , 2001 .	我第一次知道我的兒子在世界貿易中心在2001年9月11日的早上 。
we didn't know if he had perished yet until 36 hours later .	我們之前並不知道他是否已經死了 , 直到三十六小時之後 。
at the time , we knew that it was political .	當時 , 我們知道那是政治化的 。
we were afraid of what our country was going to do in the name of our son my husband , orlando , and i and our family .	我們很害怕我們的國家將會做些什麼 , 以我們兒子之名---我的丈夫 , 我和我們的家人 。
and when i saw it and yet , through the shock , the terrible shock , and the terrible explosion in our lives , literally , we were not vengeful .	當我看到它時--雖然 , 很震驚 , 很可怕的震驚 , 和我們生活中的可怕的爆炸 , 真的 , 我們沒有被復仇 。
and a couple of weeks later when zacarias moussaoui was indicted on six counts of conspiracy to commit terrorism , and the u . s . government called for a death penalty for him , if convicted , my husband and i spoke out in opposition to that , publicly .	幾週後 , 當zacariasmoussaoui被指控六項恐怖攻擊的陰謀時 , 美國政府要求對他判處死刑 , 如果他被定罪 , 我和我的丈夫對公開反對 。
through that and through human rights groups , we were brought together with several other victims' families .	透過這點以及人權團體 , 我們與其他受害者家屬合作 。
when i saw aicha in the media , coming over when her son was indicted , and i thought , " what a brave woman .	當我在媒體上看到aicha , 當她的兒子被起訴時 , 她走過來 , 我心想: 「 多麼勇敢的女人啊 !
someday i want to meet that woman when i'm stronger . "	我想跟那位女士見面 , 當我強壯一點的時候 。 」
i was still in deep grief ; i knew i didn't have the strength .	我還在深深的悲傷之中 ; 我知道我沒有力量 。
i knew i would find her someday , or we would find each other .	我知道總有一天我會找到她 , 或是我們會找到對方 。
because , when people heard that my son was a victim , i got immediate sympathy .	因為 , 當別人聽到我的兒子是受害者 , 我馬上就得到了同情 。
but when people learned what her son was accused of , she didn't get that sympathy .	但當人們知道她的兒子被指控的是什麼 , 她沒有得到那個同情 。
but her suffering is equal to mine .	但她所受的苦與我的同等重 。
so we met in november 2002 , and aicha will now tell you how that came about .	所以我們在二零零二年十一月相見 , 現在aicha會告訴你那是怎麼回事 。
aicha elwafi: good afternoon , ladies and gentlemen .	aichaelwafi:午安 , 各位先生女士
i am the mother of zacarias moussaoui .	我是zacariasmoussaoui的母親 。
and i asked the organization of human rights to put me in touch with the parents of the victims .	並請求人權組織讓我與受害者的父母取得聯繫 。
so they introduced me to five families .	所以他們介紹我認識五個家庭
and i saw phyllis , and i watched her .	我看到phyllis , 我看著她 。
she was the only mother in the group .	她是這群裡唯一的媽媽
the others were brothers , sisters .	其他都是兄弟姊妹
and i saw in her eyes that she was a mother , just like me .	我從她的眼神中看見她和我一樣是一位母親 。
i suffered a lot as a mother .	我作為一個媽媽很痛苦 。
i was married when i was 14 .	我14歲時就結婚了 。
i lost a child when i was 15 , a second child when i was 16 .	我十五歲的時候失去了一個孩子 , 是我十六歲時失去的第二個孩子 。
so the story with zacarias was too much really .	所以 , 薩卡利亞的故事太多了 。
and i still suffer , because my son is like he's buried alive .	而我依然受苦 , 因為我兒子就像是被活埋了一樣 。
i know she really cried for her son .	我知道她真的為兒子而哭 。
but she knows where he is .	但她知道他在哪裡 。
my son , i don't know where he is .	我的兒子 , 我不知道他在哪裡 。
i don't know if he's alive . i don't know if he's tortured .	我不知道他是否還活著 , 我不知道他是否受到折磨
i don't know what happened to him .	我不知道他發生了什麼事 。
so that's why i decided to tell my story , so that my suffering is something positive for other women .	所以 , 這就是為什麼我決定要說我的故事 , 讓我的苦難能夠帶給其他女性一些正面影響 。
for all the women , all the mothers that give life , you can give back , you can change .	對所有的女人 , 所有賦予生命的媽媽 , 你可以回饋 , 你可以改變 。
it's up to us women , because we are women , because we love our children .	這取決於我們女人 , 因為我們是女人 , 因為我們愛我們的孩子 。
we must be handinhand and do something together .	我們一定要手牽手 , 一起做些什麼 。
it's not against women , it's for us , for us women , for our children .	這不是反對女性 , 而是為了我們 , 為了我們女人 , 為了我們的孩子 。
i talk against violence , against terrorism .	我反對暴力 , 反對恐怖主義 。
i go to schools to talk to young , muslim girls so they don't accept to be married against their will very young .	我去學校跟年青的穆斯林女孩談話 , 這樣她們才不會接受跟她們意志力很年輕結婚的 。
so if i can save one of the young girls , and avoid that they get married and suffer as much as i did , well this is something good .	所以如果我可以拯救其中一個年輕女孩 , 並且避免她們結婚並且遭受和我一樣的苦難 , 那麼這是件好事 。
this is why i'm here in front of you .	這就是為什麼我會站在你們面前 。
pr: i would like to say that i have learned so much from aicha , starting with that day we had our very first meeting with other family members which was a very private meeting with security , because it was november 2002 , and , frankly , we were afraid of the superpatriotism of that time in the country those of us family members .	帕梅拉•羅納德:我想說我在aicha身上學到很多 , 從那天我們第一次和其他家人開會 , 那是非常私密的會議 , 因為當時是2002年11月 , 而且 , 坦白說 , 我們害怕當時國家裡的超級愛國主義──我們這些家庭成員 。
but we were all so nervous .	但我們全都好緊張 。
" why does she want to meet us ? "	「 她為什麼想跟我們見面呢 ? 」
and then she was nervous .	然後她很緊張 。
" why did we want to meet her ? "	「 我們為什麼想見她呢 ? 」
what did we want from each other ?	我們互相希望得到什麼 ?
before we knew each others' names , or anything , we had embraced and wept .	在我們知道彼此的名字或其他東西之前 , 我們已經相擁而哭了 。
then we sat in a circle with support , with help , from people experienced in this kind of reconciliation .	接著 , 我們坐在一個有支援、協助的圈子裡 , 以這種和解方式經歷的人 。
and aicha started , and she said , " i don't know if my son is guilty or innocent , but i want to tell you how sorry i am for what happened to your families .	然後aicha開始著手 , 她說: 「 我不知道我的兒子是有罪還是無罪 , 但我想告訴你 , 我如何遺憾為了你家人的遭遇 。
i know what it is to suffer , and i feel that if there is a crime , a person should be tried fairly and punished . "	我知道這是怎麼一回事 , 我也覺得如果有犯罪 , 一個人應該受到公平的對待 , 並且受到懲罰 。 」
but she reached out to us in that way , and it was , i'd like to say , it was an icebreaker .	但她以那種方式接觸我們 。 我想說 , 這是個破冰的人 。
and what happened then is we all told our stories , and we all connected as human beings .	那時發生的事是 , 我們都說了自己的故事 , 我們都以人的身分來連結 。
by the end of the afternoon it was about three hours after lunch we'd felt as if we'd known each other forever .	到了午餐結束時--大概是午餐後的三小時--我們覺得好像彼此認識了一樣 。
now what i learned from her , is a woman , not only who could be so generous under these present circumstances and what it was then , and what was being done to her son , but the life she's had .	我從她身上學到的是 , 一個女人 , 不但可以在這種現況下如此慷慨 , 以及當時的感受 , 和她的兒子所做所為 , 還能過著她的生活 。
i never had met someone with such a hard life , from such a totally different culture and environment from my own .	我從來沒有遇過一個有著如此艱辛人生的人 , 來自如此全然不同的文化和環境 。
and i feel that we have a special connection , which i value very much .	我覺得我們有一種特殊的連繫這是我非常重視的 。
and i think it's all about being afraid of the other , but making that step and then realizing , " hey , this wasn't so hard .	我想這一切都是為了害怕對方 , 但就這樣一步一步地意識到: 「 嘿 , 這不難 。
who else can i meet that i don't know , or that i'm so different from ? "	我還能遇到哪些人 , 我不知道 , 還是我真的不認識 ? 」
so , aicha , do you have a couple of words for conclusion ?	那麼 , aicha , 你有幾個詞可以總結嗎 ?
because our time is up .	因為我們的時間到了 。
aw: i wanted to say that we have to try to know other people , the other .	aw:我想說 , 我們必須試著去認識其他人 , 另一個 。
you have to be generous , and your hearts must be generous , your mind must be generous .	你要寬容 , 你的心也要寬容 , 你的心念也要寬容 。
you must be tolerant .	你一定要忍受 。
you have to fight against violence .	你必須對抗暴力 。
and i hope that someday we'll all live together in peace and respecting each other .	我希望有一天 , 我們都能活在和平中 , 能互相尊重 。
this is what i wanted to say .	這是我想說的 。
too much of the world lacks access to clean drinking water . engineer michael pritchard did something about it inventing the portable lifesaver filter , which can make the most revolting water drinkable in seconds . an amazing demo from tedglobal 2009 .	太多的世界缺乏乾淨的飲用水 。 工程師麥可普立查德對此做了點什麼 , 發明了可攜式救命過濾器 , 這能在幾秒鐘內讓最難搞的水流被飲用 。 2009年tedglobal的一項了不起的展示 。

i'd like to talk about a couple of things today .	今天我想談談幾點 。
the first thing is water .	第一件事是水 。
now i see you've all been enjoying the water that's been provided for you here at the conference , over the past couple of days .	現在我看到你們都享受過研討會提供給你們的水 , 在過去的幾天中 ,
and i'm sure you'll feel that it's from a safe source .	我相信你們會覺得它是出自安全源頭 。
but what if it wasn't ?	但如果不是呢 ?
what if it was from a source like this ?	如果它是來自這樣的發源地呢 ?
then statistics would actually say that half of you would now be suffering with diarrhea .	統計數據顯示你們之中有一半的人現在患有腹瀉
i talked a lot in the past about statistics , and the provision of safe drinking water for all .	我在過去談了很多關於統計 , 以及提供所有人安全的飲用水 。
but they just don't seem to get through .	但它們似乎無法渡過 。
and i think i've worked out why .	我想我找出原因了 。
it's because , using current thinking , the scale of the problem just seems too huge to contemplate solving .	是因為 , 用當前的想法 , 問題的規模大到無法企圖解決 。
so we just switch off: us , governments and aid agencies .	所以我們就這樣關掉了:我們、政府、和援助機構 。
well , today , i'd like to show you that through thinking differently , the problem has been solved .	今天 , 我想讓大家看看透過不同的思考方式 , 問題已經被解決了 。
by the way , since i've been speaking , another 13 , 000 people around the world are suffering now with diarrhea .	順道一提 , 從我開始演講到現在 , 全球各地又有一萬三千人正在腹瀉患者
and four children have just died .	而四個孩子剛剛死去
i invented lifesaver bottle because i got angry .	我發明了lifesaver濾水瓶 , 因為我很生氣 。
i , like most of you , was sitting down , the day after christmas in 2004 , when i was watching the devastating news of the asian tsunami as it rolled in , playing out on tv .	我和你們大部分人一樣 , 是在2004年聖誕節後的隔天 , 我在看電視上推出令人沮喪的新聞 , 在電視上演出 。
the days and weeks that followed , people fleeing to the hills , being forced to drink contaminated water or face death .	接下來的日子和數週 , 人們逃到山丘上 , 被迫喝下被污染的水 , 或是面對死亡 。
that really stuck with me .	這真的讓我印象深刻 。
then , a few months later , hurricane katrina slammed into the side of america .	接著 , 幾個月後 , 卡崔娜颶風往美國衝刺 。
" okay , " i thought , " here's a first world country , let's see what they can do . "	「 好吧 」 我想: 「 這裡有第一個世界國家 , 讓我們看看他們能做什麼 。 」
do you know it took five days to get water to the superdome ?	你知道要用五天的時間把水送到超級穹頂嗎 ?
people were shooting each other on the streets for tv sets and water .	人們在街上互相開槍 , 只為了電視機和水 。
that's when i decided i had to do something .	那時我決定我得要做點什麼 。
now i spent a lot of time in my garage , over the next weeks and months , and also in my kitchen much to the dismay of my wife .	我花了很多時間在我的車庫 , 接下來的幾週、幾個月 , 也在我的廚房裡 , 讓我妻子很失望 。
however , after a few failed prototypes , i finally came up with this , the lifesaver bottle .	然而 , 經過幾次失敗的原型後 , 我終於想到這個 , 生命saver濾水瓶 。
okay , now for the science bit .	好了 , 現在來談科學 。
before lifesaver , the best hand filters were only capable of filtering down to about 200 nanometers .	在lifesaver濾水瓶之前 , 最好的手動過濾器只能過濾小至200奈米 。
the smallest bacteria is about 200 nanometers .	最小的細菌就差不多200奈米 。
so a 200nanometer bacteria is going to get through a 200nanometer hole .	所以一個200奈米的細菌將穿過一個200奈米大的洞 。
the smallest virus , on the other hand , is about 25 nanometers .	另一方面 , 最小的病毒大約是25奈米 。
so that's definitely going to get through those 200 nanometer holes .	所以這絕對會穿過那些200奈米大的洞 。
lifesaver pores are 15 nanometers .	lifsaver濾水瓶的孔隙只有15奈米大 。
so nothing is getting through .	所以沒有任何事情能夠通過 。

traditionally , in a crisis , what do we do ?	傳統上 , 在危機中 , 我們該怎麼做 ?
then , after a few weeks , we set up camps .	然後 , 幾週之後 , 我們設立了營地 。
and people are forced to come into the camps to get their safe drinking water .	人們被迫來到營地取用安全的飲用水 。

diseases spread . more resources are required .	疾病的傳播 。 需要更多的資源 。
the problem just becomes selfperpetuating .	問題只會變成自我延續 。
but by thinking differently , and shipping these , people can stay put .	但藉由不同的思考方式 , 並且運送這些技術 , 人們可以留在原地 。
they can make their own sterile drinking water , and start to get on with rebuilding their homes and their lives .	他們可以自行製造無菌飲用水 , 開始重建家園和生活 。
now , it doesn't require a natural disaster for this to work .	現在 , 這並不需要天然災害才行 。
using the old thinking , of national infrastructure and pipe work , is too expensive .	用舊思維 , 國家基礎建設和管道的工作 , 實在是太貴了 。
when you run the numbers on a calculator , you run out of noughts .	當你用計算機來計算時 , 你會耗盡無力 。

instead of shipping water , and using manmade processes to do it , let's use mother nature . she's got a fantastic system .	與其運送水和使用人造過程去做 , 不如直接使用大自然 。 她有一個很棒的系統 。
she picks the water up from there , desalinates it , for free , transports it over there , and dumps it onto the mountains , rivers , and streams .	她從那裡取水 , 免費下鹽 , 運送到那邊 , 傾倒在山區、河川 , 和溪流上 。

to put that into context , the u . k . government spends about 12 billion pounds a year on foreign aid .	以此類推 , 英國政府每年花費約120億英鎊於國際援助 。

paddy ashdown claims that we are living in a moment in history where power is changing in ways it never has before . in a spellbinding talk at tedxbrussels he outlines the three major global shifts that he sees coming .	paddyashown宣稱我們正處於一個歷史中 , 權力正在以前所未有的方式改變 。 在tedxbrussel的一個演講中他指出他所看到的三種全球轉變 。

there's a poem written by a very famous english poet at the end of the 19th century .	有一首詩這麼寫道這是一位很有名的英國詩人在十九世紀末寫的
it was said to echo in churchill's brain in the 1930s .	據說在1930年代 , 邱吉爾的大腦會迴盪 ,
and the poem goes: " on the idle hill of summer , lazy with the flow of streams , hark i hear a distant drummer , drumming like a sound in dreams , far and near and low and louder on the roads of earth go by , dear to friend and food to powder , soldiers marching , soon to die . "	這首詩是這麼寫的: " 夏日的偶像山上漫遊的溪流我聽到了遠方的鼓聲就像夢裡的一聲遠的、近的、低沉的、響亮的在路上 , 親愛的朋友和食物到粉德 , 士兵遊行 , 很快就會死 。 "
those who are interested in poetry , the poem is " a shropshire lad " written by a . e . housman .	那些對詩很感興趣的人 , 這首詩是《shropshirelad》由a.e.豪斯曼所寫 。
but what housman understood , and you hear it in the symphonies of nielsen too , was that the long , hot , silvan summers of stability of the 19th century were coming to a close , and that we were about to move into one of those terrifying periods of history when power changes .	不過 , 豪斯曼所理解的你也在尼爾森交響曲中聽過就是十九世紀那漫長 , 炎熱 , 沉浸於穩定的夏天即將到來我們即將進入那段駭人的歷史時期當權力改變時
and these are always periods , ladies and gentlemen , accompanied by turbulence , and all too often by blood .	女士們先生們 , 這些時光總是伴隨著一陣騷動 , 通常都是血 。
and my message for you is that i believe we are condemned , if you like , to live at just one of those moments in history when the gimbals upon which the established order of power is beginning to change and the new look of the world , the new powers that exist in the world , are beginning to take form .	我給你的訊息是 , 我相信我們被譴責 , 如果你願意 , 只活在歷史上的那些時刻 , 當已成形的權力正開始有了巨大的改變 , 世界的新的觀點 , 世界存在的新權力 , 開始成形 。
and these are and we see it very clearly today nearly always highly turbulent times , highly difficult times , and all too often very bloody times .	而且我們今天也清楚地看到有非常多的動盪時期 , 非常困難的時候 , 通常也非常血腥 。
by the way , it happens about once every century .	順帶一提 , 它每個世紀都會發生一次 ,
you might argue that the last time it happened and that's what housman felt coming and what churchill felt too was that when power passed from the old nations , the old powers of europe , across the atlantic to the new emerging power of the united states of america the beginning of the american century .	你可能認為 , 上次發生時 , 豪斯曼覺得這一切就要來了 , 而邱吉爾也覺得 , 當權力從舊國家流過時 , 歐洲的舊權力 , 流過大西洋 , 到美國的新興權力 , 在美國這個世紀初 。
and of course , into the vacuum where the tooold european powers used to be were played the two bloody catastrophes of the last century the one in the first part and the one in the second part: the two great world wars .	當然 , 在那個時候歐洲人過時的權力被用來扮演兩場血腥的災難就在上世紀第一部份和第二部份那是兩場大戰 。
mao zedong used to refer to them as the european civil wars , and it's probably a more accurate way of describing them .	毛澤東曾經稱它們為歐洲內戰 , 它可能是更精確的形容方式 。
well , ladies and gentlemen , we live at one of those times .	各位先生女士 , 我們住在其中一個時期 。
but for us , i want to talk about three factors today .	但對我們來說 , 我今天想談三個因素 。
and the first of these , the first two of these , is about a shift in power .	第一 , 前兩種 , 是關於權力的移轉 。
and the second is about some new dimension which i want to refer to , which has never quite happened in the way it's happening now .	第二種是關於我所提到的新的維度 , 這種事從來沒有發生過 。
but let's talk about the shifts of power that are occurring to the world .	但 , 讓我們談談現在世上的權力轉移 。
and what is happening today is , in one sense , frightening because it's never happened before .	現在的情況 , 就某種程度來說 , 很嚇人 , 因為它從來沒有發生過 。
we have seen lateral shifts of power the power of greece passed to rome and the power shifts that occurred during the european civilizations but we are seeing something slightly different .	我們已經看到橫向的權力轉移--希臘的權力移轉到羅馬 , 和歐洲文明時期發生的權力移轉--但我們看的有些不同 。
for power is not just moving laterally from nation to nation .	權力不只是國與國之間橫向移轉 ,
it's also moving vertically .	也是垂直移動的 。
what's happening today is that the power that was encased , held to accountability , held to the rule of law , within the institution of the nation state has now migrated in very large measure onto the global stage .	現在的情況是 , 權力被賦予、承擔責任的權力 , 受到法律的牽制 , 在國家的制度中 , 現在已經在非常大的尺度上遷移到全球 。
the globalization of power we talk about the globalization of markets , but actually it's the globalization of real power .	全球化的權力 , 我們談到全球化的市場 , 但實際上卻是全球化強權 。
and where , at the nation state level that power is held to accountability subject to the rule of law , on the international stage it is not .	在國家層面上 , 權力被責任歸屬在法律上 , 而不是在國際舞台上 。
the international stage and the global stage where power now resides: the power of the internet , the power of the satellite broadcasters , the power of the money changers this vast moneygoround that circulates now 32 times the amount of money necessary for the trade it's supposed to be there to finance the money changers , if you like , the financial speculators that have brought us all to our knees quite recently , the power of the multinational corporations now developing budgets often bigger than mediumsized countries .	國際舞台和全球的權力 , 現在都還存在:網路的權力 , 衛星廣播的權力 , 貨幣大筆金錢交易的權力 , 轉換成現在這筆交易所必要的金錢 , 將數量提升到32倍 , 這筆錢通常被用來資助金援的改變者 , 如果你願意的話 , 就是那些最近把我們所有人帶到我們的膝蓋的財政支票 , 轉移到多國企業的權力 , 現在總計 , 轉變為多國發展大國企業 。
these live in a global space which is largely unregulated , not subject to the rule of law , and in which people may act free of constraint .	這些住在一個全球化的空間 , 幾乎沒有受到規範 , 沒有受到法律的制度規範 , 人們也可能不受限制 。
now that suits the powerful up to a moment .	現在那符合強權到某一刻 。
it's always suitable for those who have the most power to operate in spaces without constraint , but the lesson of history is that , sooner or later , unregulated space space not subject to the rule of law becomes populated , not just by the things you wanted international trade , the internet , etc . but also by the things you don't want international criminality , international terrorism .	總是適合那些最有權力的人在沒有拘束力的空間中操作 , 但歷史的教訓是 , 遲早 , 沒有受到法律規範的空間被充當 , 不只是因為你想要國際貿易、網路等等 , 還包括你不想要的國際犯罪、國際恐怖主義 。
the revelation of 9/11 is that even if you are the most powerful nation on earth , nevertheless , those who inhabit that space can attack you even in your most iconic of cities one bright september morning .	9•11事件的啟示是:即使你是地球上最強大的國家 , 儘管如此 , 那些太空人也可能在你最具代表性的城市中攻擊你甚至在一個九月的早晨中攻擊你 。
it's said that something like 60 percent of the four million dollars that was taken to fund 9/11 actually passed through the institutions of the twin towers which 9/11 destroyed .	據說 , 四百萬美金中大約有百分之六十拿去資助911恐怖攻擊那次恐怖攻擊的機構已經通過雙子星大樓 , 而911摧毀了 。
you see , our enemies also use this space the space of mass travel , the internet , satellite broadcasters to be able to get around their poison , which is about destroying our systems and our ways .	要知道 , 我們的敵人也使用這個空間就是大眾旅行、網路、衛星廣播公司能夠繞過它們的毒氣 , 重點在於破壞我們的系統和方式 。
sooner or later , sooner or later , the rule of history is that where power goes governance must follow .	遲早有一天 , 歷史上主導權就必須遵從 。
and if it is therefore the case , as i believe it is , that one of the phenomenon of our time is the globalization of power , then it follows that one of the challenges of our time is to bring governance to the global space .	如果真是這樣 , 正如我所相信的 , 我們這個時代的一個現象就是全球化的權力 , 那麼我們這個時代面對的挑戰就是把統治者帶到全球 。
and i believe that the decades ahead of us now will be to a greater or lesser extent turbulent the more or less we are able to achieve that aim: to bring governance to the global space .	我相信在我們領先的數十年 , 或多或少會是一場騷動 , 或多或少會讓我們達成目標:把統治者帶到全球 。
now notice , i'm not talking about government .	請注意 , 我不是在說政府 。
i'm not talking about setting up some global democratic institution .	我不是在說設立一些全球民主制度 ,
my own view , by the way , ladies and gentlemen , is that this is unlikely to be done by spawning more u . n . institutions .	順道一提 , 我自己的看法是 , 各位先生女士 , 由於產卵更多的聯合國大機構是不可能完成的 。
if we didn't have the u . n . , we'd have to invent it .	如果我們沒有聯合國 , 我們就得發明出
the world needs an international forum .	這個世界需要一個國際論壇
it needs a means by which you can legitimize international action .	它需要一種方法來合法化國際行動 。
but when it comes to governance of the global space , my guess is this won't happen through the creation of more u . n . institutions .	但當談到全球空間的統治時 , 我的猜想是 , 不是透過再創造出更多的聯合國的機構來達成 。
it will actually happen by the powerful coming together and making treatybased systems , treatybased agreements , to govern that global space .	實際上 , 強大的力量團結在一起 , 建立合約的系統、協定的協議 , 來管理那個全球空間 。
and if you look , you can see them happening , already beginning to emerge .	如果你去看 , 你可以看到它們發生 , 已經開始出現了 。
the world trade organization: treatybased organization , entirely treatybased , and yet , powerful enough to hold even the most powerful , the united states , to account if necessary .	世界貿易組織:條約為基礎的組織 , 完全以條約為基礎 , 然而 , 強大到連最強大的力量 , 美國也能在必要時考量 。
kyoto: the beginnings of struggling to create a treatybased organization .	京都:努力打造一個合約為底的組織 。
the g20: we know now that we have to put together an institution which is capable of bringing governance to that financial space for financial speculation .	二十國集團:現在我們知道 , 我們必須組建一個能夠將統治權帶到金融空間的機構 , 以做財務猜測 。
and that's what the g20 is , a treatybased institution .	這就是二十國集團因而建立的基礎制度
now there's a problem there , and we'll come back to it in a minute , which is that if you bring the most powerful together to make the rules in treatybased institutions , to fill that governance space , then what happens to the weak who are left out ?	現在有個問題了 , 我們等一下就會回到問題上 , 就是 , 如果你把最強大的人集合起來 , 讓規則以條約為基礎的機構 , 去填充統治空間 , 那還剩下的那些人 , 會怎麼樣 ?
and that's a big problem , and we'll return to it in just a second .	這是個大問題 , 我們等一下會回到這問題上 。
so there's my first message , that if you are to pass through these turbulent times more or less turbulently , then our success in doing that will in large measure depend on our capacity to bring sensible governance to the global space .	所以 , 我的第一個信息是 , 如果你多多少少經歷這些騷動 , 或多或少不安 , 那麼 , 我們的成功將取決於我們把合理的管理帶上國際舞台的能力 。
and watch that beginning to happen .	看著這些開始發生 。
my second point is , and i know i don't have to talk to an audience like this about such a thing , but power is not just shifting vertically , it's also shifting horizontally .	我的第二點是 , 我知道我不需要這樣跟觀眾談這件事 , 關於這點 , 但權力不只是直向移轉 , 權力也會橫向移轉 。
you might argue that the story , the history of civilizations , has been civilizations gathered around seas with the first ones around the mediterranean , the more recent ones in the ascendents of western power around the atlantic .	你可能會爭辯說 , 人類文明的歷史已經聚集在海洋四周最先圍繞地中海的文明群體中 , 在大西洋上 , 西方近期才出現 。
well it seems to me that we're now seeing a fundamental shift of power , broadly speaking , away from nations gathered around the atlantic [seaboard] to the nations gathered around the pacific rim .	在我看來 , 現在我們看到的 , 是權力移轉的基本面 , 廣義來說 , 遠離大西洋 , 聚集到太平洋岸邊的國家 。
now that begins with economic power , but that's the way it always begins .	現在開始從經濟開始 , 但一切都是這樣開始的
you already begin to see the development of foreign policies , the augmentation of military budgets occurring in the other growing powers in the world .	你已經開始看到世界上漸漸形成的外交政策的發展 , 軍事預算也增加 ,
i think actually this is not so much a shift from the west to the east ; something different is happening .	事實上 , 這從西方移轉到東方並沒有什麼不同 , 正在發生 。
my guess is , for what it's worth , is that the united states will remain the most powerful nation on earth for the next 10 years , 15 , but the context in which she holds her power has now radically altered ; it has radically changed .	我個人的猜測是 , 美國在未來十年、十五年保持在地球上最強大的國家 , 但她握有的權力背景現在已徹底地被改變 ; 徹底地改變了 。
we are coming out of 50 years , most unusual years , of history in which we have had a totally monopolar world , in which every compass needle for or against has to be referenced by its position to washington a world bestrode by a single colossus .	我們正走出歷史的五十年 , 最不尋常的五十年 , 在這世界中 , 我們已經擁有一個完全獨立的世界 , 每一個指南針都需要這些指南針 , 必須被指引到華盛頓--一個只有一個大腸桿弟的世界 。
but that's not a usual case in history .	但在歷史上這並非常見的情況 。
in fact , what's now emerging is the much more normal case of history .	事實上 , 現在正在漸漸浮現的是歷史上較常見的例子 。
you're beginning to see the emergence of a multipolar world .	你開始會看到多極化世界的出現 。
up until now , the united states has been the dominant feature of our world .	到目前為止 , 美國一直是我們世界的主導特色 。
they will remain the most powerful nation , but they will be the most powerful nation in an increasingly multipolar world .	他們會保持最強大的國家 , 但他們在越來越多的世界中 , 會是最強大的國家 。
and you begin to see the alternative centers of power building up in china , of course , though my own guess is that china's ascent to greatness is not smooth .	你就會開始看到其他在中國建立的權力中心 , 當然 , 雖然我自己猜想的是 , 中國的偉大中心並不光滑 。
it's going to be quite grumpy as china begins to democratize her society after liberalizing her economy .	當中國在自由經濟後將處於民主化她的社會也變得相當棘手
but that's a subject of a different discussion .	但那是另一個主題 。
you see india , you see brazil .	看到印度 , 巴西
you see increasingly that the world now looks actually , for us europeans , much more like europe in the 19th century .	你可以看到這個世界現在看起來 , 對於我們歐洲人來說 , 看起來更像是十九世紀的歐洲 。
europe in the 19th century: a great british foreign secretary , lord canning , used to describe it as the " european concert of powers . "	十九世紀的歐洲 , 一位偉大的英國外交大臣坎寧曾形容它是 「 歐洲人的權力音樂會 」
there was a balance , a fivesided balance .	有一個平衡 , 一個五面體的平衡 。
britain always played to the balance .	英國向來是平衡的 。
if paris got together with berlin , britain got together with vienna and rome to provide a counterbalance .	如果巴黎和柏林一起來 , 英國和維也納和羅馬結合 , 來對抗羅馬 。
now notice , in a period which is dominated by a monopolar world , you have fixed alliances nato , the warsaw pact .	現在請注意 , 在這段期間 , 由單一強國統治的時期 , 你有固定的同盟國北約組織 , 華沙修女 。
a fixed polarity of power means fixed alliances .	固定權力的對立 , 就表示是固定結盟 。
but a multiple polarity of power means shifting and changing alliances .	但有多個對立的權力 , 就意味著要轉換和改變結盟 。
and that's the world we're coming into , in which we will increasingly see that our alliances are not fixed .	這就是我們即將進入的世界我們會逐漸發現我們的同盟國並非固定不變
canning , the great british foreign secretary once said , " britain has a common interest , but no common allies . "	傑出的英國外交大臣坎寧曾說過: 「 英國有共同的利益 , 但沒有共同的盟友 。 」
and we will see increasingly that even we in the west will reach out , have to reach out , beyond the cozy circle of the atlantic powers to make alliances with others if we want to get things done in the world .	我們會發現 , 即使我們身處西方 , 也要能伸出援手 , 跨出大西洋的舒適圈 , 能和他人結盟 , 只要我們能把事情做好 。
note , that when we went into libya , it was not good enough for the west to do it alone ; we had to bring others in .	要注意 , 當我們進入利比亞時 , 僅靠西方國家獨處是不夠的 , 我們得要把他人帶進來 。
we had to bring , in this case , the arab league in .	在這個案例中 , 我們必須引進阿拉伯聯盟 。
my guess is iraq and afghanistan are the last times when the west has tried to do it themselves , and we haven't succeeded .	我的猜測是伊拉克和阿富汗最後幾次 , 西方國家試圖靠它們自己 , 我們還沒有成功 。
my guess is that we're reaching the beginning of the end of 400 years i say 400 years because it's the end of the ottoman empire of the hegemony of western power , western institutions and western values .	我的猜測是 , 我們已經到達400年底了 , 我說400年了 , 因為那是鄂圖曼帝國位於西方權力的象徵 , 西方的機構和西方的價值 。
you know , up until now , if the west got its act together , it could propose and dispose in every corner of the world .	你知道嗎 , 直到現在 , 如果西方國家共同採取行動 , 就可以在世界每個角落提出和反駁 。
but that's no longer true .	但已經不再是如此了 。
take the last financial crisis after the second world war .	把第二次世界大戰後最後一次金融危機
the west got together the bretton woods institution , world bank , international monetary fund the problem solved .	西方國家集合了布雷頓森林機構、世界銀行、國際貨幣基金--問題解決了 。
now we have to call in others .	現在我們必須號召其他人
now we have to create the g20 .	現在我們得要創造二十國集團 。
now we have to reach beyond the cozy circle of our western friends .	現在我們必須超越西方的舒適圈 。
let me make a prediction for you , which is probably even more startling .	讓我為各位做個預測 , 這可能還更令人吃驚 。
i suspect we are now reaching the end of 400 years when western power was enough .	我懷疑我們已經到了400年後 , 當時西方的權力已經足夠了 。
people say to me , " the chinese , of course , they'll never get themselves involved in peacemaking , multilateral peacemaking around the world . "	有人對我說: 「 中國 , 當然 , 他們永遠不會讓自己參與調停 , 世界各地的多邊和平調停 。 」
oh yes ? why not ?	噢 , 是嗎 ? 為什麼不呢 ?
how many chinese troops are serving under the blue beret , serving under the blue flag , serving under the u . n . command in the world today ?	有多少中國軍隊在藍色貝雷特下 , 在藍色的旗子下 , 在聯合國的指令下服務 ?
how many americans ? 11 .	有多少美國人 ? 十一份 。
what is the largest naval contingent tackling the issue of somali pirates ?	到底什麼是最大規模的海軍陸戰隊在處理索馬利亞海盜的議題 ?
the chinese naval contingent .	中國的海軍大會
of course they are , they are a mercantilist nation .	他們當然是 , 他們是位商人主義國家 。
they want to keep the sea lanes open .	他們想要保持航道的暢通
increasingly , we are going to have to do business with people with whom we do not share values , but with whom , for the moment , we share common interests .	漸漸地 , 我們得要和和我們沒有共享價值的人做生意 , 但對於誰 , 目前 , 我們共同分享共同的利益 。
it's a whole new different way of looking at the world that is now emerging .	這是個全新的角度來看這個正在興起的世界 。
and here's the third factor , which is totally different .	第三個因素 , 它是完全不同的 。
today in our modern world , because of the internet , because of the kinds of things people have been talking about here , everything is connected to everything .	今天 , 在我們的現代世界 , 因為網路 , 因為人們一直在談論的各種事物 , 所有的事物都會連結到一切 。
we are now interdependent .	我們現在相互依賴 。
we are now interlocked , as nations , as individuals , in a way which has never been the case before , never been the case before .	我們現在被封鎖 , 作為國家 , 作為個體 , 以前從來沒有這樣做過 。
the interrelationship of nations , well it's always existed .	國與國之間的關係 , 嗯 , 它一直都存在 。
diplomacy is about managing the interrelationship of nations .	外交就是管理國家之間的相互關係 。
but now we are intimately locked together .	但現在我們密不可分地被關在一起 。
you get swine flu in mexico , it's a problem for charles de gaulle airport 24 hours later .	墨西哥的豬流感 , 24小時後 , 查爾斯戴•高爾機場的問題出現了 。
lehman brothers goes down , the whole lot collapses .	雷曼兄弟倒閉了 , 全部都倒下了 。
there are fires in the steppes of russia , food riots in africa .	俄羅斯的大草原發生火災非洲的糧食暴動
we are all now deeply , deeply , deeply interconnected .	我們彼此之間有很深、很深的連結 。
and what that means is the idea of a nation state acting alone , not connected with others , not working with others , is no longer a viable proposition .	意思就是 , 一個國家單獨行動 , 不再與他人建立聯繫 , 不再與他人合作 , 不再是一項可行的提案 。
because the actions of a nation state are neither confined to itself , nor is it sufficient for the nation state itself to control its own territory , because the effects outside the nation state are now beginning to affect what happens inside them .	因為一個國家的行動也不受制於自己 , 也不受制於國家本身來控制自己的國土 。 因為國家之外的影響如今已開始影響國內發生的事 。
i was a young soldier in the last of the small empire wars of britain .	當時我還是個年輕的士兵 , 在英國最後一場小型帝國戰爭中 ,
at that time , the defense of my country was about one thing and one thing only: how strong was our army , how strong was our air force , how strong was our navy and how strong were our allies .	那時 , 我的國家要保護的是一件事 , 只有一件事:我們的軍隊多強 , 我們的空軍多強 , 我們的海軍多強 , 我們同盟國多厲害 。
that was when the enemy was outside the walls .	當時敵人就在城牆外
now the enemy is inside the walls .	現在敵人在城牆內
now if i want to talk about the defense of my country , i have to speak to the minister of health because pandemic disease is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of agriculture because food security is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of industry because the fragility of our hitech infrastructure is now a point of attack for our enemies as we see from cyber warfare i have to speak to the minister of home affairs because who has entered my country , who lives in that terraced house in that inner city has a direct effect on what happens in my country as we in london saw in the 7/7 bombings .	現在 , 如果我想談談我國家的國防 , 我必須和衛生署談 , 因為大流行病對我的安全造成威脅 , 我必須和農業部談 , 因為糧食安全對我的安全造成威脅 , 我必須和工業部談談 , 因為我們的高科技設施很脆弱 , 對於我們的敵人的攻擊 , 如同我們從網路戰爭上看到的攻擊 , 我得和國內外的人談 , 因為我們已經進入了西伯利亞的家鄉 , 我們的房子 。
it's no longer the case that the security of a country is simply a matter for its soldiers and its ministry of defense .	一個國家的安全不再只是軍人和國防部的問題 。
it's its capacity to lock together its institutions .	鎖定制度的能力
and this tells you something very important .	而這告訴你非常重要的一點 。
it tells you that , in fact , our governments , vertically constructed , constructed on the economic model of the industrial revolution vertical hierarchy , specialization of tasks , command structures have got the wrong structures completely .	它告訴你 , 事實上 , 我們的政府 , 垂直建構 , 建構在工業革命的經濟模型--縱向層級結構 , 分工任務的專長化--已經完全搞錯了結構 。
you in business know that the paradigm structure of our time , ladies and gentlemen , is the network .	在企業你們知道我們時代的典範結構女士們 , 就是網絡
it's your capacity to network that matters , both within your governments and externally .	網絡的能力很重要 , 無論在你的政府內部還是在外部 。
so here is ashdown's third law .	這是ashown的第三定律 。
by the way , don't ask me about ashdown's first law and second law because i haven't invented those yet ; it always sounds better if there's a third law , doesn't it ?	對了 , 別問我第一條法則和第二條法則因為我還沒發明出來那總是比較好聽 , 如果有第三條法則 , 不是嗎 ?
ashdown's third law is that in the modern age , where everything is connected to everything , the most important thing about what you can do is what you can do with others .	shown的第三定律是在現代 , 每件事都有關連 , 最重要的是 , 你能做的事是你和他人能夠做的事 。
the most important bit about your structure whether you're a government , whether you're an army regiment , whether you're a business is your docking points , your interconnectors , your capacity to network with others .	關於你的結構 , 最重要的一點是 , 不論你是政府 , 不論你是軍事部隊 , 不論你是企業 , 是你要的圓點 , 你的互聯社 , 你和其他人聯絡的能力 。
you understand that in industry ; governments don't .	你了解在工業中 , 政府不會
but now one final thing .	但現在 , 最後一件事
if it is the case , ladies and gentlemen and it is that we are now locked together in a way that has never been quite the same before , then it's also the case that we share a destiny with each other .	如果是這樣 , 各位先生女士 , 我們現在被鎖在一起 , 以一種前所未有的方式鎖在一起 , 那也是我們和彼此有著相同的命運 。
suddenly and for the very first time , collective defense , the thing that has dominated us as the concept of securing our nations , is no longer enough .	突然間 , 這是第一次 , 集體防護 , 支配我們國家安全的概念已經不夠了 。
it used to be the case that if my tribe was more powerful than their tribe , i was safe ; if my country was more powerful than their country , i was safe ; my alliance , like nato , was more powerful than their alliance , i was safe .	過去是這樣如果我的部落比他們的部落更強大 , 我就安全了 ; 如果我的國家比他們的國家強 , 我就安全了 ; 我的結盟 , 就像北約組織 , 比起他們結盟一樣強大 , 我就安全了 。
it is no longer the case .	不再是如此了 。
the advent of the interconnectedness and of the weapons of mass destruction means that , increasingly , i share a destiny with my enemy .	大規模毀滅性武器的相互連結以及大規模毀滅性武器的出現 , 意味著我與敵人分享我的命運 。
when i was a diplomat negotiating the disarmament treaties with the soviet union in geneva in the 1970s , we succeeded because we understood we shared a destiny with them .	當我還是外交官的時候 , 在1970年代與日內瓦的蘇聯在日內瓦談判協定時 , 我們成功是因為我們了解我們和他們有著共同的命運 。
collective security is not enough .	集體安全是不夠的 。
peace has come to northern ireland because both sides realized that the zerosum game couldn't work .	和平也來到北愛爾蘭因為雙方了解 , 零和遊戲是行不通的
they shared a destiny with their enemies .	他們和敵人有著共同的命運
one of the great barriers to peace in the middle east is that both sides , both israel and , i think , the palestinians , do not understand that they share a collective destiny .	阻礙著中東和平的其中一個強大的障礙是以色列與巴勒斯坦人都不明白他們共同的命運
and so suddenly , ladies and gentlemen , what has been the proposition of visionaries and poets down the ages becomes something we have to take seriously as a matter of public policy .	所以 , 各位 , 突然間 , 提議有遠見的人和詩人 , 都變成了我們必須要認真看待的公共政策 。
i started with a poem , i'll end with one .	我從一首詩開始 , 以一首
the great poem of john donne's .	約翰•多恩的偉大詩作
" send not for whom the bell tolls . "	「 不要為誰把鈴聲送給誰 」
the poem is called " no man is an island . "	這首詩叫做 " 沒有人是孤島 " 。
and it goes: " every man's death affected me , for i am involved in mankind , send not to ask for whom the bell tolls , it tolls for thee . "	內容是: 「 每一個人的死亡都影響了我 , 為了我也參與人類 , 請不要問鐘聲為誰響 , 反而給了我讚 。 」
for john donne , a recommendation of morality .	對johndonne來說 , 推薦道德
for us , i think , part of the equation for our survival .	對我們來說 , 我認為 , 方程式的一部分是為了我們的生存 。
to find the path to long life and health , dan buettner and team study the world's " blue zones , " communities whose elders live with vim and vigor to recordsetting age . at tedxtc , he shares the 9 common diet and lifestyle habits that keep them spry past age 100 .	為了找到延長生命和健康的道路 , 丹•布埃納和世界團隊研究 「 藍色地帶 」 , 他們的長者與病毒共處 , 記錄著年齡 。 在tedxtc , 他共有9個共同飲食和生活方式的習慣 , 使他們能活到100歲以上 。
biology , culture , exploration , food , health , life , science	生物、文化、探索、食物、健康、生命、科學 。
dan buettner: how to live to be 100+	danbuetner:如何活到100+10 。
something called the danish twin study established that only about 10 percent of how long the average person lives , within certain biological limits , is dictated by our genes .	有個丹麥雙胞胎的研究證實在某種生物限制下 , 人平均壽命只有百分之十
the other 90 percent is dictated by our lifestyle .	其他百分之九十是由我們的生活方式主宰
so the premise of blue zones: if we can find the optimal lifestyle of longevity we can come up with a de facto formula for longevity .	所以藍寶地的前提是:如果我們能找到長壽的最佳生活方式 , 我們就能得出一個實際的壽命公式 。
but if you ask the average american what the optimal formula of longevity is , they probably couldn't tell you .	但如果你問一般美國人長壽的最佳公式是什麼 , 他們大概都說不出來 。
they've probably heard of the south beach diet , or the atkins diet .	他們可能聽說過南海灘飲食或是阿提金斯飲食
you have the usda food pyramid .	有美國農業部的食物金字塔 ,
there is what oprah tells us .	歐普拉告訴我們
there is what doctor oz tells us .	歐茲博士告訴我們
the fact of the matter is there is a lot of confusion around what really helps us live longer better .	事實是 , 對於真正幫助我們活得更好的事 , 總是有很多困惑 。
should you be running marathons or doing yoga ?	你應該跑馬拉松還是做瑜珈 ?
should you eat organic meats or should you be eating tofu ?	應該吃有機肉嗎 ? 還是豆腐 ?
when it comes to supplements , should you be taking them ?	當談及補充物時 , 你是不是該把它們
how about these hormones or resveratrol ?	那麼這些荷爾蒙或白藜蘆醇呢 ?
and does purpose play into it ?	而且目的性會影響到它嗎 ?
spirituality ? and how about how we socialize ?	靈性 ? 那我們如何社交呢 ?
well , our approach to finding longevity was to team up with national geographic , and the national institute on aging , to find the four demographically confirmed areas that are geographically defined .	我們尋找長壽的方法是與國家地理還有國家老化研究院合作找到四個人口確定地理界線分明的區塊
and then bring a team of experts in there to methodically go through exactly what these people do , to distill down the crosscultural distillation .	然後請一個專家團隊去有方法的體驗一下這些人的動作 , 提高了跨文化的精華 。
and at the end of this i'm going to tell you what that distillation is .	最後我會告訴你們精華是什麼
but first i'd like to debunk some common myths when it comes to longevity .	但首先我想破除一些常見的迷思長壽的迷思
and the first myth is if you try really hard you can live to be 100 .	第一個迷思是 , 如果你很努力就能活到一百歲 。
the problem is , only about one out of 5 , 000 people in america live to be 100 .	問題是 , 美國只有五千分之一的人能活到一百歲 。
your chances are very low .	你的機會非常低 。
even though it's the fastest growing demographic in america , it's hard to reach 100 .	即使它是美國成長最快的人口 , 但很難達到一百歲 。
the problem is that we're not programmed for longevity .	問題是我們並非長壽的程式 。
we are programmed for something called procreative success .	我們是為了所謂的繁衍成功而設計的 。
i love that word .	我很喜歡這個詞 。
it reminds me of my college days .	這讓我想起大學時
biologists term procreative success to mean the age where you have children and then another generation , the age when your children have children .	生物學家把成功的定義為 , 即你有孩子的年齡 , 接著再下一代 , 當你的孩子有孩子時的年齡 。
after that the effect of evolution completely dissipates .	在那演化的影響完全消失了之後
if you're a mammal , if you're a rat or an elephant , or a human , in between , it's the same story .	如果你是哺乳類 , 如果你是隻老鼠或大象 , 或人或之間 , 都是一樣的故事 。
so to make it to age 100 , you not only have to have had a very good lifestyle , you also have to have won the genetic lottery .	要讓它活到一百歲 , 你不僅需要擁有非常好的生活方式 , 你還得中了基因樂透 。
the second myth is , there are treatments that can help slow , reverse , or even stop aging .	第二個迷思是 , 有治療方法可以幫助緩慢、逆轉、甚至停止老化 。
when you think of it , there is 99 things that can age us .	仔細想想 , 總共有99件事可以讓我們老化 。
deprive your brain of oxygen for just a few minutes , those brain cells die , they never come back .	只要你的腦袋缺氧幾分鐘腦細胞就會死 , 從不復返
play tennis too hard , on your knees , ruin your cartilage , the cartilage never comes back .	玩網球太辛苦了 , 膝蓋破了你的軟骨 , 軟骨永遠不會回來了 。
our arteries can clog . our brains can gunk up with plaque , and we can get alzheimer's .	我們的動脈會堵塞 。 我們的大腦會用斑塊黏住 , 我們就能得老年癡呆症 。
there is just too many things to go wrong .	有太多事會出錯了 。
our bodies have 35 trillion cells , trillion with a " t . " we're talking national debt numbers here .	我們的身體有三十五兆個細胞 , 用 " t " 的兆頭 , 我們在這裡說的是國債 。
those cells turn themselves over once every eight years .	那些細胞每八年轉動一次 。
and every time they turn themselves over there is some damage . and that damage builds up .	每當它們自身 , 就會造成一些傷害 , 而傷害會不斷增加 。
and it builds up exponentially .	並且以指數方式建立起來 。
it's a little bit like the days when we all had beatles albums or eagles albums and we'd make a copy of that on a cassette tape , and let our friends copy that cassette tape , and pretty soon , with successive generations that tape sounds like garbage .	這有點像我們都擁有披頭四或老鷹合唱團的唱片專輯而我們則在錄音帶上複製這首我們讓朋友複製這些錄音帶很快的 , 後續的代相傳錄音帶聽起來像垃圾
well , the same things happen to our cells .	同樣的事情也發生在我們的細胞上
that's why a 65yearold person is aging at a rate of about 125 times faster than a 12yearold person .	這就是為什麼一個65歲的人老化的速率比一個125歲的人快125倍
so , if there is nothing you can do to slow your aging or stop your aging , what am i doing here ?	所以 , 如果沒辦法減緩老化或停止老化我在這裡幹什麼 ?
well , the fact of the matter is the best science tells us that the capacity of the human body , my body , your body , is about 90 years , a little bit more for women .	嗯 , 事實上最好的科學告訴我們 , 人體、我的身體、你的身體的容量 , 大約是90年 , 還多一點女人 。
but life expectancy in this country is only 78 .	但這個國家的預期壽命只有78歲
so somewhere along the line , we're leaving about 12 good years on the table .	所以在生命的某個階段 , 我們在桌子上留下約12年的美好 。
these are years that we could get .	這些年來我們能夠
and research shows that they would be years largely free of chronic disease , heart disease , cancer and diabetes .	研究顯示 , 他們大部份不會罹患慢性病、心臟病、癌症 , 及糖尿病 。
we think the best way to get these missing years is to look at the cultures around the world that are actually experiencing them , areas where people are living to age 100 at rates up to 10 times greater than we are , areas where the life expectancy is an extra dozen years , the rate of middle age mortality is a fraction of what it is in this country .	我們認為 , 要讓這些消失的歲月 , 最好的方式是去看看世界各地的文化 , 那些人的壽命高達100歲的地區 , 比我們多出了10倍 , 那些預期壽命多出十倍的地方 , 中年死亡率是這個國家的一小部分 。
we found our first blue zone about 125 miles off the coast of italy , on the island of sardinia .	我們發現的第一個藍寶地是在義大利海岸外約一百二十五英里處 , 薩丁尼亞島上 。
and not the entire island , the island is about 1 . 4 million people , but only up in the highlands , an area called the nuoro province .	不是整座島 , 整座島約有一百四十萬人 , 只是高地上 , 一個叫努奧羅省的地方 。
and here we have this area where men live the longest , about 10 times more centenarians than we have here in america .	這裡我們有一區男性最長壽百歲人瑞的年齡比美國還長十倍
and this is a place where people not only reach age 100 , they do so with extraordinary vigor .	這裡的人不僅活到一百歲而已他們還發動了非凡的動力
places where 102 year olds still ride their bike to work , chop wood , and can beat a guy 60 years younger than them .	一百零二歲的老人仍舊騎腳踏車去工作 , 砍柴 , 還能打敗比他們年輕六十歲的人 。
their history actually goes back to about the time of christ .	他們的歷史實際上可追溯到大約基督的時代 。
it's actually a bronze age culture that's been isolated .	這其實是種孤立的青銅器文化 。
because the land is so infertile , they largely are shepherds , which occasions regular , lowintensity physical activity .	因為這片土地是如此地不孕 , 它們大多是牧羊人 , 經常是低強度的身體活動 。
their diet is mostly plantbased , accentuated with foods that they can carry into the fields .	他們的飲食多以植物為主 , 多半以食物為基礎 , 送到田地 。
they came up with an unleavened whole wheat bread called carta musica made out of durum wheat , a type of cheese made from grassfed animals so the cheese is high in omega3 fatty acids instead of omega6 fatty acids from cornfed animals , and a type of wine that has three times the level of polyphenols than any known wine in the world .	他們想出一種未發酵的全麥麵包 , 叫做木頭麥子麵包 , 一種乳酪 , 由草餵養的動物製成 , 所以這種乳酪含在omega-3脂肪酸而不是omega-6脂肪酸 , 來自玉米餵養的動物 , 還有一種葡萄酒 , 比任何已知的葡萄酒都多了三倍 。
but the real secret i think lies more in the way that they organize their society .	但我認為真正的秘密是他們組織社會的方式 。
and one of the most salient elements of the sardinian society is how they treat older people .	而薩丁尼亞社會最突出的元素之一 , 就是他們對待老年人的方式 。
you ever notice here in america , social equity seems to peak at about age 24 ?	你有沒有注意到在美國 , 社會平等在24歲左右達到高峰 ?
just look at the advertisements .	只要看看那些廣告
here in sardinia , the older you get the more equity you have , the more wisdom you're celebrated for .	在薩丁尼亞這裡 , 你越長越平等 , 就有越多的智慧被讚頌 。
you go into the bars in sardinia , instead of seeing the sports illustrated swimsuit calendar , you see the centenarian of the month calendar .	你走進薩丁尼亞的酒吧你看到的不是運動畫刊的泳裝日曆而是看到百歲人瑞的月曆
this , as it turns out , is not only good for your aging parents to keep them close to the family it imparts about four to six years of extra life expectancy research shows it's also good for the children of those families , who have lower rates of mortality and lower rates of disease .	結果發現 , 這不只讓老邁的父母和家人更親近還增加預期壽命四到六年的研究顯示這對那些家庭的孩子也是有益的他們有較低的死亡率和較低的疾病發生率
that's called the grandmother effect .	這就是所謂的祖母效應 。
we found our second blue zone on the other side of the planet , about 800 miles south of tokyo , on the archipelago of okinawa .	我們在地球的另一端發現了第二個藍色地帶 , 在東京的南端 , 大約有800英里 , 在琉球的群島上 。
okinawa is actually 161 small islands .	琉球實際上是161個小島
and in the northern part of the main island , this is ground zero for world longevity .	而主島的北端是世界長壽的原點
this is a place where the oldest living female population is found .	這個地方是最老的女性人口中找到的 。
it's a place where people have the longest disabilityfree life expectancy in the world .	這裡的人有著世界上最長、最沒有殘疾的預期壽命 。
they have what we want .	他們有我們想要的
they live a long time , and tend to die in their sleep , very quickly , and often , i can tell you , after sex .	牠們壽命很長 , 通常在睡眠時很快就會死去 , 通常我還可以告訴你 , 在做愛後 。
they live about seven good years longer than the average american .	他們比一般美國人多活七年
five times as many centenarians as we have in america .	五倍於美國的百歲人瑞
one fifth the rate of colon and breast cancer , big killers here in america .	得結腸癌和乳癌的比率有五分之一 , 在美國這裡是大殺手 。
and one sixth the rate of cardiovascular disease .	心血管疾病率的六分之一
and the fact that this culture has yielded these numbers suggests strongly they have something to teach us .	而這個文化所產生的事實 , 強烈地表明了這些數字 , 他們有能力教導我們 。
what do they do ?	他們會怎麼做 ?
once again , a plantbased diet , full of vegetables with lots of color in them .	再一次 , 植物為主的飲食 , 含有大量顏色的蔬菜 。
and they eat about eight times as much tofu as americans do .	而且他們吃大約八倍多的豆腐跟美國人一樣
more significant than what they eat is how they eat it .	比他們吃的食物更為重要 。
they have all kinds of little strategies to keep from overeating , which , as you know , is a big problem here in america .	他們有各種小戰略 , 可以避免過食 , 如你所知 , 這在美國是大問題 。
a few of the strategies we observed: they eat off of smaller plates , so they tend to eat fewer calories at every sitting .	我們觀察到的少數幾種策略:他們吃較小的盤子 , 所以每次坐著都會少吃一點卡路里 。
instead of serving family style , where you can sort of mindlessly eat as you're talking , they serve at the counter , put the food away , and then bring it to the table .	與其像家人那樣 , 不如你說話時那樣專心地吃 , 他們在櫃檯上安裝食物 , 再把食物帶走 , 再把食物送上桌 。
they also have a 3 , 000yearold adage , which i think is the greatest sort of diet suggestion ever invented .	他們還有一句三千年的格言 , 我覺得這是有史以來最棒的飲食建議 。
it was invented by confucius .	是孔子想出來的 。
and that diet is known as the hara , hatchi , bu diet .	而那飲食就是大家所知的哈拉、哈茨、布丁飲食 。
it's simply a little saying these people say before their meal to remind them to stop eating when their stomach is [80] percent full .	簡單地說 , 這些人在餐前說 , 提醒他們吃到八成後就不吃了 。
it takes about a half hour for that full feeling to travel from your belly to your brain .	全身從肚子到腦袋大概只需要一個半小時
and by remembering to stop at 80 percent it helps keep you from doing that very thing .	藉由記住要停80% , 就能協助你做到這件事 。
but , like sardinia , okinawa has a few social constructs that we can associate with longevity .	但是 , 像薩丁尼亞 , 琉球有些社會結構讓我們可以把長壽聯繫起來
we know that isolation kills .	我們知道孤立無援 。
fifteen years ago , the average american had three good friends .	十五年前美國人平均有三個好朋友
we're down to one and half right now .	目前我們只剩下一半 。
if you were lucky enough to be born in okinawa , you were born into a system where you automatically have a half a dozen friends with whom you travel through life .	如果你夠幸運生在琉球 , 你生在一個系統裡 , 你會自動擁有半打的朋友 , 和他們一生之旅 。
they call it a moai . and if you're in a moai you're expected to share the bounty if you encounter luck , and if things go bad , child gets sick , parent dies , you always have somebody who has your back .	他們稱之為 " moai " 。 如果你坐上一台moai你會期待看到運氣好 , 如果事情不順 , 孩子會生病、父母去世 , 你總是有人背著你的背 。
this particular moai , these five ladies have been together for 97 years .	這位moai , 這五位女士已經聚在一起九十七年了
their average age is 102 .	他們的平均年齡是一百零二歲
typically in america we've divided our adult life up into two sections .	通常在美國我們已經把成人生活分成兩段
there is our work life , where we're productive .	有我們的工作 , 我們有生產力 。
and then one day , boom , we retire .	然後有一天 , 碰 , 我們退休
and typically that has meant retiring to the easy chair , or going down to arizona to play golf .	通常那就表示要退休給容易玩的椅子 , 或是下到亞利桑那州去打高爾夫 。
in the okinawan language there is not even a word for retirement .	在琉球語裡甚至沒有退休這個詞
instead there is one word that imbues your entire life , and that word is " ikigai . "	取而代之的是 , 那個詞是 「 生存 」 。
and , roughly translated , it means " the reason for which you wake up in the morning . "	大致翻譯是: " 早上起床的理由 "
for this 102yearold karate master , his ikigai was carrying forth this martial art .	對這位一百零二歲的空手道大師來說他的生存價值就是推進這項武術
for this hundredyearold fisherman it was continuing to catch fish for his family three times a week .	對這位一百歲的漁夫來說 , 漁夫每週要漁獲三次 。
and this is a question . the national institute on aging actually gave us a questionnaire to give these centenarians .	這是一個問題 。 國家老化研究院確實給了我們一個問卷 , 給了這些百歲人瑞 。
and one of the questions , they were very culturally astute , the people who put the questionnaire .	其中一個問題 , 他們非常文化化地洞察那些問卷的人 。
one of the questions was , " what is your ikigai ? "	其中一個問題是: 「 你的生存價值是什麼 ? 」
they instantly knew why they woke up in the morning .	他們馬上就知道為什麼要在早上起床
for this 102 year old woman , her ikigai was simply her greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	對這位一百零二歲的老太太來說 , 她的生存環境只是她的曾曾曾孫女 。
two girls separated in age by 101 and a half years .	兩個女孩在101歲半的時間裡分開 ,
and i asked her what it felt like to hold a greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	我問她感覺如何抱著一個曾曾曾孫女
and she put her head back and she said , " it feels like leaping into heaven . "	她回過頭 , 說: 「 感覺就像飛躍上天堂 。 」
i thought that was a wonderful thought .	我覺得這想法很棒 。
my editor at geographic wanted me to find america's blue zone .	我在地理的編輯要我去找美國的藍寶地 。
and for a while we looked on the prairies of minnesota , where actually there is a very high proportion of centenarians .	有一陣子我們去看明尼蘇達州的草原那裡百歲人瑞的比例非常高
but that's because all the young people left .	但那是因為所有年輕人都離開了
so , we turned to the data again .	所以 , 我們再次轉向資料 。
and we found america's longestlived population among the seventhday adventists concentrated in and around loma linda , california .	我們發現了美國最長壽的人口 , 包括七天大進軍人 , 集中在加州洛馬林達附近 。
adventists are conservative methodists .	冒險家是保守派的衛理公會教徒 。
they celebrate their sabbath from sunset on friday till sunset on saturday .	他們在星期五日出日落慶祝安息日直到星期六日出
a " 24hour sanctuary in time , " they call it .	他們稱之為 「 二十四時的庇護 」 。
and they follow five little habits that conveys to them extraordinary longevity , comparatively speaking .	他們遵循五個小習慣 , 相對來說 , 傳達給他們非凡的長壽習慣 。
in america here , life expectancy for the average woman is 80 .	在美國 , 一般女人的平均壽命是80歲 。
but for an adventist woman , their life expectancy is 89 .	但對一個冒險的女性來說 , 她們的預期壽命是89 。
and the difference is even more pronounced among men , who are expected to live about 11 years longer than their american counterparts .	男性之間的差異更明顯他們預期能多活十一年比起美國同伴來說
now , this is a study that followed about 70 , 000 people for 30 years .	這個研究追蹤了大約七萬人三十年
sterling study . and i think it supremely illustrates the premise of this blue zone project .	很傑出的研究 。 而且我認為這可以說是這個藍寶地計畫的基礎
this is a heterogeneous community .	這是一個異質族群 ,
it's white , black , hispanic , asian .	是白人、黑人、西班牙裔、亞洲人 。
the only thing that they have in common are a set of very small lifestyle habits that they follow ritualistically for most of their lives .	他們唯一共有的是一套非常小型的生活習慣 , 他們一輩子在儀式上都會遵從 。
they take their diet directly from the bible .	他們直接從聖經來的飲食
genesis: chapter one , verse [29] , where god talks about legumes and seeds , and on one more stanza about green plants , ostensibly missing is meat .	創世紀:第一章 , 第二十九節 , 上帝談到豆子和種子 , 再談到綠色植物 , 很明顯少了肉 。
they take this sanctuary in time very serious .	他們非常認真地看待這個避難所 。
for 24 hours every week , no matter how busy they are , how stressed out they are at work , where the kids need to be driven , they stop everything and they focus on their god , their social network , and then , hardwired right in the religion , are nature walks .	每週24小時 , 不論多忙 , 工作壓力多大 , 孩子需要被驅使 , 他們停止一切 , 專注於他們的神、他們的社交網路 , 接著 , 在宗教當中 , 天生就是會走路的 。
and the power of this is not that it's done occasionally , the power is it's done every week for a lifetime .	強大的力量並不是偶爾會這樣做 , 強權是每週都為了一生都這麼做 。
none of it's hard . none of it costs money .	一點都不困難 , 一點都不花錢
adventists also tend to hang out with other adventists .	冒險家也常和其他的冒險家在一起
so , if you go to an adventist's party you don't see people swilling jim beam or rolling a joint .	所以 , 如果你去參加一個冒險家的派對你不會看到有人搖著jimbeam或滾動關節
instead they're talking about their next nature walk , exchanging recipes , and yes , they pray .	相反地 , 他們談的是他們的下一本性行走 , 交換食譜 , 沒錯 , 他們禱告 。
but they influence each other in profound and measurable ways .	但它們會以很深遠且可測的方法互相影響 。
this is a culture that has yielded ellsworth whareham .	這個文化孕育了埃爾斯沃•偉倫
ellsworth whareham is 97 years old .	埃爾斯沃•偉倫九十七歲
he's a multimillionaire , yet when a contractor wanted 6 , 000 dollars to build a privacy fence , he said , " for that kind of money i'll do it myself . "	他是千萬富翁可是當包商想要六千美元來建立隱私圍的時候他說: 「 為了那種錢我自己來做 。 」
so for the next three days he was out shoveling cement , and hauling poles around .	所以接下來的三天他都在外頭鏟水泥把杆子拖來拖去
and predictably , perhaps , on the fourth day he ended up in the operating room .	可以預料的 , 也許在第四天 , 他最後到了手術室 。
but not as the guy on the table ; the guy doing openheart surgery .	但不是手術台上這個人而是做開心手術的那個人
at 97 he still does 20 openheart surgeries every month .	九十七歲時 , 他每個月都要做二十次開心手術 。
ed rawlings , 103 years old now , an active cowboy , starts his morning with a swim .	艾德•羅林斯 , 現在一百零三歲是一個活躍的牛仔 , 早上就開始游泳
and on weekends he likes to put on the boards , throw up rooster tails .	在週末時 , 他喜歡踏上衝浪板 , 丟擲雞尾巴 。
her grandson actually lives in the twin cities here .	她的孫子其實住在雙子城這裡 。
she starts her day with lifting weights .	她每天從舉重開始
she rides her bicycle .	她騎著腳踏車
and then she gets in her rootbeer colored 1994 cadillac seville , and tears down the san bernardino freeway , where she still volunteers for seven different organizations .	接著 , 她到她位於1994年的根腹中 , 在聖博納迪諾高速公路上 , 在那裡 , 她仍然是七個不同組織的志工 。
i've been on 19 hardcore expeditions .	我曾參與十九次遠征 。
i'm probably the only person you'll ever meet who rode his bicycle across the sahara desert without sunscreen .	我大概是唯一你認識的人裡唯一會騎著腳踏車穿越撒哈拉沙漠沒有防曬油
but i'll tell you , there is no adventure more harrowing than riding shotgun with marge deton .	但我跟你說 , 沒有任何探險比坐火槍的人還要恐怖 。
" a stranger is a friend i haven't met yet ! " she'd say to me .	「 陌生人是我還沒遇到的朋友 ! 」 她跟我說 。
so , what are the common denominators in these three cultures ?	那麼 , 這三種文化中哪些共同點呢 ?
what are the things that they all do ?	他們都在做什麼 ?
and we managed to boil it down to nine .	我們成功的把它歸結為九項 。
in fact we've done two more blue zone expeditions since this and these common denominators hold true .	事實上 , 自從這之後 , 我們又做了兩次藍寶地探險 , 這些共同點也同樣適用 。
and the first one , and i'm about to utter a heresy here , none of them exercise , at least the way we think of exercise .	第一個 , 我將要向各位報告 , 沒有一個是運動 , 至少是我們對運動的看法 。
instead , they set up their lives so that they are constantly nudged into physical activity .	取而代之的是 , 他們建立的生活 , 使他們不斷地被帶入身體的活動 。
these 100yearold okinawan women are getting up and down off the ground , they sit on the floor , 30 or 40 times a day .	這些百歲的琉球女人每天坐在地板上30到40次
sardinians live in vertical houses , up and down the stairs .	薩丁尼亞人住在垂直的房子裡 , 樓梯上下 。
every trip to the store , or to church or to a friend's house occasions a walk .	每次去商店或教堂或去朋友家都要走路
they don't have any conveniences .	他們沒有任何的便利
there is not a button to push to do yard work or house work .	沒有一個按鈕可以用來做院子或做房子的工作 。
if they want to mix up a cake , they're doing it by hand .	如果他們想攪拌一塊蛋糕 , 他們就用手工製作 。
that burns calories just as much as going on the treadmill does .	和跑步機一樣能燃燒卡路里 ,
when they do do intentional physical activity , it's the things they enjoy . they tend to walk , the only proven way to stave off cognitive decline , and they all tend to have a garden .	當他們有意地做動作時 , 就是他們所享受的東西 。 他們走路時 , 唯一可以被證明能避免認知衰退的方法 , 他們都傾向有一個花園 ,
they know how to set up their life in the right way so they have the right outlook .	他們知道如何以正確的方式建立自己的人生 , 讓他們有正確的人生觀 。
each of these cultures take time to downshift .	每一種文化花時間在降低
the sardinians pray . the seventhday adventists pray .	薩丁尼亞人祈禱 , 祈禱七天的冒險家祈禱
the okinawans have this ancestor veneration .	琉球人的祖先有這種
but when you're in a hurry or stressed out , that triggers something called the inflammatory response , which is associated with everything from alzheimer's disease to cardiovascular disease .	但當你匆匆促促促或壓力大時 , 會引發一種發炎反應 , 這種反應跟每一件事都有關 , 從老年癡呆到心血管疾病 。
when you slow down for 15 minutes a day you turn that inflammatory state into a more antiinflammatory state .	當你一天放慢十五分鐘 , 你就會把那個發炎狀態變成更加抗炎的狀態 。
they have vocabulary for sense of purpose , ikigai , like the okinawans .	他們有語彙 , 為了使命感 , 像琉球人的 「 生存感 」 。
you know the two most dangerous years in your life are the year you're born , because of infant mortality , and the year you retire .	你知道你生命中最危險的兩年就是你出生那年 , 因為嬰兒死亡率以及退休那年
these people know their sense of purpose , and they activate in their life , that's worth about seven years of extra life expectancy .	這些人知道自己的使命感 , 並且啟動他們的生活 , 這價值約七年額外壽命 。
there's no longevity diet .	沒有長壽飲食
instead , these people drink a little bit every day , not a hard sell to the american population .	相反地 , 這些人每天都喝一點酒 , 對美國人口一點都不好賣 。
they tend to eat a plantbased diet .	往往吃植物性飲食
doesn't mean they don't eat meat , but lots of beans and nuts .	不是說他們不吃肉 , 而是有很多豆類和堅果 。
and they have strategies to keep from overeating , little things that nudge them away from the table at the right time .	而且他們有策略不受過食的影響 , 一些小東西在對的時間將他們推離餐桌 。
and then the foundation of all this is how they connect .	所有這些的基礎是他們彼此連結的方式 。
they put their families first , take care of their children and their aging parents .	他們把家人擺第一照顧好小孩跟年邁父母
they all tend to belong to a faithbased community , which is worth between four and 14 extra years of life expectancy if you do it four times a month .	它們全都屬於一個以信仰為基礎的社群 , 值四到十四年的預期壽命 , 如果你每月做四次 。
and the biggest thing here is they also belong to the right tribe .	最重要的是他們也屬於對的部落.
they were either born into or they proactively surrounded themselves with the right people .	他們不是生來就要就是他們積極地圍繞著對的人
we know from the framingham studies , that if your three best friends are obese there is a 50 percent better chance that you'll be overweight .	我們從佛明罕研究中得知如果你三個最好的朋友都胖你有一半的機率會過重
so , if you hang out with unhealthy people , that's going to have a measurable impact over time .	所以 , 如果你和不健康的人混在一起 , 隨著時間就會有顯著的影響 。
instead , if your friend's idea of recreation is physical activity , bowling , or playing hockey , biking or gardening , if your friends drink a little , but not too much , and they eat right , and they're engaged , and they're trusting and trustworthy , that is going to have the biggest impact over time .	反之 , 如果你朋友的休閒活動是體力活動 , 保齡球 , 或打曲棍球、自行車、園藝 , 如果你的朋友喝了一點點 , 但不過量 , 他們吃得很對 , 也很投入 , 信任而且值得信賴 , 那會隨著時間產生最大影響 。
diets don't work . no diet in the history of the world has ever worked for more than two percent of the population .	節食沒用 , 世界歷史上從來沒有減肥成功過百分之二的人口
exercise programs usually start in january ; they're usually done by october .	運動計劃通常一月開始 , 通常十月才會做 。
when it comes to longevity there is no short term fix in a pill or anything else .	談到長壽並沒有短期固定藥物或其他東西
but when you think about it , your friends are longterm adventures , and therefore , perhaps the most significant thing you can do to add more years to your life , and life to your years . thank you very much .	但當你仔細想想 , 你的朋友是長期的冒險 , 因此 , 也許是你能做的最重要的事 , 可以為你的生活增加更多年歲和年歲增生 , 非常感謝你 。
ink that conducts electricity ; a window that turns from clear to opaque at the flip of a switch ; a jelly that makes music . all this stuff exists , and catarina mota says: it's time to play with it . mota leads us on a tour of surprising and cool new materials , and suggests that the way we'll figure out what they're good for is to experiment , tinker and have fun .	墨水能導電 ; 一扇從明確轉向不透明轉向的窗口 ; 一顆製造音樂的果凍 。 所有東西的確存在 。 卡塔琳莫塔說:該是和它一起玩的時候了 。 mota帶領我們一陣驚奇和酷極了的新材料 , 建議我們找出它們有什麼好處 , 就是去做實驗、去玩 。
creativity , design , technology	創造力、設計、科技
catarina mota: play with smart materials	catarinamota:玩智慧型材料
i have a friend in portugal whose grandfather built a vehicle out of a bicycle and a washing machine so he could transport his family .	我有一個在葡萄牙的朋友 , 他的祖父用腳踏車造了一台車 , 還有一台洗衣機 , 讓他能夠運送他的家人 。
he did it because he couldn't afford a car , but also because he knew how to build one .	他這麼做是因為他買不起車 , 也因為他知道如何建造一個
there was a time when we understood how things worked and how they were made , so we could build and repair them , or at the very least make informed decisions about what to buy .	曾經有段時間我們了解事物如何運作 , 及如何被製造出來 , 以便建立和修理 , 或至少能夠做出有根據的判斷來決定要買什麼 。
many of these doityourself practices were lost in the second half of the 20th century .	許多這些diy的做法在二十世紀下半葉失真了 。
but now , the maker community and the opensource model are bringing this kind of knowledge about how things work and what they're made of back into our lives , and i believe we need to take them to the next level , to the components things are made of .	但現在 , 製造者和開放原始碼的模型正把這類知識帶回我們的生活中 , 我相信我們需要把這些知識帶到下一個階段 , 讓組成東西的要素被製造出來 。
for the most part , we still know what traditional materials like paper and textiles are made of and how they are produced .	大部分的時間 , 我們仍然知道紙和紡織品等傳統原料是由什麼製成的 , 以及如何生產出來的 。
but now we have these amazing , futuristic composites plastics that change shape , paints that conduct electricity , pigments that change color , fabrics that light up .	但是現在我們有了這些了不起又有未來感的複合材料 , 可以改變形狀 , 可以畫出可以導電的油漆 , 可以改變顏色的顏料 , 可以發光的布 。
let me show you some examples .	讓我給你們看一些例子 。
so conductive ink allows us to paint circuits instead of using the traditional printed circuit boards or wires .	所以導電油墨讓我們不需要用傳統印刷電路或電線來作畫電路或電線 。
in the case of this little example i'm holding , we used it to create a touch sensor that reacts to my skin by turning on this little light .	在我舉的這個小例子中 , 我們用它來建立一個觸控感測器 , 藉由開啟這個小燈 , 來對我的皮膚產生反應 。
conductive ink has been used by artists , but recent developments indicate that we will soon be able to use it in laser printers and pens .	藝術家用到導電油墨 , 但近期的發展顯示 , 我們很快就能將它用在雷射印表機和筆上 。
and this is a sheet of acrylic infused with colorless lightdiffusing particles .	這種微生物的光環注入了無色的散光粒子 。
what this means is that , while regular acrylic only diffuses light around the edges , this one illuminates across the entire surface when i turn on the lights around it .	意思就是 , 雖然普通的丙烯酸只會在邊緣散光 , 但這顆在我開燈的時候 , 整個表面都會發光 。
two of the known applications for this material include interior design and multitouch systems .	這類材質的應用目前已知有兩個包括室內設計及多點觸控系統 。
and thermochromic pigments change color at a given temperature .	熱變色顏料則會在特定溫度下變色
