so he actually streams twoway audio and video between any two smart devices .	所以他實際上是在任意兩個智慧型設備之間做雙向音訊和視訊串流 。
so you can log in through the browser , and it's kind of like skype on wheels .	所以你可以透過瀏覽器來登入 , 有點像是在輪子上用skype 。
so we were talking before about telepresence , and this is a really cool example .	所以我們之前就談到遠程呈現 , 這是一個很酷的例子 。
you can imagine an eightyearold girl , for example , who has an iphone , and her mom buys her a robot .	你可以想像一個八歲大的女孩 , 例如 , 她有iphone , 而她媽媽買給她一個機器人 。
that girl can take her iphone , put it on the robot , send an email to grandma , who lives on the other side of the country .	那個女孩可以拿著她的iphone , 放在機器人上 , 寄一封電子郵件給住在該國另一端的祖母 。
grandma can log into that robot and play hideandgoseek with her granddaughter for fifteen minutes every single night , when otherwise she might only be able to get to see her granddaughter once or twice a year .	奶奶可以登入那個機器人 , 和她的孫女一起玩捉迷藏遊戲 , 每個晚上十五分鐘 , 否則她一年可能只能去看她的孫女一次或兩次 。
so those are a couple of the really cool things that romo can do today .	所以這些是romo今天能做的幾個很酷的事 。
but i just want to finish by talking about something that we're working on in the future .	但我只想談談我們未來正在努力的事 。
this is actually something that one of our engineers , dom , built in a weekend .	這實際上是我們的一個工程師 , dom , 在一個週末就建造出來的 。
it's built on top of a google open framework called blockly .	它是建立在google開放框架上的 , 叫做blockly 。
this allows you to drag and drop these blocks of semantic code and create any behavior for this robot you want .	這可以讓你拖拉這些方塊的語義代碼 , 創造任何你想要這個機器人的行為 。
you do not have to know how to code to create a behavior for romo .	你不需要知道如何編碼才能創造romo行為 。
and you can actually simulate that behavior in the browser , which is what you see romo doing on the left .	你實際上可以在瀏覽器中去模擬這種行為 , 就像你在左邊看到romo正在做的事 。
and then if you have something you like , you can download it onto your robot and execute it in real life , run the program in real life .	如果你有你喜歡的東西 , 你可以下載到你的機器人 , 在現實生活中執行它 , 在現實生活中執行這個程式 。
and then if you have something you're proud of , you can share it with every other person who owns a robot in the world .	然後如果你有某樣東西你很自豪 , 你可以和世界上任何一個擁有機器人的人分享 。
so all of these wifi–enabled robots actually learn from each other .	因此 , 所有這些無線上網的機器人 , 實際上會互相學習 。
the reason we're so focused on building robots that everyone can train is that we think the most compelling use cases in personal robotics are personal .	我們之所以如此專注於建造一個人人都可以訓練的機器人 , 是因為我們認為在個人機器人中 , 最能引人注目的使用方式 , 是很個人的 。
they change from person to person .	它們會因人而異 。
so we think that if you're going to have a robot in your home , that robot ought to be a manifestation of your own imagination .	所以 , 我們認為 , 如果你要在你的家中有一個機器人 , 那機器人應該是你想像中的一種表現 。
so i wish that i could tell you what the future of personal robotics looks like .	所以我希望我能告訴你個人機器人的未來是什麼樣子 。
to be honest , i have no idea .	老實說 , 我也不知道 。
but what we do know is that it isn't 10 years or 10 billion dollars or a large humanoid robot away .	但我們確實知道的是 , 它不是10年或100億美元 , 就是一個大型的人型機器人走出來 。
the future of personal robotics is happening today , and it's going to depend on small , agile robots like romo and the creativity of people like yourselves .	個人機器人的未來就發生在今天 , 它取決於體積小且敏捷的機器人 , 像romo這樣還有像你們一樣的人的創造力 。
so we can't wait to get you all robots , and we can't wait to see what you build .	所以我們等不及把你全部的機器人給你了 , 我們也等不及要看看你所建造的東西 。
author and activist isabel allende discusses women , creativity , the definition of feminism and , of course , passion in this talk .	作者和社會運動家伊莎貝爾.阿言德討論過女人、創意、女性主義的定義 , 當然 , 還有在這次演講中充滿熱情的熱情 。
entertainment , global issues , love , parenting , storytelling , women , world cultures	娛樂 , 全球議題 , 愛 , 養育 , 說故事 , 女人 , 世界文化
isabel allende tells tales of passion	伊莎貝爾•阿言德講述關於熱情的故事
thank you so much . it's really scary to be here among the smartest of the smart .	非常感謝你們 。 真的很可怕可以來到這位聰明的人之中 。
i'm here to tell you a few tales of passion .	我在這裡要告訴你幾個關於熱情的故事 。
there's a jewish saying that i love .	有個猶太人說我很喜歡
what is truer than truth ? answer: the story .	比事實更真誠的是什麼 ? 答案就是:故事 。
i'm a storyteller . i want to convey something that is truer than truth about our common humanity .	我是一個說故事的人 。 我想要傳達一個事實 , 比事實更真誠 。 關於我們共通的人性 。
all stories interest me , and some haunt me until i end up writing them .	所有故事都引起我的興趣 , 有些故事使我心煩 , 直到我寫它們為止 。
certain themes keep coming up: justice , loyalty , violence , death , political and social issues , freedom .	某些主題不斷出現:正義、忠誠、暴力、死亡、政治及社會議題、自由 。
i'm aware of the mystery around us , so i write about coincidences , premonitions , emotions , dreams , the power of nature , magic .	我意識到我們周遭的奧秘 , 所以我撰寫巧合、預兆、情緒、夢想、自然的力量、魔法 。
in the last 20 years i have published a few books , but i have lived in anonymity until february of 2006 , when i carried the olympic flag in the winter olympics in italy .	在過去的20年裡 , 我出版了幾本書 , 但是我一直活在匿名中 , 直到2006年2月 , 我帶著加州冬季奧運時的旗幟 。
that made me a celebrity . now people recognize me in macy's , and my grandchildren think that i'm cool .	這讓我成了名人 。 現在人們在梅西百貨公司認可我 , 我的孫子們都覺得我很酷 。
allow me to tell you about my four minutes of fame .	讓我告訴你們我名氣的四分鐘
one of the organizers of the olympic ceremony , of the opening ceremony , called me and said that i had been selected to be one of the flagbearers .	一名籌辦奧運開幕式的籌辦人打電話通知我獲選成為護旗者之一
i replied that surely this was a case of mistaken identity because i'm as far as you can get from being an athlete .	我回覆說 , 這肯定是拼錯身分的一個案例 , 因為我從運動員的角度來看 。
actually , i wasn't even sure that i could go around the stadium without a walker .	事實上 , 我甚至不確定自己可以在體育館裡穿梭不需要助行器 。
i was told that this was no laughing matter .	有人告訴我這可不是開玩笑 。
this would be the first time that only women would carry the olympic flag .	這將是第一次 , 只有女性會帶著奧運旗幟 。
five women , representing five continents , and three olympic gold medal winners .	五位女性 , 分別代表五大洲 , 和三位奧運金牌得主 。
my first question was , naturally , what was i going to wear ?	我第一個問題是 , 很自然地 , 我會穿什麼 ?
a uniform , she said , and asked for my measurements .	一件制服 , 她說 , 並且要求我的量尺 。
i had a vision of myself in a fluffy anorak , looking like the michelin man .	我對自己有遠見 , 在一個虛張聲勢的麻醉劑裡面 , 看起來像個米其林人 。
by the middle of february , i found myself in turin , where enthusiastic crowds cheered when any of the 80 olympic teams was in the street .	到了2月中 , 我在杜林 , 那裡充滿熱情的群眾歡呼當80個奧運的隊伍在街上 。
those athletes had sacrificed everything to compete in the games .	那些運動員犧牲了要在遊戲中競爭的一切 。
they all deserved to win , but there's the element of luck .	他們都值得勝任 , 但還有運氣的元素 。
a speck of snow , an inch of ice , the force of the wind , can determine the result of a race or a game .	雪上的火花 , 冰塊 , 風的力量 , 會決定比賽的結果 。
however , what matters most more than training or luck is the heart .	然而 , 最重要的不只是訓練或是運氣好 ,
only a fearless and determined heart will get the gold medal .	只有無懼且堅定的心才能獲得金牌 。
it is all about passion .	這一切都是為了熱情 。
the streets of turin were covered with red posters announcing the slogan of the olympics .	杜林街上滿是紅色海報上面印著奧運標語 。
passion lives here . isn't it always true ?	熱情就在這裡 。 這不一定是真的嗎 ?
heart is what drives us and determines our fate .	心是驅動我們、決定我們的命運的因素 。
that is what i need for my characters in my books: a passionate heart .	這就是我書中角色所需要的:充滿熱情的心 。
i need mavericks , dissidents , adventurers , outsiders and rebels , who ask questions , bend the rules and take risks .	我需要模仿 , 異議者 , 冒險家 , 外人和反叛者 , 問問題的人 , 扭轉規則 , 冒險 。
people like all of you in this room .	像在座各位一樣的人們
nice people with common sense do not make interesting characters .	常識的好人不會製造有趣的角色 。
they only make good former spouses .	他們只會做好前夫 。
in the green room of the stadium , i met the other flag bearers: three athletes , and the actresses susan sarandon and sophia loren .	在體育館的綠色房間裡 , 我認識了其他護旗手:三位運動員 , 還有蘇珊薩倫和蘇菲雅羅蘭 。
also , two women with passionate hearts: wangari maathai , the nobel prizewinner from kenya who has planted 30 million trees . and by doing so , she has changed the soil , the weather , in some places in africa , and of course the economic conditions in many villages .	還有兩位心中充滿熱情的女性來自肯亞的諾貝爾獎得主 , 種了三千萬棵樹 。 如此一來 , 她改變了土壤、天氣 , 在非洲的某些地方 , 當然也改變了許多村落的經濟狀況 。
and somaly mam , a cambodian activist who fights passionately against child prostitution .	還有柬埔寨活動家索瑪利•曼她熱情地反抗孩童妓女 。
when she was 14 years old , her grandfather sold her to a brothel .	14歲時 , 她的祖父把她賣到妓院
she told us of little girls raped by men who believe that having sex with a very young virgin will cure them from aids .	她告訴我們 , 小女孩被男人強暴那些人相信和年紀很小的處女做愛可以治好愛滋病
and of brothels where children are forced to receive five , 15 clients per day , and if they rebel , they are tortured with electricity .	而在小妓院裡 , 孩子們被迫每天接客5 , 15個 , 如果他們反叛 , 就會被電擊折磨 。
in the green room i received my uniform .	在我收到制服的綠色房間裡
it was not the kind of outfit that i normally wear , but it was far from the michelin man suit that i had anticipated . not bad , really .	那不是我平常穿的那種服裝 , 但它離米其林男裝還很遠 , 我曾預期到過 。 其實不好 , 真的 。
i looked like a refrigerator .	我看起來像個冰箱 。
but so did most of the flagbearers , except sophia loren , the universal symbol of beauty and passion .	除了蘇菲雅羅蘭外 , 大部分的旗幟都還有很多美麗與熱情的象徵 。
sophia is over 70 and she looks great .	蘇菲雅超過70歲 , 她看起來很棒 。
she's sexy , slim and tall , with a deep tan .	她很性感、纖瘦、很高 , 帶著很深的棕色 。
now , how can you have a deep tan and have no wrinkles ?	現在 , 你怎麼能有一支深色皮膚且沒有皺紋呢 ?
when asked in a tv interview , " how could she look so good ? "	當電視記者問: 「 她怎麼能這麼好看 ? 」
she replied , " posture . my back is always straight , and i don't make old people's noises . "	她回: 「 保持好的姿勢 。 我的背總是直的 , 我不發出老人的噪音 。 」
so , there you have some free advice from one of the most beautiful women on earth .	所以 , 你有一些免費的建議 , 來自地球上最美麗的女性之一 。
no grunting , no coughing , no wheezing , no talking to yourselves , no farting .	不貪婪、咳嗽、氣喘不自言自語、不放屁
well , she didn't say that exactly .	嗯 , 她並沒有說完全是這樣 。
at some point around midnight , we were summoned to the wings of the stadium , and the loudspeakers announced the olympic flag , and the music started by the way , the same music that starts here , the aida march .	到了約午夜時分 , 我們被召喚去體育館的翅膀 , 擴音器宣佈了奧運會旗 。 順道一提 , 同樣的音樂一開始在這邊演奏 , 阿依達進行了遊行 。
sophia loren was right in front of me she's a foot taller than i am , not counting the poofy hair .	蘇菲雅羅蘭就在我面前 , 她比我高一呎 , 不去算那根大便的頭髮 。
she walked elegantly , like a giraffe on the african savannah , holding the flag on her shoulder . i jogged behind on my tiptoes holding the flag on my extended arm , so that my head was actually under the damn flag .	她優雅地走著 , 就像非洲草原上的長頸鹿將旗子的一角舉在肩上 。 我則在後面小跑步 , 手臂舉著旗子 , 這樣我的頭才真正在那面該死的旗子下面 。
all the cameras were , of course , on sophia .	所有的相機當然是蘇菲雅上
that was fortunate for me , because in most press photos i appear too , although often between sophia's legs .	這對我來說很幸運 , 因為在大部分我出現的新聞照片中 , 雖然通常是出現在蘇菲雅的雙腿之間 。
a place where most men would love to be .	一個多數男人都很想待的地方
the best four minutes of my entire life were those in the olympic stadium .	我一生中最棒的四分鐘 , 是那些在奧運體育館中的人 。
my husband is offended when i say this although i have explained to him that what we do in private usually takes less than four minutes so he shouldn't take it personally .	我老公很生氣 , 當我說這句話時雖然我曾向他解釋 , 我們私下作的事通常都花不到4分鐘 , 所以他不應該親自承受 。
i have all the press clippings of those four magnificent minutes , because i don't want to forget them when old age destroys my brain cells .	我擁有那四分鐘的所有剪報因為我不想忘記這些年邁破壞我的腦細胞
i want to carry in my heart forever the key word of the olympics passion .	我想永遠的懷著奧運的關鍵字
so here's a tale of passion .	這裡有一個關於熱情的故事 。
the year is 1998 , the place is a prison camp for tutsi refugees in congo .	時間是1998年 , 地點是剛果境內圖西族難民營 。
by the way , 80 percent of all refugees and displaced people in the world are women and girls .	順帶一提 , 世界上80%的難民及流民都是婦女及女童 。
we can call this place in congo a death camp , because those who are not killed will die of disease or starvation .	我們可以把這個地方稱為剛果的死亡集中營 , 因為那些沒有被殺的人 , 都會死於疾病或飢餓 。
the protagonists of this story are a young woman , rose mapendo , and her children .	這個故事的主角是一名年輕女子 , 蘿絲•瑪班多 , 也是她的孩子 。
she's pregnant and a widow .	她懷孕了而且還是寡婦 。
soldiers have forced her to watch as her husband was tortured and killed .	士兵強迫她看著她的丈夫被虐待和殺害 。
somehow she manages to keep her seven children alive , and a few months later , she gives birth to premature twins .	不知怎麼的 , 她竟然讓她7個孩子活了下來 , 幾個月後 , 她生下雙胞胎 。
two tiny little boys .	兩個小男孩
she cuts the umbilical cord with a stick , and ties it with her own hair .	她用棍子剪斷臍帶然後用頭髮將之綁起來
she names the twins after the camp's commanders to gain their favor , and feeds them with black tea because her milk cannot sustain them .	她用營地的指揮官的名字為雙胞胎命名以取得他們的青睞 , 並用黑色茶餵他們因為她的牛奶無法維持它們 。
when the soldiers burst in her cell to rape her oldest daughter , she grabs hold of her and refuses to let go , even when they hold a gun to her head .	當士兵闖進她的牢房要強暴她大女兒時她抓住她的大女兒不放手即使他們拿著槍抵著她的頭
somehow , the family survives for 16 months , and then , by extraordinary luck , and the passionate heart of a young american man , sasha chanoff , who manages to put her in a u . s . rescue plane , rose mapendo and her nine children end up in phoenix , arizona , where they're now living and thriving .	不知怎的 , 這家人存活了16個月 , 然後 , 靠著絕佳的運氣 , 還有一個美國年輕男子薩夏•查洛夫的熱心 , 他成功地把她放到美國救援機上 , 蘿絲和她的九個孩子 , 最後到了亞利桑那州鳳凰城 , 在那裡他們活著、茁壯成長 。
mapendo , in swahili , means great love .	瑪班多在斯瓦希里語中的意思是很棒的愛
the protagonists of my books are strong and passionate women like rose mapendo .	我書中的主角都是堅強且富熱情的女性就像蘿絲•瑪班多
i don't make them up . there's no need for that .	我不編造它們 , 不需要這些 。
i look around and i see them everywhere .	我環顧四周 , 隨處可見 。
i have worked with women and for women all my life .	我一生都在研究女性和女性 。
i know them well .	我對他們很了解 。
i was born in ancient times , at the end of the world , in a patriarchal catholic and conservative family .	我出生在遠古時代 , 在世界末日 , 在父權天主教及保守家庭中 。
no wonder that by age five i was a raging feminist although the term had not reached chile yet , so nobody knew what the heck was wrong with me .	難怪我到了五歲 , 是個憤怒的女權主義者雖然這個名詞還沒到智利 , 所以沒有人知道我到底是哪根筋不對勁 。
i would soon find out that there was a high price to pay for my freedom , and for questioning the patriarchy .	我很快就發現 , 為了我的自由而付出高昂的代價 , 以及質疑父權制度 。
but i was happy to pay it , because for every blow that i received , i was able to deliver two .	但我高興地付出代價 , 因為每當我被擊中一擊 , 我就能夠分送兩顆 。
once , when my daughter paula was in her twenties , she said to me that feminism was dated , that i should move on .	有一次 , 我的女兒寶拉二十多歲 , 她告訴我 , 女權主義已經過時了 , 我應該繼續走下去 。
we had a memorable fight . feminism is dated ?	我們經歷了一場令人難忘的戰鬥 。 女權主義約會嗎 ?
yes , for privileged women like my daughter and all of us here today , but not for most of our sisters in the rest of the world who are still forced into premature marriage , prostitution , forced labor they have children that they don't want or they cannot feed .	沒錯 , 對於像我女兒和在座各位這樣有特權的女性來說 , 但不是對世界上大部分的姊妹們 , 她們仍然被迫結婚 , 賣淫 , 被迫勞動為她們不想要或無法養活的孩子 。
they have no control over their bodies or their lives .	他們無法掌控自己的身體或人生 。
they have no education and no freedom .	他們沒有受過教育也沒有自由
they are raped , beaten up and sometimes killed with impunity .	他們會被強暴、毆打 , 有時還會因為懲罰而被殺 。
for most western young women of today , being called a feminist is an insult .	對於現今大部分西方年輕女性來說 , 被稱為 「 女性主義者 」 是種侮辱 。
feminism has never been sexy , but let me assure you that it never stopped me from flirting , and i have seldom suffered from lack of men .	女權從來沒有很性感 , 但讓我保證我從來沒有因此失去調情 , 我也很少缺乏男性 。
feminism is not dead , by no means .	女權還沒死 , 絕對不是 。
it has evolved . if you don't like the term , change it , for goddess' sake .	它演化了 。 如果你不喜歡這個名詞就換它一下 , 換女神之名 。
call it aphrodite , or venus , or bimbo , or whatever you want ; the name doesn't matter , as long as we understand what it is about , and we support it .	稱之為愛芙若蒂、維納斯、布波 , 或其他你想要的東西 ; 名稱不重要 , 只要我們了解它是什麼 , 就會支持它 。
so here's another tale of passion , and this is a sad one .	接下來是另一種熱情的故事而這則是悲傷的故事
the place is a small women's clinic in a village in bangladesh .	這個地方是孟加拉一個小婦女的診所 。
the year is 2005 .	這一年是2005年
jenny is a young american dental hygienist who has gone to the clinic as a volunteer during her threeweek vacation .	珍妮是個年輕的美國衛生專家 , 她到診所當義工 , 在度假期間 。
she's prepared to clean teeth , but when she gets there , she finds out that there are no doctors , no dentists , and the clinic is just a hut full of flies .	她準備了乾淨的牙齒 , 但當她到達那裡時 , 她發現那裡沒有醫生 , 沒有牙醫 , 診所只不過是一個蒼蠅的小屋 。
outside , there is a line of women who have waited several hours to be treated .	在外面 , 有一排的女人已經等了好幾個小時才接受治療 。
the first patient is in excruciating pain because she has several rotten molars .	第一個病人痛苦難當 , 因為她有好幾顆腐爛的臼齒 。
jenny realizes that the only solution is to pull out the bad teeth .	珍妮意識到 , 唯一解決方案就是拔掉壞牙 。
she's not licensed for that ; she has never done it .	她沒有執照 , 她從來沒有做過 。
she risks a lot and she's terrified .	她常常去冒險 , 而且很害怕 。
she doesn't even have the proper instruments , but fortunately she has brought some novocaine .	她甚至沒有合適的儀器 , 幸運的是她帶來了一些禁果 。
jenny has a brave and passionate heart .	珍妮有顆勇敢而充滿熱情的心
she murmurs a prayer and she goes ahead with the operation .	她默默禱告 , 然後開始營運 。
at the end , the relieved patient kisses her hands .	最後 , 病患吻了她的手 。
that day the hygienist pulls out many more teeth .	那天衛生人員拔出更多的牙齒 。
the next morning , when she comes again to the socalled clinic , her first patient is waiting for her with her husband .	第二天早上 , 當她再次來到所謂的診所時她的第一個病人跟丈夫在那等她
the woman's face looks like a watermelon .	這位女士的臉看起來像個西瓜 。
it is so swollen that you can't even see the eyes .	腫到看不見眼睛 。
the husband , furious , threatens to kill the american .	丈夫 , 憤怒 , 威脅要殺死美國人 ,
jenny is horrified at what she has done , but then the translator explains that the patient's condition has nothing to do with the operation .	珍妮被自己造成的後果嚇壞了 , 但翻譯解釋病人的狀況和手術無關 。
the day before , her husband beat her up because she was not home in time to prepare dinner for him .	前一天 , 她的丈夫因為不在家為他準備晚餐 , 而打了她一頓
millions of women live like this today .	今天數百萬的女性都這樣過生活 。
they are the poorest of the poor .	他們是最貧窮的人們 。
although women do twothirds of the world's labor , they own less than one percent of the world's assets .	雖然全世界有三分之二的勞動力 , 但卻擁有不到1%的全球資產 。
they are paid less than men for the same work if they're paid at all , and they remain vulnerable because they have no economic independence , and they are constantly threatened by exploitation , violence and abuse .	她們與男人同工 , 薪水較低 , 如果她們有薪水可領 , 而且她們仍然很脆弱 , 因為她們沒有經濟獨立的權利 , 且她們經常受到剝削、暴力和虐待的威脅 。
it is a fact that giving women education , work , the ability to control their own income , inherit and own property , benefits the society .	事實是給予女性教育 , 工作 , 掌管自己收入的能力 , 繼承並擁有財產 , 為社會帶來益處 。
if a woman is empowered , her children and her family will be better off .	如果女人有力量的話 , 她的孩子和家人就會過得更好 。
if families prosper , the village prospers , and eventually so does the whole country .	如果家庭繁榮 , 村落的繁榮 , 最終整個國家也是如此 。
wangari maathai goes to a village in kenya .	旺加里•馬塔伊到肯亞的村落
she talks with the women and explains that the land is barren because they have cut and sold the trees .	她和女人們談 , 並解釋土地已經貧瘠 , 因為他們砍了樹和種了 。
she gets the women to plant new trees and water them , drop by drop .	她讓女人們種植新的樹木然後澆水 , 一滴接著一滴
in a matter of five or six years , they have a forest , the soil is enriched , and the village is saved .	只要五六年 , 他們就有一片森林 , 土壤得以豐富 , 村落得以拯救 。
the poorest and most backward societies are always those that put women down .	最貧窮和最落後的社會總是那些會讓女性失望的社會 。
yet this obvious truth is ignored by governments and also by philanthropy .	但這個顯而易見的事實卻被政府以及慈善機構忽略 。
for every dollar given to a women's program , 20 dollars are given to men's programs .	女性相關計畫每得到1美元就有20美元給男性生計劃
women are 51 percent of humankind .	女性佔人類總數的51%
empowering them will change everything more than technology and design and entertainment .	給予他們力量 , 將改變一切 , 不僅是科技、設計和娛樂 。
i can promise you that women working together linked , informed and educated can bring peace and prosperity to this forsaken planet .	我可以向你保證 , 女性一起工作聯繫、通知、受教育 , 可以為這個分裂的星球帶來和平與繁榮 。
in any war today , most of the casualties are civilians , mainly women and children . they are collateral damage .	在今天的任何戰爭中 , 大部分的傷亡者是平民 , 主要是婦女和兒童 。 她們是附帶損傷 。
men run the world , and look at the mess we have .	男人掌管世界 , 看看我們所擁有的亂
what kind of world do we want ?	我們想要怎樣的世界 ?
this is a fundamental question that most of us are asking .	這是我們大多數人都在問的基本問題 。
does it make sense to participate in the existing world order ?	參與現有的世界秩序是否合理 ?
we want a world where life is preserved and the quality of life is enriched for everybody , not only for the privileged .	我們想要一個保存生命的世界 , 一個生活品質能夠被所有人激發 , 不只是特權人士 。
in january i saw an exhibit of fernando botero's paintings at the uc berkeley library .	一月份 , 我看到費南多•巴特羅的畫展在柏克萊加大大學圖書館
no museum or gallery in the united states , except for the new york gallery that carries botero's work , has dared to show the paintings because the theme is the abu ghraib prison .	在美國 , 沒有任何博物館或畫廊 , 除了紐約畫廊 , 會帶著巴特羅的作品 , 勇敢地展示出繪畫 , 因為那主題是發生在阿布格萊布監獄 。
they are huge paintings of torture and abuse of power , in the voluminous botero style .	它們是大量的折磨及濫用權力的畫作 , 以大量的推特方式呈現 。
i have not been able to get those images out of my mind or my heart .	我無法將那些影像從我的腦海或我的心中
what i fear most is power with impunity .	我最擔心的是無障礙的權力 。
i fear abuse of power , and the power to abuse .	我害怕濫用權力 , 以及濫用權力 。
in our species , the alpha males define reality , and force the rest of the pack to accept that reality and follow the rules .	在我們這個物種中 , 雄性領袖會定義現實 , 迫使雄性領袖接受那樣的現實 , 並遵守規則 。
the rules change all the time , but they always benefit them , and in this case , the trickledown effect , which does not work in economics , works perfectly .	規則常常在變 , 但規則總是對他們有益 , 在這個例子中 , 「 下滲效應 」 並不能在經濟中運作 , 完美地運作 。
abuse trickles down from the top of the ladder to the bottom .	虐待會從梯子的頂端向下滲到下方 。
women and children , especially the poor , are at the bottom .	婦女和兒童 , 尤其是窮人 , 待在最底層 。
even the most destitute of men have someone they can abuse a woman or a child .	即使是最貧困的男人也有人可以虐待女人或小孩
i'm fed up with the power that a few exert over the many through gender , income , race , and class .	我受夠了少數幾個人透過性別、收入、種族和階級來消耗的力量 。
i think that the time is ripe to make fundamental changes in our civilization .	我認為現在時機已經成熟 , 可以為我們的文明做出根本的改變 。
but for real change , we need feminine energy in the management of the world .	但 , 若要真正改變 , 我們就需要女性的能量在世界上的管理 。
we need a critical number of women in positions of power , and we need to nurture the feminine energy in men .	我們需要讓女性佔有權力地位的關鍵人物 , 我們需要培養男性中女性的能量 。
i'm talking about men with young minds , of course .	我指的是有年輕頭腦的男人 , 當然
old guys are hopeless ; we have to wait for them to die off .	老男人是毫無希望的 , 我們必須等他們離世
yes , i would love to have sophia loren's long legs and legendary breasts .	沒錯 , 我很想擁有蘇菲雅羅蘭的長腿和傳說中的乳房 。
but given a choice , i would rather have the warrior hearts of wangari maathai , somaly mam , jenny and rose mapendo .	但如果有選擇的話 , 我寧願有勇士的心像汪佳•瑪太、蘇曼麗•瑪太、珍妮和蘿絲•瑪班多
i want to make this world good .	我想要讓這個世界變得好 。
not better , but to make it good .	不是比較好 , 而是要讓它變好 。
why not ? it is possible . look around in this room all this knowledge , energy , talent and technology .	為何不呢 ? 這是可能的 。 看看這間屋子裡充滿了知識、能量、才華和科技
let's get off our fannies , roll up our sleeves and get to work , passionately , in creating an almost perfect world .	讓我們離開我們的粉絲 , 捲起袖子 , 開始工作 , 創造一個近乎完美的世界 。
every day , in a city the size of london , 30 million meals are served . but where does all the food come from ? architect carolyn steel discusses the daily miracle of feeding a city , and shows how ancient food routes shaped the modern world .	每天 , 在倫敦這麼大的城市 , 提供三千萬份餐點 , 但一切都是從哪裡來的 ? 建築師卡魯琳鋼製討論的是要餵飽一個城市的日常奇蹟 , 並顯示古代食物路線如何形塑現代世界 。
cities , culture , food , global issues	城市、文化、食物、全球議題
carolyn steel: how food shapes our cities	carolynsteel:食物如何塑造我們的城市
how do you feed a city ?	如何餵飽一個城市 ?
it's one of the great questions of our time .	這是我們這個時代一個很棒的問題 。
yet it's one that's rarely asked .	卻很少被問到 。
we take it for granted that if we go into a shop or restaurant , or indeed into this theater's foyer in about an hour's time , there is going to be food there waiting for us , having magically come from somewhere .	我們理所當然地認為如果我們走進一家商店或餐廳 , 或確實走進這間戲院 , 大概一個小時內 , 那裡將會有食物在等著我們 , 神奇地從某處過來 。
but when you think that every day for a city the size of london , enough food has to be produced , transported , bought and sold , cooked , eaten , disposed of , and that something similar has to happen every day for every city on earth , it's remarkable that cities get fed at all .	但當你想像每天為倫敦這麼大的城市每天要有足夠的食物被製造 , 運輸 , 買賣 , 煮飯 , 吃掉 , 丟棄 , 那種類似的事情 , 每天都要發生 , 為了每個城市 , 都必須有很高的糧食可供給 。
we live in places like this as if they're the most natural things in the world , forgetting that because we're animals and that we need to eat , we're actually as dependent on the natural world as our ancient ancestors were .	我們生活在這樣的地方 , 彷彿是世上最自然的東西 , 忘了這點 , 因為我們是動物 , 我們需要吃 , 我們其實和我們的遠古祖先一樣依賴大自然 。
and as more of us move into cities , more of that natural world is being transformed into extraordinary landscapes like the one behind me it's soybean fields in mato grosso in brazil in order to feed us .	隨著更多人搬進城市 , 更多自然世界被轉變為非凡的景觀 , 就像我身後的那個景象一樣──在巴西馬托格羅索的馬托格羅索的大豆田 , 為我們提供食物 。
these are extraordinary landscapes , but few of us ever get to see them .	這些非凡的景色但少有人見識過
and increasingly these landscapes are not just feeding us either .	越來越多的風景不只用來餵飽我們 。
as more of us move into cities , more of us are eating meat , so that a third of the annual grain crop globally now gets fed to animals rather than to us human animals .	更多人搬到城市裡 , 更多人在吃肉 , 每年全球有三分之一的年穀物被拿來餵動物 , 而不是用在我們人類 。
and given that it takes three times as much grain actually ten times as much grain to feed a human if it's passed through an animal first , that's not a very efficient way of feeding us .	而要花三倍的穀物--事實上是十倍的穀物--如果用動物穿過的話 , 餵飽我們並不是很有效率的方法 。
and it's an escalating problem too .	這也是一個日趨劇增的問題 。
by 2050 , it's estimated that twice the number of us are going to be living in cities .	估計到了2050年 , 我們居住的人口數是城市裡的兩倍 。
and it's also estimated that there is going to be twice as much meat and dairy consumed .	同時估計也將有兩倍的肉與乳製品消耗
so meat and urbanism are rising hand in hand .	所以肉類和城市化的手勢都在上升 。
and that's going to pose an enormous problem .	這將是個巨大的問題 。
six billion hungry carnivores to feed , by 2050 .	要餵飽六十億個肉食性動物到2050年
that's a big problem . and actually if we carry on as we are , it's a problem we're very unlikely to be able to solve .	那是個很大的問題 。 如果我們繼續走下去 , 那會是個我們無法解決的問題 。
nineteen million hectares of rainforest are lost every year to create new arable land .	每年有一千九百萬公頃的熱帶雨林消失 , 造就了新的可耕地 。
although at the same time we're losing an equivalent amount of existing arables to salinization and erosion .	雖然同時我們也失去相當大量的可耕地 , 來對鹽化和侵蝕 。
we're very hungry for fossil fuels too .	我們也非常渴望石化燃料 。
it takes about 10 calories to produce every calorie of food that we consume in the west .	在西方 , 每製造一卡路里的食物要耗去十卡路里的能量
and even though there is food that we are producing at great cost , we don't actually value it .	儘管我們有些食物以極大的成本生產 , 但事實上我們並不重視它 。
half the food produced in the usa is currently thrown away .	半數在美國生產的食物 , 目前都被丟棄 。
and to end all of this , at the end of this long process , we're not even managing to feed the planet properly .	要結束這一切 , 在這個漫長過程的最後 , 我們甚至沒有管理好要讓地球有適當的食物 。
a billion of us are obese , while a further billion starve .	幾十億人過胖 , 另外還有十億人挨餓
none of it makes very much sense .	沒有一個很有道理 。
and when you think that 80 percent of global trade in food now is controlled by just five multinational corporations , it's a grim picture .	當你認為現在全球百分之八十的食物交易只掌握在五大跨國企業這是一個嚴峻的照片
as we're moving into cities , the world is also embracing a western diet .	在我們搬進城市的同時 , 世界也在擁抱西方飲食 。
and if we look to the future , it's an unsustainable diet .	如果我們看向未來 , 它是不可持續的飲食 。
so how did we get here ?	所以 , 我們怎麼會變成這樣 ?
and more importantly , what are we going to do about it ?	更重要的是 , 我們對此該怎麼辦 ?
well , to answer the slightly easier question first , about 10 , 000 years ago , i would say , is the beginning of this process in the ancient near east , known as the fertile crescent .	嗯 , 先回答稍微容易一點的問題 , 大約一萬年前 , 我會說是這個過程的開始 , 在古老的近東地區 , 稱為新月沃土 。
because , as you can see , it was crescent shaped .	因為 , 如你所見 , 它是近代的形狀 。
and it was also fertile .	而且肥沃 。
and it was here , about 10 , 000 years ago , that two extraordinary inventions , agriculture and urbanism , happened roughly in the same place and at the same time .	大約在一萬年前 , 在這裡有兩項非凡的發明農業和都市化大約在同一地點同一時間發生
this is no accident , because agriculture and cities are bound together . they need each other .	這並非偶然 , 因為農業與城市是分不開的 , 它們互相需要
because it was discovery of grain by our ancient ancestors for the first time that produced a food source that was large enough and stable enough to support permanent settlements .	因為那是人類遠古祖先第一次發現穀物的來源 , 大到足以支撐永久定居地的食物 。
and if we look at what those settlements were like , we see they were compact .	如果我們觀察一下這些居住地的樣子 , 我們會發現它們很緊密 。
they were surrounded by productive farm land and dominated by large temple complexes like this one at ur , that were , in fact , effectively , spiritualized , central food distribution centers .	他們被有生產力的農場包圍並以大型神殿為中心像這一個在烏爾的神殿在當時是神聖化的中央食物分配中心
because it was the temples that organized the harvest , gathered in the grain , offered it to the gods , and then offered the grain that the gods didn't eat back to the people .	因為是寺廟安排了收割 , 聚集在穀物上 , 將之送給神 , 接著提供了那些神不吃回來的穀物 。
so , if you like , the whole spiritual and physical life of these cities was dominated by the grain and the harvest that sustained them .	所以 , 如果你願意 , 這些城市的精神及實體生活是由穀物和穀物所主宰 , 而能夠維持它們的收穫 。
and in fact , that's true of every ancient city .	事實上每個古老的城市都是如此
but of course not all of them were that small .	當然他們沒有全部都那麼小 。
famously , rome had about a million citizens by the first century a . d .	著名的是 , 羅馬在西元一世紀前 , 擁有約一百萬公民
so how did a city like this feed itself ?	所以 , 像這樣的城市是怎麼來的 ?
the answer is what i call " ancient food miles . "	答案就是我所謂的 「 古代食物里程 」 。
basically , rome had access to the sea , which made it possible for it to import food from a very long way away .	基本上 , 羅馬有機會接近海水這使得食物從很遠的地方運來
this is the only way it was possible to do this in the ancient world , because it was very difficult to transport food over roads , which were rough .	這是在遠古時期 , 唯一能做到這點的方法 , 因為把食物運到馬路上是非常困難的 , 這種做法很粗糙 。
and the food obviously went off very quickly .	食物很快就壞掉 。
so rome effectively waged war on places like carthage and egypt just to get its paws on their grain reserves .	所以羅馬有效地對地方發動戰爭 , 例如在他們的穀物保護區和埃及 , 只為了在他們的穀物儲備上取得爪子 。
and , in fact , you could say that the expansion of the empire was really sort of one long , drawn out militarized shopping spree , really .	事實上 , 你可以說 , 整個帝國的擴張其實是非常長的一個 , 從軍事化的購物中心抽取出來的 。
in fact i love the fact , i just have to mention this: rome in fact used to import oysters from london , at one stage . i think that's extraordinary .	事實上我很喜歡這個事實 , 我只需要提到羅馬事實上用來進口牡蠣來自倫敦的牡蠣在某個階段我覺得這很不平凡
so rome shaped its hinterland through its appetite .	所以羅馬靠著食慾塑造了它的內陸 。
but the interesting thing is that the other thing also happened in the preindustrial world .	但有趣的是 , 另一件事情也發生在工業化前的世界 。
if we look at a map of london in the 17th century , we can see that its grain , which is coming in from the thames , along the bottom of this map .	如果我們看看十七世紀的倫敦地圖 , 我們可以看到 , 它的穀物是從泰晤士河運進來的 , 沿著這張地圖的下方 。
so the grain markets were to the south of the city .	所以穀物市場到了城市的南方
and the roads leading up from them to cheapside , which was the main market , were also grain markets .	而通往廉價市場的道路也是主要市場的穀物市場
and if you look at the name of one of those streets , bread street , you can tell what was going on there 300 years ago .	如果你看看那些街道的名稱 , 麵包街 , 你可以判斷出300年前在那裏發生了什麼 。
and the same of course was true for fish .	魚類也一樣 。
fish was , of course , coming in by river as well . same thing .	當然 , 魚是從河裡來的 。 同樣的道理 。
and of course billingsgate , famously , was london's fish market , operating onsite here until the mid1980s .	當然比林斯門是有名的 , 是倫敦的魚市場 , 一直到1980年代中期都在使用 。
which is extraordinary , really , when you think about it .	仔細想想 , 這是很不尋常的 。
everybody else was wandering around with mobile phones that looked like bricks and sort of smelly fish happening down on the port .	其他人都帶著看起來像磚塊的手機到處逛逛 , 聞起來像港口裡的魚 。
this is another thing about food in cities: once its roots into the city are established , they very rarely move .	這是另一個與城市食物有關的一個現象:一旦它的根源被建立起來 , 它們幾乎不會移動 。
meat is a very different story because , of course , animals could walk into the city .	肉類的故事不盡相同 , 因為 , 當然 , 動物可以走進城市 。
so much of london's meat was coming from the northwest , from scotland and wales .	所以倫敦的大部分肉品是從西北方來的從蘇格蘭及威爾斯
so it was coming in , and arriving at the city at the northwest , which is why smithfield , london's very famous meat market , was located up there .	所以 , 它就來了 , 到了西北方的城市 , 這也是為什麼史密斯菲爾德 , 倫敦非常著名的肉市場 , 被放到那裡 。
poultry was coming in from east anglia and so on , to the northeast .	家禽類從東安格利亞進入東北方
i feel a bit like a weather woman doing this . anyway , and so the birds were coming in with their feet protected with little canvas shoes .	我覺得這有點像天氣女子氣象 。 總之 , 所以鳥類會用腳保護小帆布 。
and then when they hit the eastern end of cheapside , that's where they were sold , which is why it's called poultry .	然後當他們撞到廉價商店東端時 , 這就是為什麼他們被賣掉的原因 , 叫做poultry 。
and , in fact , if you look at the map of any city built before the industrial age , you can trace food coming in to it .	事實上 , 如果你去看任何城市地圖 , 工業時代前就已經建成 , 你可以追蹤食物的來源 。
you can actually see how it was physically shaped by food , both by reading the names of the streets , which give you a lot of clues .	你可以看到它是如何被食物所塑造的 , 兩者都藉由閱讀街道的名稱 , 這給你很大的線索 。
friday street , in a previous life , is where you went to buy your fish on a friday .	星期五街 , 在以前是你在星期五去買魚的地方 。
but also you have to imagine it full of food .	但你也要想像它佈滿了食物 。
because the streets and the public spaces were the only places where food was bought and sold .	因為街道和公共空間是唯一買賣食物的地方 。
and if we look at an image of smithfield in 1830 you can see that it would have been very difficult to live in a city like this and be unaware of where your food came from .	如果我們看一張1830年史密斯菲爾德的圖片你會發現很難住在這樣的一個城市而且不清楚你的食物從哪裡來
in fact , if you were having sunday lunch , the chances were it was mooing or bleating outside your window about three days earlier .	事實上 , 如果你在吃禮拜天的午餐的話 , 可能三天前在你的窗外吹著或流血的可能性 。
so this was obviously an organic city , part of an organic cycle .	這顯然是個有機城市 , 有機循環的一部分 。
and then 10 years later everything changed .	十年後一切都改變了
this is an image of the great western in 1840 .	這是1840年大西部的圖像
and as you can see , some of the earliest train passengers were pigs and sheep .	你可以看到 , 最早的火車旅客中有一些是豬和羊 。
so all of a sudden , these animals are no longer walking into market .	所以一夕之間 , 這些動物不再自己走進市場
they're being slaughtered out of sight and mind , somewhere in the countryside .	牠們在眼不見心為淨的情況下被屠宰在鄉下的某處
and they're coming into the city by rail .	並藉由鐵路進入城市 。
and this changes everything .	而這會改變一切 。
to start off with , it makes it possible for the first time to grow cities , really any size and shape , in any place .	從頭開始 , 第一次發展城市 , 任何大小和形狀 , 都可以在任何地方發展 。
cities used to be constrained by geography ; they used to have to get their food through very difficult physical means .	過去城市受限於地理環境 ; 過去城市必須用非常困難的手段來取得食物 。
all of a sudden they are effectively emancipated from geography .	突然間 , 它們從地理環境中被有效地解放了 。
and as you can see from these maps of london , in the 90 years after the trains came , it goes from being a little blob that was quite easy to feed by animals coming in on foot , and so on , to a large splurge , that would be very , very difficult to feed with anybody on foot , either animals or people .	正如你們從倫敦的這些地圖上所看到的 , 在火車到來的九十年後 , 火車從一個很容易餵飽的小點 , 動物走進來 , 如此這般 , 到一個很大的突觸 , 很難跟任何人一起吃東西 , 不論是動物或人 。
and of course that was just the beginning . after the trains came cars , and really this marks the end of this process .	當然這只是個開端 。 火車之後又來了汽車 , 真正的呈現了這個過程的結局
it's the final emancipation of the city from any apparent relationship with nature at all .	這是城市最終的解放從任何明顯與自然的關係
and this is the kind of city that's devoid of smell , devoid of mess , certainly devoid of people , because nobody would have dreamed of walking in such a landscape .	這種城市聞不到、沒有混亂 , 也沒有人的特質 , 因為沒有人會夢想能在這片土地上行走 。
in fact , what they did to get food was they got in their cars , drove to a box somewhere on the outskirts , came back with a week's worth of shopping , and wondered what on earth to do with it .	事實上 , 他們獲得食物的做法是他們上了車 , 開到郊區的一個箱子上 , 帶著一個星期的購物回來 , 想著 , 到底該拿它怎麼辦 。
and this really is the moment when our relationship , both with food and cities , changes completely .	而這就是我們與食物、城市的關係完全改變的時刻 。
here we have food that used to be the center , the social core of the city at the periphery .	這裡我們有食物曾經是中心地帶 , 是城市的社會核心--邊緣地帶 。
it used to be a social event , buying and selling food .	曾經是社交活動 , 買賣食物 。
we used to cook ; now we just add water , or a little bit of an egg if you're making a cake or something .	我們曾經做菜 ; 現在只需要加點水或是一點點卵 , 如果你要做蛋糕的話
we don't smell food to see if it's okay to eat .	我們聞不到食物 , 看食物是否安然無恙 。
we just read the back of a label on a packet .	我們只看一下包裝上的標籤 。
and we don't value food . we don't trust it .	而且我們不重視食物 。 我們不信任它 。
so instead of trusting it , we fear it .	所以 , 我們不再信任它 , 而是害怕它 。
and instead of valuing it , we throw it away .	而不是去評價它 , 我們丟掉它 。
one of the great ironies of modern food systems is that they've made the very thing they promised to make easier much harder .	現代飲食習慣最諷刺的一點就是他們把前景看得很簡單
by making it possible to build cities anywhere and any place , they've actually distanced us from our most important relationship , which is that of us and nature .	透過讓城市可以在任何地方、任何地方建造城市 , 實際上 , 它們已經讓我們遠離了最重要的關係 , 就是我們和自然界的關係 。
and also they've made us dependent on systems that only they can deliver , that , as we've seen , are unsustainable .	而且它們也讓我們依賴只有它們可以運送的系統 。 如同我們所見 , 這些系統是不可持續的 。
so what are we going to do about that ?	所以 , 我們要怎麼做 ?
it's not a new question .	這不是個新的問題 。
500 years ago it's what thomas more was asking himself .	五百年前湯瑪斯.摩爾就在問他自己:
this is the frontispiece of his book " utopia . "	這是他的書《烏托邦》前茅 。
and it was a series of semiindependent citystates , if that sounds remotely familiar , a day's walk from one another where everyone was basically farmingmad , and grew vegetables in their back gardens , and ate communal meals together , and so on .	而且那是一系列半自給自足的城邦 , 如果那聽起來很熟悉 , 每天各自散步 , 基本上每個人都在耕作 , 在他們的後花園種蔬菜 , 一起享用餐點等等 。
and i think you could argue that food is a fundamental ordering principle of utopia , even though more never framed it that way .	我認為 , 你可以主張 , 食物是烏托邦的基本原則 , 即使多數人未曾如此形容它 。
and here is another very famous " utopian " vision , that of ebenezer howard , " the garden city . "	還有另一個非常著名的 「 烏托邦 」 的遠景 , 是埃本内則.霍華的 " 田園城市 " 。
same idea: series of semiindependent citystates , little blobs of metropolitan stuff with arable land around , joined to one another by railway .	同樣的想法:一系列半自給自足的城邦 , 小小的都會區 , 周圍有可耕地 , 加入彼此通用鐵路 。
and again , food could be said to be the ordering principle of his vision .	食物可以被說是他視覺的原則 。
it even got built , but nothing to do with this vision that howard had .	它甚至被做出來了 , 但與霍華所擁有的願景無關 。
and that is the problem with these utopian ideas , that they are utopian .	而這就是這些烏托邦理念的問題他們就是烏托邦
utopia was actually a word that thomas moore used deliberately .	烏托邦的確是湯瑪斯.摩爾刻意使用的字眼 。
it was a kind of joke , because it's got a double derivation from the greek .	這是個笑話 , 因為希臘文裡有雙重的衍生物 。
it can either mean a good place , or no place .	它可能意味著一個好地方 , 或沒有地方 。
because it's an ideal . it's an imaginary thing . we can't have it .	因為它是理想的、想像的、我們無法擁有它
and i think , as a conceptual tool for thinking about the very deep problem of human dwelling , that makes it not much use .	我認為 , 作為一個概念工具 , 用來思考人類居住的深刻問題 , 使得它不太有用 。
so i've come up with an alternative , which is sitopia , from the ancient greek , " sitos " for food , and " topos " for place .	所以 , 我提出了一個替代方案 , 就是 「 希托邦 」 , 來自古希臘的 「 sitos 」 , 以供食物 , 以及 「 topos 」 。
i believe we already live in sitopia .	我相信我們已經住在希托邦了 。
we live in a world shaped by food , and if we realize that , we can use food as a really powerful tool a conceptual tool , design tool , to shape the world differently .	我們生活在一個由食物形塑的世界 , 如果我們意識到 , 我們能用食物來當作強大的工具--一個概念性的工具 , 設計工具 , 用不同的方式塑造這個世界 。
so if we were to do that , what might sitopia look like ?	所以如果我們這樣做 , 希托邦會長什麼樣子 ?
well i think it looks a bit like this .	我覺得它看起來有點像這樣 。
i have to use this slide . it's just the look on the face of the dog .	我必須用這張投影片 , 只是在狗的臉上
but anyway , this is it's food at the center of life , at the center of family life , being celebrated , being enjoyed , people taking time for it .	但無論如何 , 這是生命中心的食物 , 在家庭生活的中心 , 被讚頌、被享受 , 人們花時間在此事上 。
this is where food should be in our society .	這才是我們社會中食物應有的地位
but you can't have scenes like this unless you have people like this .	但你不可能有這樣的場景 , 除非你有這樣的人 。
by the way , these can be men as well .	順道一提 , 這些也可以是男性
it's people who think about food , who think ahead , who plan , who can stare at a pile of raw vegetables and actually recognize them .	那些人會想到食物 , 他們會預先思考 , 計畫要先計畫好 , 能盯著一堆生菜 , 實際地認出它們 。
we need these people . we're part of a network .	我們需要這些人 。 我們是網路的一部分 。
because without these kinds of people we can't have places like this .	因為如果沒有這一類的人我們不可能有這樣的地方
here , i deliberately chose this because it is a man buying a vegetable .	在這裡 , 我故意選這個 , 因為這是男人在買菜 。
but networks , markets where food is being grown locally .	但網路 , 食物在當地生長的市場
it's common . it's fresh .	這很常見 , 很新鮮 。
it's part of the social life of the city .	是城市社交生活的一部分
because without that , you can't have this kind of place , food that is grown locally and also is part of the landscape , and is not just a zerosum commodity off in some unseen hellhole .	因為沒有了這些 , 你就無法擁有這樣的地方 , 本地生長的食物 , 同時也是景觀的一部分 , 不只是一個你看不到的地獄環境的零和商品 。
cows with a view .	牛的視野 。
steaming piles of humus .	成堆的humus 。
this is basically bringing the whole thing together .	這基本上是把整個東西結合在一起 。
and this is a community project i visited recently in toronto .	這是我最近去了一趟多倫多的社區計畫 。
it's a greenhouse , where kids get told all about food and growing their own food .	它是一間溫室 , 孩子們會被告知關於食物的一切 , 並自己種植食物 。
here is a plant called kevin , or maybe it's a plant belonging to a kid called kevin . i don't know .	這裡有一株叫做凱文的植物 , 或許這是一種植物屬於名叫凱文的孩子 , 我不知道 。
but anyway , these kinds of projects that are trying to reconnect us with nature is extremely important .	但無論如何 , 這類試圖將我們與大自然重新連結的計畫極其重要 。
so sitopia , for me , is really a way of seeing .	所以 , 希托邦 , 對我而言 , 其實是一種看待的方式 。
it's basically recognizing that sitopia already exists in little pockets everywhere .	基本上 , 我們已經意識到 , 希托邦已經存在於任何地方的小口袋裡了 。
the trick is to join them up , to use food as a way of seeing .	秘訣是要加入他們 , 用食物當作一種看不見的方式 。
and if we do that , we're going to stop seeing cities as big , metropolitan , unproductive blobs , like this .	如果我們這樣做 , 我們將不會再把城市看成是大型、都會區、沒有生產力的區塊 , 就像這樣 。
we're going to see them more like this , as part of the productive , organic framework of which they are inevitably a part , symbiotically connected .	我們會把它們看得更像這樣 , 一個有機的有機框架 , 一個不可避免地連結在一起的部分 。
but of course , that's not a great image either , because we need not to be producing food like this anymore .	當然 , 這也不是一個很棒的形象 , 因為我們不需要再這樣生産食物 。
we need to be thinking more about permaculture , which is why i think this image just sums up for me the kind of thinking we need to be doing .	我們需要多考量永續農業 , 這也是為什麼我認為這張圖只為我總結出我們需要做的事 。
it's a reconceptualization of the way food shapes our lives .	重新概念化的呈現食物如何塑造我們的生活
the best image i know of this is from 650 years ago .	我對此所知最好的形象是從650年前開始
it's ambrogio lorenzetti's " allegory of good government . "	安布洛吉歐.羅倫澤提的 " 良好政府的寓言 "
it's about the relationship between the city and the countryside .	和城市和鄉間的關係
and i think the message of this is very clear .	我認為這件事的訊息是非常清楚的 。
if the city looks after the country , the country will look after the city .	如果城市照顧這城市 , 國家會照顧這城市 。
and i want us to ask now , what would ambrogio lorenzetti paint if he painted this image today ?	我現在想問問安布洛吉歐.羅倫澤提如果他今天畫了這張圖會有什麼樣的顏料 ?
what would an allegory of good government look like today ?	對好政府的寓言會是怎樣的今日 ?
because i think it's an urgent question .	因為我認為這是一個很迫切的問題 。
it's one we have to ask , and we have to start answering .	這是我們得要問的 , 我們得要開始回答 。
we know we are what we eat .	我們知道我們吃的東西
we need to realize that the world is also what we eat .	我們需要意識到 , 我們所吃的世界 ,
but if we take that idea , we can use food as a really powerful tool to shape the world better .	但如果我們把這個想法 , 我們可以利用食物做為一個真正有力的工具 , 來改善世界 。
weeks from the charter for compassion launch , karen armstrong looks at religion's role in the 21st century: will its dogmas divide us ? or will it unite us for common good ? she reviews the catalysts that can drive the world's faiths to rediscover the golden rule .	在《慈悲出發的憲章》的數週後 , 凱倫•阿姆斯壯在二十一世紀中所扮演的角色:它會讓我們分裂嗎 ? 或者它會讓我們團結在一起 , 成為我們的共同點 ? 她會修改那些催化劑 , 來驅使世界的信仰 , 去重新發現黃金法則 。
god , ted prize , global issues , politics , religion , tedglobal2009 , violence	上帝 , ted大獎 , 全球議題 , 政治 , 宗教 , tedglobal2009 , 暴力事件
karen armstrong: let's revive the golden rule	karenarmstrong:讓我們重振黃金法則
for years i've been feeling frustrated , because as a religious historian , i've become acutely aware of the centrality of compassion in all the major world faiths .	多年來我一直感到沮喪 , 因為作為一個宗教歷史學家 , 我開始敏銳地意識到 , 同情心的核心 , 在所有主要世界的信仰中 。
every single one of them has evolved their own version of what's been called the golden rule .	每一條都進化出自己所謂的 「 黃金法則 」 。
sometimes it comes in a positive version " always treat all others as you'd like to be treated yourself . "	有時 , 會有正面的版本 「 全心全意、善待別人 」 。
and equally important is the negative version " don't do to others what you would not like them to do to you . "	同樣重要的是負面的版本 「 不要對他人做你不希望他們對你做的事 。 」
look into your own heart , discover what it is that gives you pain and then refuse , under any circumstance whatsoever , to inflict that pain on anybody else .	放眼自己的內心 , 發掘痛苦 , 然後在任何情況下拒絕 , 將那痛苦加諸在他人身上 。
and people have emphasized the importance of compassion , not just because it sounds good , but because it works .	人們強調憐憫的重要 , 不只是因為它很好聽 , 而是因為它很有效 。
people have found that when they have implemented the golden rule as confucius said , " all day and every day , " not just a question of doing your good deed for the day and then returning to a life of greed and egotism , but to do it all day and every day , you dethrone yourself from the center of your world , put another there , and you transcend yourself .	人們發現 , 當他們實施了黃金法則 , 如孔子說的: 「 一整天和每一天 。 」 這個問題不單是做好自己在做的好事接著又回到貪婪和自負的生活中 , 而是一整天都在執行 , 你把自己這個世界的中心給剝奪掉 , 把另一個變成在那裡 , 你就會超越自己 。
and it brings you into the presence of what's been called god , nirvana , rama , tao .	它會把你帶到一個名為 「 神 」 、 「 涅鼓 」 、 「 完人 」 的境界 。
something that goes beyond what we know in our egobound existence .	某種超越我們所知的自大的存在的東西 。
but you know you'd never know it a lot of the time , that this was so central to the religious life .	但你知道你從來都不知道 , 宗教生活的核心 。
because with a few wonderful exceptions , very often when religious people come together , religious leaders come together , they're arguing about abstruse doctrines or uttering a council of hatred or inveighing against homosexuality or something of that sort .	因為有少數美好的例外 , 當宗教人士聚在一起 , 宗教領袖聚在一起 , 他們爭論的主張是異教徒 , 或是引發一連串仇恨的議會或反對同性戀或同性戀等等 。
often people don't really want to be compassionate .	通常人們不太想要有同情心 。
i sometimes see when i'm speaking to a congregation of religious people a sort of mutinous expression crossing their faces because people often want to be right instead .	我有時會看到 , 當我在和一群宗教人物談話時 , 會出現一種互相表達的表情 , 會讓他們的臉交疊 , 因為人們通常會想要對的 。
and that of course defeats the object of the exercise .	這當然也違反了運動的本質 。
now why was i so grateful to ted ?	我為什麼感激ted ?
because they took me very gently from my booklined study and brought me into the 21st century , enabling me to speak to a much , much wider audience than i could have ever conceived .	因為他們輕輕的從我的書本研究帶我進入21世紀 , 讓我能夠和更寬廣的觀眾對話 , 遠超過我所能想像的 。
because i feel an urgency about this .	因為我對此感到緊急 ,
if we don't manage to implement the golden rule globally , so that we treat all peoples , wherever and whoever they may be , as though they were as important as ourselves , i doubt that we'll have a viable world to hand on to the next generation .	如果我們不想辦法在全球實行黃金法則 , 這樣我們對待所有人 , 無論在哪裡 , 無論他們是誰 , 無論他們是誰 , 無論在哪裡 , 都能像我們自己一樣重要的是 , 我懷疑我們會有一個可行的世界來傳遞給下一代 。
the task of our time , one of the great tasks of our time , is to build a global society , as i said , where people can live together in peace .	我們這個時代的任務 , 這個時代的偉大任務之一 , 就是建立一個全球化的社會 , 如我所說的 , 人們可以和平共處 。
and the religions that should be making a major contribution are instead seen as part of the problem .	而應該要做出重大貢獻的宗教卻被視為問題的一部分 。
and of course it's not just religious people who believe in the golden rule .	當然 , 也不只有虔誠的人也相信黃金法則
this is the source of all morality , this imaginative act of empathy , putting yourself in the place of another .	這是所有道德的源頭 , 這種富有想像力的同理心 , 讓你自己置身於另一個人之處 。
and so we have a choice , it seems to me .	所以我們有選擇 , 在我看來是這樣 。
we can either go on bringing out or emphasizing the dogmatic and intolerant aspects of our faith , or we can go back to the rabbis . rabbi hillel , the older contemporary of jesus , who , when asked by a pagan to sum up the whole of jewish teaching while he stood on one leg , said , " that which is hateful to you , do not do to your neighbor .	我們可以繼續 , 或者強調我們的信仰教條和不寬容的面向 , 或者我們可以回到拉比希爾的拉比希爾 , 即耶穌現代的拉比希爾 , 當他被一個異教徒叫他總結出猶太教義時 , 他說: 「 那對你來說很討厭 , 不對你的鄰居做 。
that is the torah and everything else is only commentary . "	「 這就是教義 , 其他都只是評論而已 。 」
and the rabbis and the early fathers of the church who said that any interpretation of scripture that bred hatred and disdain was illegitimate .	還有教會的拉比和早期的父親 , 他說任何對經文的解讀只要帶著憎恨和鄙視 , 都是違法的 。
and we need to revive that spirit .	而我們需要讓那個精神復甦 。
and it's not just going to happen because a spirit of love wafts us down .	這不只會發生因為愛的精神喚醒了我們
we have to make this happen , and we can do it with the modern communications that ted has introduced .	我們得讓這件事成真 , 我們也要用ted現代溝通來做到 。
already i've been tremendously heartened at the response of all our partners .	我已經非常的高興 , 能回應我們所有的夥伴 。
in singapore , we have a group going to use the charter to heal divisions recently that have sprung up in singaporean society , and some members of the parliament want to implement it politically .	在新加坡 , 我們有個團體要用憲章來治癒新加坡社會最近出現的分歧 , 議會的某些成員想要在政治上實施 。
in malaysia , there is going to be an art exhibition in which leading artists are going to be taking people , young people , and showing them that compassion also lies at the root of all art .	在馬來西亞 , 將有一場藝術展覽 , 主導藝術家將帶領人們 , 年輕人 , 並向他們展示 , 慈悲也是一切藝術的根源 。
throughout europe , the muslim communities are holding events and discussions , are discussing the centrality of compassion in islam and in all faiths .	在整個歐洲 , 穆斯林社群舉辦了許多活動和討論 , 正討論著同情心的核心 , 在伊斯蘭和所有信仰中 。
but it can't stop there . it can't stop with the launch .	但是它不能就此停止 。 它不能隨著發射升空 。
religious teaching , this is where we've gone so wrong , concentrating solely on believing abstruse doctrines .	宗教的教誨 , 是我們出了差錯的地方 , 僅僅只專注於相信深不可測的教義 。
religious teaching must always lead to action .	宗教的教導一定會導致行動
and i intend to work on this till my dying day .	而我打算在我快要死掉的日子裡工作 。
and i want to continue with our partners to do two things educate and stimulate compassionate thinking .	我想要繼續和我們的夥伴一起做兩件事 , 來教育和刺激同情心 。
education because we've so dropped out of compassion .	教育是因為我們已如此地退出同情心
people often think it simply means feeling sorry for somebody .	人們經常認為那只代表對其他人感到遺憾 。
but of course you don't understand compassion if you're just going to think about it .	但你當然不能理解同情心如果你只想著同情心
you also have to do it .	你也必須去做 。
i want them to get the media involved because the media are crucial in helping to dissolve some of the stereotypical views we have of other people , which are dividing us from one another .	我希望媒體能參與其中 , 因為媒體很重要 , 協助我們破除其他人對某些刻板印象的看法 , 使我們彼此分裂 。
the same applies to educators .	同樣的適用於教育工作者
i'd like youth to get a sense of the dynamism , the dynamic and challenge of a compassionate lifestyle .	我希望青年能夠感受到一種有同情心的生活方式的活力和挑戰 。
and also see that it demands acute intelligence , not just a gooey feeling .	同時也看到這需要敏銳的情報 , 而不是僅僅只是一種呆滯的感覺 。
i'd like to call upon scholars to explore the compassionate theme in their own and in other people's traditions .	我想要大聲呼籲學者 , 去探索他們自己和其他人傳統中的同情心主題 。
and perhaps above all , to encourage a sensitivity about uncompassionate speaking , so that because people have this charter , whatever their beliefs or lack of them , they feel empowered to challenge uncompassionate speech , disdainful remarks from their religious leaders , their political leaders , from the captains of industry .	最重要的可能是 , 鼓勵對於沒有同情心的言論的敏感度 , 這麼一來 , 因為有這種憲章 , 不論他們的信仰為何 , 或缺乏他們覺得有能力挑戰不夠同情心的言論 , 不留情的評論來自於他們的宗教領袖、政治領袖 , 來自產業界的船長 。
because we can change the world , we have the ability .	因為我們可以改變世界 , 我們有能力
i would never have thought of putting the charter online .	我從來不會想到要把憲章放在網路上 。
i was still stuck in the old world of a whole bunch of boffins sitting together in a room and issuing yet another arcane statement .	我還困在舊世界中 , 一大群人坐在一間房間中 , 同時又發表了另一種神奇的聲明 。
and ted introduced me to a whole new way of thinking and presenting ideas .	而ted向我介紹一個全新的思考方式 , 並且向我展示想法 。
because that is what is so wonderful about ted .	因為那是ted美妙的地方 。
in this room , all this expertise , if we joined it all together , we could change the world .	在這個房間裡 , 所有的專長 , 如果我們聯合起來 , 我們就可以改變世界 。
and of course the problems sometimes seem insuperable .	當然有時候這些問題看似無法解決 。
but i'd just like to quote , finish at the end with a reference to a british author , an oxford author whom i don't quote very often , c . s . lewis .	但我只想引用最後一位英國作家一句牛津的作者的話 。 我不太常引用她的話 , c.s.路易斯 。
but he wrote one thing that stuck in my mind ever since i read it when i was a schoolgirl .	但他寫了一篇我腦海中一直停留在想的事情 , 從我讀到學校的時候 。
it's in his book " the four loves . "	在他的書《四人道》中
he said that he distinguished between erotic love , when two people gaze , spellbound , into each other's eyes .	他說他區分出愛欲的愛情 , 當兩個人凝視著 , 為對方的眼神拼貼 。
and then he compared that to friendship , when two people stand side by side , as it were , shoulder to shoulder , with their eyes fixed on a common goal .	接著 , 他將這段感情與友情比較 , 當兩個人站在一起 , 和他們肩並肩 , 用他們的眼神固定在一個共同目標上 。
we don't have to fall in love with each other , but we can become friends .	我們不需要相互墜入愛河 , 但我們可以變成朋友 。
and i am convinced .	我深信不疑 。
i felt it very strongly during our little deliberations at vevey , that when people of all different persuasions come together , working side by side for a common goal , differences melt away .	我強烈的感覺到它 , 在我們被威脅的小小的故意點中 , 當所有不同說服的人聚在一起 , 肩並肩地工作 , 為了共同的目標 , 差異會漸消融 。
and we learn amity .	而且我們學會了仁愛 。
and we learn to live together and to get to know one another .	我們學著一起生活 , 去認識彼此 。
thank you very much .	非常感謝 。
david macaulay relives the winding and sometimes surreal journey toward the completion of rome antics , his illustrated homage to the historic city .	大衛馬卡拉依靠著勝利 , 有時是超現實的旅程 , 朝著羅馬示威前進 , 他對歷史城市致敬 。
macarthur grant , art , arts , book , cities , communication , culture , design , entertainment , humor , storytelling	麥克阿瑟•格蘭特 , 藝術、藝術、書籍、城市、溝通、文化、設計、娛樂、幽默、說故事 。
i draw to better understand things .	我畫畫 , 是為了更好地理解事物
sometimes i make a lot of drawings and i still don't understand what it is i'm drawing .	有時候我畫了很多卻還是不明白我在畫什麼
those of you who are comfortable with digital stuff and even smug about that relationship might be amused to know that the guy who is best known for " the way things work , " while preparing for part of a panel for called understanding , spent two days trying to get his laptop to communicate with his new cd burner .	那些對數位資訊感到舒服的人 , 甚至對那種關係感到羞恥 , 知道 「 事情運作的方式 」 最為人所知的那個人 , 同時準備了一部分的 「 理解 」 , 花了兩天的時間 , 試圖讓他的筆電和他的新cd燒錄器溝通 。

i've always managed my own extensions so it never even occurred to me to read the instructions , but i did finally figure it out . i had to figure it out , because along with the invitation came the frightening reminder that there would be no projector , so bringing those carousels would no longer be necessary but some alternate form of communication would .	我一直都在管理自己的延伸 , 所以我從來沒有想過要看說明書 , 但我終於弄清楚了 。 我必須弄清楚 , 因為隨著邀請 , 提醒自己不會有投影器 , 所以帶來這些焦糖就不會再有必要了 , 只是一些其他的溝通形式 。
now , i could talk about something that i'm known for , something that would be particularly appropriate for many of the more technically minded people here , or i could talk about something i really care about .	現在 , 我可以談談我所知道的一些事情 , 一些對於在座有更多嚴格想法的人 , 或者我可以談談我真正關心的事 。

well , i went to rhode island school of design in the second half of the '60s to study architecture .	嗯 , 我在羅德島設計學院念建築時大約是六零年代後期
i was lucky enough to spend my last year , my fifth year , in rome as a student . it changed my life .	我很幸運 , 能在我當學生的最後一年、第五年去羅馬度過 。 這改變了我的一生 。
not the least reason was the fact that i had spent those first four years living at home , driving into risd everyday , driving back .	不是因為前四年我都住在家裡 , 每天開車到rsid家裡 , 開回家 。
i missed the '60s . i read about them ; i understand they were pretty interesting . i missed them , but i did spend that extraordinary year in rome , and it's a place that is never far from my mind .	我錯過了六十年代 。 我讀到這些故事 , 我了解它們非常有趣 。 我錯過了它們 , 但是我在羅馬渡過了很不平凡的一年 , 這地方從不遠離我的想法 。
so , whenever given an opportunity , i try to do something in it or with it or for it .	所以 , 只要有機會 , 我就會試著去做些什麼 , 不論是用在它身上或它身上 。

all different materials , all different styles , all different times , drawings from sketchbooks looking at the details of rome .	所有不同的材質 , 風格 , 每次都不同 , 從sketchbook上畫畫看看羅馬的細節 。
part of the reason i'm showing you these is that it sort of helps illustrate this process i go through of trying to figure out what it is i feel about rome and why i feel it .	我給你們看這些 , 有一部分的原因是 , 它幫助我清楚闡述這個過程 , 我試圖找出我對羅馬的感覺 , 以及為什麼我會有這種感受 。

a book is not only a neat way of collecting and storing information , it's a series of layers .	書不只一種整齊的收集和儲存資訊的方式 , 也包含了一系列的層次 。

but think of them as layers . i mean , rome is a place of layers horizontal layers , vertical layers and i thought , well just peeling off a page would allow me to if i got you thinking about it the right way would allow me to sort of show you the depth of layers .	但把它們想像成層次 。 我的意思是 , 羅馬是個有層次的橫向地層 , 垂直地層 , 而我想 , 如果我讓你可以用正確的方式來思考這個問題 , 可以讓我向你們展示一些層次的深度 。
the stucco on the walls of most of the buildings in rome covers the scars ; the scars of centuries of change as these structures have been adapted rather than being torn down .	羅馬的大多數建築物的牆面上印著許多個世紀前的傷痕這些結構已經被改造而不是被拆掉
if i do a foldout page on the lefthand side and let you just unfold it , you see behind it what i mean by scar tissue .	如果我在左手邊做一個摺疊頁然後讓你解開它 , 你就會看到我所說的傷疤組織 。
you can see that in 1635 , it became essential to make smaller windows because the bad guys were coming or whatever .	你可以看到在1635年 , 要做出更小的窗戶是不可或缺的 , 因為壞人要來了或者是其他東西 。
adaptations all get buried under the stucco .	各種適應作用都埋在粘核下
i could peel out a page of this palazzo to show you what's going on inside of it .	我可以從這張山羊皮紙上撕出一頁給大家看 , 讓大家看看裡面的狀況 。
but more importantly , i could also show you what it looks like at the corner of one of those magnificent buildings with all the massive stone blocks , or the fake stone blocks done with brick and stucco , which is more often the case .	更重要的是 , 我還可以向你們展示在這些壯麗的建築物的角落裡 , 有著巨大的石塊 , 或用磚頭和加工的假石塊所做的假石塊 , 這些石塊比較常見 。
so it becomes slightly threedimensional .	因此 , 稍微變成立體了 。
i could take you down one of those narrow little streets into one of those surprising piazzas by using a double gate fold double foldout page which , if you were like me reading a popup book as a child , you hopefully stick your head into .	我可以把你從一條狹窄的小街上帶到一條令人驚訝的廣場 , 只要用一個雙面大門式的摺疊頁--如果你跟我小時候一樣--讀本雙層的書 , 你就可以把你的頭伸進去 。
you wrap the pages around your head and are in that piazza for that brief period of time .	把頭裹住的頁面 , 就在那短暫的時間內 ,
and i've really not done anything much more complicated than make foldout pages .	我沒有做任何更複雜的事情 , 比做摺疊頁更複雜 。

and if i turn the book the other way , we're looking across the square at the front of the pantheon .	如果我把書換個角度來看 , 我們就在廣場的正面看著 。
no foldouts , no tricks just a book that isn't open the whole way .	沒有摺疊 , 沒有把戲--只是本不會打開的書 。

so we get inside the pantheon and it grows and so on and so forth .	我們進入萬神殿內部 , 它生長著 , 諸如此類 。
and i thought , maybe i'm on the right track , but it sort of lost its human quality .	我心想 , 也許我是正走在正確的軌道上 , 但它好像失去了人類的特質 。
so i went back to the notion of story , which is always a good thing to have if you're trying to get people to pay attention to a book and pick up information along the way .	所以我回到故事的觀點 , 如果你要讓人們注意一本書 , 一路上拿起資訊 , 那一定是件好事 。
" pigeon's progress " struck me as a catchy title .	「 鴿子的進展 」 讓我印象深刻 。
if it was a homing pigeon , it would be called " homer's odyssey . "	如果牠是位愛的鴿子 , 牠就會被稱為 「 荷馬的奧德賽 」 。
but it was the journey of the . . .	但那卻是那趟旅程......
i mean , if a title works , use it . but it would be a journey that went through rome and showed all the things that i like about rome .	我是說 , 如果一個頭銜能用它 。 但它會是一趟旅程 , 穿越羅馬 , 展示所有我喜歡的羅馬 。
it's a pigeon sitting on top of a church .	是一隻鴿子坐在教堂的上方
goes off during the day and does normal pigeon stuff . comes back , the whole place is covered with scaffolding and green netting and there's no way this pigeon can get home .	白天出去做一些正常的鴿子 。 回來了 , 整個地方都被鷹架和綠色防護網包覆著 , 完全沒有辦法讓這隻鴿子回家 。
so it's a homeless pigeon now and it's going to have to find another place to live , and that allows me to go through my catalog of favorite things , and we start with the tall ones and so on .	所以現在是一隻流浪鴿 , 而且牠還得找另一個地方住 , 這讓我可以從我喜歡的東西的目錄中找到 , 我們從高大的鴿子開始 。
maybe it has to go back and live with family members ; that's not always a good thing , but it does sort of bring pigeons together again .	也許牠必須回去和家人同住 ; 這並不總是件好事 , 但牠的確會帶著鴿子在一起 。
and i thought , that's sort of interesting , but maybe there's a person who should be involved in this in some way .	我心想 , 這有點有趣 , 但或許有一個人應該要以某種方式來參與這個活動 。
so i kind of came up with this old guy who spends his life looking after sick pigeons .	所以我想出了這個老傢伙 , 終其一生都在照顧生病的鴿子 。
he'll go anywhere to get them dangerous places and whatnot and they become really friends with this guy , and learn to do tricks for him and entertain him at lunchtime and stuff like that .	他會去任何地方 , 去讓他們危險的地方 , 不論是什麼 , 他們都會和他成為朋友 , 學著為他做把戲 , 到午餐時間玩笑 , 諸如此類 。
there's a real bond that develops between this old man and these pigeons .	有一個真實的鍵結在這個老人和這些鴿子之間發展出來
but unfortunately he gets sick . he gets really sick at the end of the story .	但不幸的是 , 他病得很重 。 他病的很重 。
he's taught them to spell his name , which is aldo .	他教他們拼他的名字 , 艾爾多 。
they show up one day after three or four days of not seeing him he lives in this little garret and they spell his name and fly around .	有一天 , 在三四天沒見到他之後 , 他住在這個小垃圾桶裡 , 他們拼他的名字 , 飛來飛去 。
and he finally gets enough strength together to climb up the ladder onto the roof , and all the pigeons , a la red balloon , are there waiting for him and they carry him off over the walls of the city .	他終於得到了足夠的力量 , 可以爬上梯子 , 爬到屋頂上 , 所有的鴿子 , 一只洛杉磯紅氣球 , 都在那等著他 , 然後他們把他帶到城市的牆上 。
and i forgot to mention this: whenever he lost a pigeon , he would take that pigeon out beyond the walls of the city .	我忘了提到這個:每當他失去了一隻鴿子的時候 , 他就會把那隻鴿子帶到城墻外面 。
in the old roman custom , the dead were never buried within the walls .	在舊羅馬的習俗中 , 死者從來沒有埋在牆裡 。
and i thought that's a really cheery story .	我覺得這真是一個令人高興的故事 。
. that's really going to go a long way .	這真的要走很長的路 。
so anyway , i went through . . . and again , if packaging doesn't work and if the stories aren't going anywhere , i just come up with titles and hope that a title will sort of kick me off in the right direction .	所以 , 總之 , 我經歷了...如果包裝沒有用 , 如果故事沒用 , 我只要想出標題 , 希望書名就會把我往正確的方向踢掉 。
and sometimes it does focus me enough and i'll even do a title page .	有時它的確讓我很專注 , 我甚至會畫一個標題頁 。
so , these are all title pages that eventually led me to the solution i settled on , which is the story of a young woman who sends a message on a homing pigeon she lives outside the walls of the city of rome to someone in the city .	所以 , 這些全都是書名 , 最終讓我找到了我安定的解決方案 , 這個故事是一位年輕女子傳達一個信息 , 她住在羅馬城外 , 和城市中的人 。
and the pigeon is flying down above the appian way here .	這隻鴿子飛到阿匹手的上方
you can see the tombs and pines and so on and so forth along the way .	你可以看到這些墓和松果在過程中等等 。
if you see the red line , you are seeing the trail of the pigeon ; if you don't see the red line , you are the pigeon .	如果你看見這條紅線 , 你就看見了鴿子的軌跡 ; 如果你看不到紅線 , 你就是那隻鴿子 。
and it becomes necessary and possible , at this point , to try to convey what that sense would be like of flying over the city without actually moving .	在這個時點 , 它是必要的且可能的 , 試著傳達那種飛越城市的感覺 , 卻沒有實際移動 。
past the pyramid of cestius these will seem very familiar to you , even if you haven't been to rome recently past the gatehouse .	過了賽斯提烏斯金字塔 , 你應該很熟悉 , 即使你最近沒去過羅馬 。
this is something that's a little bit unusual .	這個東西有一點不尋常 。
this pigeon does something that most homing pigeons do not do: it takes the scenic route , which was a device that i felt was necessary to actually extend this book beyond about four pages .	這隻鴿子做了一件很不可思議的事:它採取了一條景色路線 , 那個我覺得有必要的裝置 , 能夠將這本書延長到四頁之外 。
so , we circle around the coliseum , past the church of santa maria in cosmedin and the temple of hercules towards the river .	所以 , 我們在羅馬競技場周圍繞著 , 穿過在宇宙中的聖母堂 , 以及海克力士直達河的神廟 。
we almost collide with the cornice of the palazzo farnese designed by michelangelo , built of stone taken from the coliseum narrow escape .	差點撞上法尼西羅河公園的天地 , 由米開朗基羅設計的石頭建構 , 從羅馬競技場上逃脫 。
we swoop down over the campo de' fiori .	我們俯瞰鮮花廣場
this is one of those things i show to my students because it's a complete bastardization a denial of any rules of perspective .	這是我給我學生看的其中一樣東西 , 因為這完全是違背了所有觀點的規則 。
the only rule of perspective that i think matters is if it looks believable , you've succeeded .	我覺得唯一重要的觀點規則是只要看起來可信 , 你就成功了 。
but you try and figure out where the vanishing points meet here ; a couple are on mars and a couple of others in cremona .	但你要試著找出消失的地點在哪裡 ; 一對夫妻在克雷莫那州和其他幾個 。
but into the piazza in front of santa maria della pace , where invariably a soccer game is going on , and we're hit by a soccer ball .	但在聖母堂前面的廣場上 , 那裡無可避免地一場足球賽正要上演 , 我們被足球撞擊了 。
now this is a terrible illustration of being hit by a soccer ball .	這張圖說明了被足球擊中的情形很糟 。
i have all the pieces: there's santa maria della pace , there's a soccer ball , there's a little bit of a bird's wing nothing's happening , so i had to rethink it .	我有所有的片斷:這裡有聖母堂 , 足球 , 還有一點點 , 鳥的翅膀什麼都沒發生 , 所以我得重新思考 。
and if you do want to see santa maria della pace , these books are really flexible , incredibly interactive just turn it around and look at it the other way .	如果你真的想看清楚聖母堂 , 這些書很有彈性 , 非常有互動性 , 只要把它翻過來 , 就會用另一種方式來看 。
through the alley , we can see the impact is captured in the red line .	穿過巷子 , 我們可以看到影響被記錄在紅線中 。
and then bird manages to pull itself together past this medieval tower one of the few remaining medieval towers towards the church of sant'agnese and around the dome looking down into piazza navona which we've already mentioned and seen and flown over a couple of times ; there's the bernini statue of the four rivers and then past the wonderful borromini sant'ivo , stopping just long enough on the 26foot diameter oculus of the pantheon to catch our breath .	接著 , 鳥會在中世紀的塔樓上拉合 , 這是少數剩下的中世紀塔樓之一 , 朝聖之教前進 , 在圓頂上 , 向下看向廣場納瓦納瓦納 , 我們已經看過並飛過數次 ; 這裡有四條河流的柏尼雕像 , 接著超越了美麗的博羅米諾山家園 , 在26英尺高的西洋山脈上 , 停下夠久 , 停下了 。
and then we can swoop inside and around ; and because we're flying , we don't really have to worry about gravity at this particular moment in time , so this drawing can be oriented in any way on the page .	接著 , 我們可以在裡頭盤旋 , 因為我們是在飛 , 在這個特定的時刻 , 我們不用擔心重力 , 所以這幅圖可以用任何方式呈現在紙上 。
we get a little exuberant as we pass gesu ; it's not surprising to sort of mimic the architecture in this way .	當我們通過gesu , 我們會變得更加精彩 。 一點也不意外地模仿這個建築物 。
past the wonderful wall filled with the juxtaposition that i was talking about ; beautiful carvings set into the walls above the neon " ristorante " sign , and so on .	再過來這面牆內佈滿了我剛才提到的對比牆面的美麗雕刻 , 出現在尼龍之上 " ristorante " 的牆上 , 諸如此類的 。
and eventually , we arrive at the courtyard of the palazzo , which is our destination .	最後我們來到了palazzo的庭院 , 也就是我們的目的地 。
straight up through the courtyard into a little window into the attic , where somebody is working at the drawing board .	穿過庭院 , 進入閣樓的小窗口 , 有人在畫板上工作 。
he removes the message from the leg of the bird ; this is what it says .	他從這隻鳥的腿上摘下了這個訊息 , 它是這樣說的 。
as we look at the drawing board , we see what he's working on is , in fact , a map of the journey that the pigeon has just taken , and the red line extends through all the sights .	當我們看畫板時 , 我們看到他正在寫的東西 , 事實上 , 是一張鴿子剛走過的旅程地圖 , 紅線延伸到所有的視野 。
and if you want the information , so that we complete this cycle of understanding , all you have to do is read these paragraphs .	如果你想要資訊 , 我們就完成理解的循環 , 你只需要讀讀這些段落 。
thank you very much .	非常感謝 。
mit researcher skylar tibbits works on selfassembly the idea that instead of building something , we can create materials that build themselves , much the way a strand of dna zips itself together . it's a big concept at early stages ; tibbits shows us three inthelab projects that hint at what a selfassembling future might look like .	麻省理工學院的天鵝在進行自我組合這個想法與其建立某樣東西 , 我們可以創造一些材料 , 許多將自己製造出來的材料 。 大多是dna鏈在初期階段的概念 ; tibbits向我們展示了三個刺激項目 , 暗示著自我組裝未來可能的樣子 。
skylar tibbits: can we make things that make themselves ?	摩天大提琴:我們能否做出讓自己做出來的東西 ?
today i'd like to show you the future of the way we make things .	今天我想向你們展示我們製造東西的方式的未來 。
i believe that soon our buildings and machines will be selfassembling , replicating and repairing themselves .	我相信 , 很快的 , 我們的建築物和機器將會自我組合、複製和修復自己 。
so i'm going to show you what i believe is the current state of manufacturing , and then compare that to some natural systems .	所以我要給你們看我相信的是當前的製造業狀態 , 然後跟一些自然系統比較 。
so in the current state of manufacturing , we have skyscrapers two and a half years [of assembly time] , 500 , 000 to a million parts , fairly complex , new , exciting technologies in steel , concrete , glass .	所以在當前的製造業狀態 , 我們有摩天大樓--兩年半的時間 , 50萬至一百萬個部分組成 , 相當複雜 , 令人振奮的新技術在鋼鐵 , 水泥 , 玻璃 。
we have exciting machines that can take us into space five years [of assembly time] , 2 . 5 million parts .	我們有令人興奮的機器可以帶我們進到太空五年後 , 250萬個部分 。
but on the other side , if you look at the natural systems , we have proteins that have two million types , can fold in 10 , 000 nanoseconds , or dna with three billion base pairs we can replicate in roughly an hour .	但在另一邊 , 如果你看一下自然系統 , 我們有兩百萬類型的蛋白質 , 可以在一萬納秒折疊 , 或dna有三十億個鹼基對 , 我們可以在大約一小時複製 。
so there's all of this complexity in our natural systems , but they're extremely efficient , far more efficient than anything we can build , far more complex than anything we can build .	所以 , 我們的自然系統有這麼多的複雜性 , 但它們非常有效率 , 遠遠超過任何我們可以建立的東西 , 遠遠超過任何我們可以建造的複雜性 。
they're far more efficient in terms of energy .	他們在能源方面的效率遠高於
they hardly ever make mistakes .	它們幾乎不會犯錯 。
and they can repair themselves for longevity .	而且他們可以長壽的修復
so there's something super interesting about natural systems .	所以自然界的系統有些超級有趣 。
and if we can translate that into our built environment , then there's some exciting potential for the way that we build things .	如果我們能將它翻譯到我們的建築環境中 , 那麼將會有一些令人振奮的潛力來建造東西 。
and i think the key to that is selfassembly .	我認為關鍵是自我組裝 。
so if we want to utilize selfassembly in our physical environment , i think there's four key factors .	所以 , 如果我們想要在我們的物理環境中使用自組裝 , 我認為有四個關鍵因素 。
the first is that we need to decode all of the complexity of what we want to build so our buildings and machines .	第一 , 我們需要解碼我們所要建設的一切複雜性 , 所以我們的建築物和機器 。
and we need to decode that into simple sequences basically the dna of how our buildings work .	我們需要解碼成簡單的序列--基本上就是我們建築物如何運作的dna 。
then we need programmable parts that can take that sequence and use that to fold up , or reconfigure .	接著 , 我們需要可編程的部分 , 可以用該序列來摺疊 , 或重新配置 。
we need some energy that's going to allow that to activate , allow our parts to be able to fold up from the program .	我們需要一些能讓它啟動的能量 , 讓我們的部分能夠折疊程式 。
and we need some type of error correction redundancy to guarantee that we have successfully built what we want .	我們需要某種類型的修正冗餘 , 來保證我們已經成功地建立我們所想要的 。
so i'm going to show you a number of projects that my colleagues and i at mit are working on to achieve this selfassembling future .	所以我要給你們看一些項目 , 是我和我在麻省理工學院的同事們正在努力實現這個自我組裝的未來 。
the first two are the macrobot and decibot .	前兩個是macrobot和decibot 。
so these projects are largescale reconfigurable robots 8 ft . , 12 ft . long proteins .	所以這些項目都是大規模的可重構機器人--8英尺 , 12英尺長的蛋白質 。
they're embedded with mechanical electrical devices , sensors .	它們嵌入機械式的電子設備 , 傳感器
you decode what you want to fold up into , into a sequence of angles so negative 120 , negative 120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , negative 120 something like that ; so a sequence of angles , or turns , and you send that sequence through the string .	你要解讀什麼便折疊成什麼 , 成序列的角度--負120 , 負120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , 120 , 負120--類似的東西 , 一連串的角度 , 或輪流順序 , 你便發送那個序列 。
each unit takes its message so negative 120 it rotates to that , checks if it got there and then passes it to its neighbor .	每個單位都需要它的消息--負120 , 它會旋轉 , 檢查它是否到了那裡 , 然後把它傳遞給它的鄰居 。
so these are the brilliant scientists , engineers , designers that worked on this project .	所以這些傑出的科學家、工程師、設計師在這個項目上工作 。
and i think it really brings to light: is this really scalable ?	我認為這真的會帶來光明:這真的可擴展嗎 ?
i mean , thousands of dollars , lots of man hours made to make this eightfoot robot .	我的意思是 , 數千美元 , 數千個男人花費了大量的時間來製造這八呎高的機器人 。
can we really scale this up ? can we really embed robotics into every part ?	我們可以把規模再擴大嗎 ? 我們真的可以把機器人嵌入每一個部分嗎 ?
the next one questions that and looks at passive nature , or passively trying to have reconfiguration programmability .	下一個問題 , 並著眼於被動的天性 , 或被動地試圖重新配置可編程 。
but it goes a step further , and it tries to have actual computation .	但它更進一步 , 它嘗試以實際的計算 。
it basically embeds the most fundamental building block of computing , the digital logic gate , directly into your parts .	它基本上嵌入了最基本的運算基礎 , 即數位邏輯閘 , 直接嵌入到你的零件 。
so this is a nand gate .	所以這是nandgate 。
you have one tetrahedron which is the gate that's going to do your computing , and you have two input tetrahedrons .	你有一個正四面體 , 它是門 , 會做你的計算 , 你有兩個輸入的正四面體 。
one of them is the input from the user , as you're building your bricks .	其中一個是來自使用者的輸入 , 當你在建構你的磚塊時 ,
the other one is from the previous brick that was placed .	另一塊是從以前放置的磚 。
and then it gives you an output in 3d space .	然後它在3d空間給你輸出
so what this means is that the user can start plugging in what they want the bricks to do .	所以這意味著 , 使用者可以開始把積木塞在他們想要的積木上 。
it computes on what it was doing before and what you said you wanted it to do .	它會計算它之前的狀況 , 和你說你想要它做的事 。
and now it starts moving in threedimensional space so up or down .	現在它開始在三維空間裡移動--向上或向下 。
so on the lefthand side , [1 , 1] input equals 0 output , which goes down .	所以在左手邊 , [1 , 1]輸入1等於輸出0 , 它便向下 。
on the righthand side , [0 , 0] input is a 1 output , which goes up .	在右手邊 , [0 , 0]輸入1輸出 , 它便上升 。
and so what that really means is that our structures now contain the blueprints of what we want to build .	這意味著我們的結構現在包含著我們所要建構的藍圖 。
so they have all of the information embedded in them of what was constructed .	所以他們有了所有建構出來的資訊 。
so that means that we can have some form of selfreplication .	那就表示 , 我們可以有某種形式的自我複製 。
in this case i call it selfguided replication , because your structure contains the exact blueprints .	在這個例子中 , 我稱之為自我導向的複製 , 因為你的結構包含了確切的藍圖 。
if you have errors , you can replace a part .	如果你有錯誤 , 你可以更換零件 。
all the local information is embedded to tell you how to fix it .	所有局部嵌入的信息會告訴你如何解決它 。
so you could have something that climbs along and reads it and can output at one to one .	所以你可以擁有攀登的東西將它讀取 , 然後在一對一輸出 。
it's directly embedded ; there's no external instructions .	它是直接嵌入 ; 沒有外部的指令 。
so the last project i'll show is called biased chains , and it's probably the most exciting example that we have right now of passive selfassembly systems .	我將展示的最後一個項目被稱為偏置鏈 , 它可能是我們現在被動自組裝系統最令人興奮的例子 。
so it takes the reconfigurability and programmability and makes it a completely passive system .	所以它採取可重構性和可編程性 , 使其成為完全被動的系統 。
so basically you have a chain of elements .	所以基本上你有一連串元素 。
each element is completely identical , and they're biased .	每個元素是完全相同的 , 而且它們偏頗 。
so each chain , or each element , wants to turn right or left .	所以每條連鎖鏈 , 或每一項元素 , 都想要向右或向左轉 。
so as you assemble the chain , you're basically programming it .	所以當你組裝鏈 , 你基本上是在為它編寫程式 。
you're telling each unit if it should turn right or left .	你告訴每個單位是否應該向右或向左轉 。
so when you shake the chain , it then folds up into any configuration that you've programmed in so in this case , a spiral , or in this case , two cubes next to each other .	所以當你搖晃鏈 , 它便折疊成任何你編程的配置--在這個例子中 , 一個螺旋 , 或在這個例子中 , 是兩個彼此相鄰的立方體 。
so you can basically program any threedimensional shape or onedimensional , twodimensional up into this chain completely passively .	所以基本上你可以編寫任何立體的形狀--或單面的 , 二維--完全被動地進入這條鏈 。
so what does this tell us about the future ?	所以 , 這告訴我們什麼關於未來的訊息 ?
i think that it's telling us that there's new possibilities for selfassembly , replication , repair in our physical structures , our buildings , machines .	我認為 , 它告訴我們 , 自我組裝、複製、修復的新可能性 , 存在於我們的物理結構、建築、機器當中 。
there's new programmability in these parts .	這些部分有新的可編程性 。
and from that you have new possibilities for computing .	從而計算出新的可能性 。
we'll have spatial computing .	我們將會有空間的計算 。
imagine if our buildings , our bridges , machines , all of our bricks could actually compute .	想像一下 , 如果我們的建築物 , 橋樑 , 機器 , 我們所有的磚其實可以計算 。
that's amazing parallel and distributed computing power , new design possibilities .	那是驚人的並行和分散運算能力 , 新的設計可能性 。
so it's exciting potential for this .	因此 , 它是令人興奮的潛力 。
so i think these projects i've showed here are just a tiny step towards this future , if we implement these new technologies for a new selfassembling world .	所以 , 我認為我在這裡展示的這些計畫 , 只是對這個未來的一小步 , 如果我們實現這些新技術 , 為一個新的自組裝世界 。
we've been to the moon , we've mapped the continents , we've even been to the deepest point in the ocean twice . what's left for the next generation to explore ? biologist and explorer nathan wolfe suggests this answer: almost everything . and we can start , he says , with the world of the unseeably small .	我們曾去過月球 , 我們已繪製了大陸地圖 , 甚至去過海洋最深的一點 。 下一代還有什麼需要探索 ? 生物學家和探險家nathanwolfe所提出的答案:幾乎所有的一切 。 他可以開始了 , 他說: 「 以不可思議的小世界 」 。
biodiversity , exploration , microbiology , science	生物多樣性、探索性、微生物學、科學
nathan wolfe: what's left to explore ?	內森.沃爾夫:還有什麼需要探索 ?
recently i visited beloit , wisconsin .	最近我去了威斯康辛州的貝洛伊特市 。
and i was there to honor a great 20th century explorer , roy chapman andrews .	我在那裡向一位偉大的20世紀探險家roychapmanandrews
during his time at the american museum of natural history , andrews led a range of expeditions to uncharted regions , like here in the gobi desert .	他在美國自然歷史博物館的時期 , andrews率領一系列到未標明地區的探險活動 , 像是這裏的戈壁沙漠 。
he was quite a figure .	他是個很像的人物 。
he was later , it's said , the basis of the indiana jones character .	據說他後來成為印第安那瓊斯這個角色的基礎 。
and when i was in beloit , wisconsin , i gave a public lecture to a group of middle school students .	當我在威斯康辛州的貝洛伊特市時 , 我對一群中學學生發表公眾演說 。
and i'm here to tell you , if there's anything more intimidating than talking here at ted , it'll be trying to hold the attention of a group of a thousand 12yearolds for a 45minute lecture .	我在這裡告訴大家 , 如果有任何事情比在ted這裡演講還要嚇人 , 那就是試著要在45分鐘的演講內掌握1000個12歲孩童的注意力 。
at the end of the lecture they asked a number of questions , but there was one that's really stuck with me since then .	講座結束後 , 他們問了幾個問題 , 但有一個自此之後深深印我腦海中 。
there was a young girl who stood up , and she asked the question: " where should we explore ? "	有一個年輕女孩站起來 , 她問了這個問題: 「 我們應該去哪裡探索 ? 」
i think there's a sense that many of us have that the great age of exploration on earth is over , that for the next generation they're going to have to go to outer space or the deepest oceans in order to find something significant to explore .	我認為我們當中許多人已經擁有很棒的探索時代已經結束了 , 對下一代來說 , 他們將不得不前往外太空或最深的海洋 , 去尋找一些重要的值得探險的東西 。
but is that really the case ?	但真的是這樣嗎 ?
is there really nowhere significant for us to explore left here on earth ?	地球上真的沒有我們能探索的重大元兇嗎 ?
it sort of made me think back to one of my favorite explorers in the history of biology .	這有點讓我回想起生物學史上我最喜歡的探險家之一 。
this is an explorer of the unseen world , martinus beijerinck .	這是未被看見的世界的探險家 , martinusbeijerinck 。
so beijerinck set out to discover the cause of tobacco mosaic disease .	beijerinck一開始要找出菸草鑲嵌病的原因 。
what he did is he took the infected juice from tobacco plants and he would filter it through smaller and smaller filters .	他做的事是取出菸草植物的受感染汁液 , 經過越來越小的過濾 。
and he reached the point where he felt that there must be something out there that was smaller than the smallest forms of life that were ever known bacteria , at the time .	到達那個程度 , 他覺得一定有什麼比當時所知的最小型態的生命形式還要更微小 。
he came up with a name for his mystery agent .	他為他的神秘代理想了個名字 。
he called it the virus latin for " poison . "	他把病毒稱為 「 毒藥的拉丁文 」 。
