i just want to say that we are applying this to many world problems: changing the dropout rates of school kids , combating addictions , enhancing teen health , curing vets' ptsd with time metaphors getting miracle cures promoting sustainability and conservation , reducing physical rehabilitation where there is a 50percent drop out rate , altering appeals to suicidal terrorists , and modifying family conflicts as timezone clashes .	我只想說 , 我們正在把這方法應用在許多世界問題上:改變學校學童的輟學率 , 打擊毒癮 , 增強青少年健康 , 用時間隱喻法治療退伍軍人的創傷 , 來促進可持續性和保育 , 減少身體康復的頻率 , 降低50%的比率 , 改變吸引自殺式恐怖分子的發生 , 改變家庭關係 , 修正家庭關係 , 如修正時間衝突般 。
so i want to end by saying: many of life's puzzles can be solved by understanding your time perspective and that of others .	最後 , 我想說的是 , 生活中許多的謎題都可以藉由了解自己的時間和他人的觀點來解決 。
and the idea is so simple , so obvious , but i think the consequences are really profound .	這個想法如此簡單、顯而易見 , 但我認為後果是很深遠的 。
how many of today's headlines will matter in 100 years ? 1000 ? kirk citron's " long news " project collects stories that not only matter today , but will resonate for decades even centuries to come . at ted2010 , he highlights recent headlines with the potential to shape our future .	一百年後有多少今天的標題會被重視 ? 一百年後 ? kirkciton的 「 長篇新聞 」 計畫收集了現今不只重大 , 還會在接下來的數十年得到共鳴 。 在ted2010 , 他強調了近期標題 , 有潛力可以塑造我們的未來 。
future , global issues , media , news , science	未來 , 全球議題 , 媒體 , 新聞 , 科學
kirk citron: and now , the real news	kirkcitron:現在 , 真正的新聞 。
we are drowning in news .	我們淹沒在新聞中 。
reuters alone puts out three and a half million news stories a year .	單是路透社一家一年就發佈350萬則新聞
that's just one source .	那只是其中一個來源 。
my question is: how many of those stories are actually going to matter in the long run ?	我的問題是:這些故事當中 , 有多少在長期來看是重要的 ?
that's the idea behind the long news .	這是背後的好消息 。
it's a project by the long now foundation , which was founded by tedsters including kevin kelly and stewart brand .	這個計畫是 「 長遠當代基金會 」 由ted成員凱文凱利和史都華布蘭德所創立的 。
and what we're looking for is news stories that might still matter 50 or 100 or 10 , 000 years from now .	我們在尋找的是一個新聞 , 可能在50、100或10或10 , 000年後仍然會被重視 。
and when you look at the news through that filter , a lot falls by the wayside .	當你透過那種過濾器看新聞時 , 很多事情就會掉下來 。
to take the top stories from the a . p . this last year , is this going to matter in a decade ?	以去年a.p.p.的上層故事為例 , 這在十年內會很重要嗎 ?
is this going to matter in 50 or 100 years ?	這在50或100年後會很重要嗎 ?
okay , that was kind of cool .	好吧 , 還滿酷的 。
but the top story of this past year was the economy , and i'm just betting that , sooner or later , this particular recession is going to be old news .	但去年最主要的報導是經濟 , 我只是打賭 , 遲早 , 這個衰退的報導會是舊消息 。
so , what kind of stories might make a difference for the future ?	那麼 , 什麼樣的故事會對未來造成影響 ?
well , let's take science .	嗯 , 就科學來說 ,
someday , little robots will go through our bloodstreams fixing things .	總有一天 , 小機器人會穿透我們的血液管道 , 修理東西 。
that someday is already here if you're a mouse .	如果你是老鼠的話那總有一天已經到來了
some recent stories: nanobees zap tumors with real bee venom ; they're sending genes into the brain ; a robot they built that can crawl through the human body .	最近一些故事:奈米蜜蜂用真蜂毒液將腫瘤傳送進腦部 , 一個建造可爬行人體的機器人 。
what about resources ? how are we going to feed nine billion people ?	資源方面呢 ? 我們要如何養活九十億人 ?
we're having trouble feeding six billion today .	今天我們有高達60億的糧食問題 。
as we heard yesterday , there's over a billion people hungry .	正如我們昨天聽到的 , 這裡有超過十億人在挨餓 。
britain will starve without genetically modified crops .	不用基因改造作物 , 英國就會餓死 。
bill gates , fortunately , has bet a billion on [agricultural] research .	幸運的是 , 比爾蓋茲投入了十億在農業研究上 。
what about global politics ?	那全球政治呢 ?
the world's going to be very different when and if china sets the agenda , and they may .	世界將大不相同 , 何時為中國設立議程 , 他們也可能
they've overtaken the u . s . as the world's biggest car market , they've overtaken germany as the largest exporter , and they've started doing dna tests on kids to choose their careers .	他們超過美國成為世界上最大的汽車市場 , 已經超過德國成為最大的出口國 , 已經開始在兒童身上做dna測試 , 來選擇他們的職業 。
we're finding all kinds of ways to push back the limits of what we know .	我們發現各種途徑 , 推開我們所知的極限
some recent discoveries: there's an ant colony from argentina that has now spread to every continent but antarctica ; there's a selfdirected robot scientist that's made a discovery soon , science may no longer need us , and life may no longer need us either ; a microbe wakes up after 120 , 000 years .	一些近期的發現:從阿根廷有一個蟻群 , 已經傳播到每一個大陸 , 但是南極洲 ; 有一個自導型機器人科學家 , 很快的 , 科學可能不再需要我們了 , 生命也許也不需要我們 ; 微生物在120 , 000年後醒來 。
it seems that with or without us , life will go on .	好像有沒有我們 , 生命都會延續下去 。
but my pick for the top long news story of this past year was this one: water found on the moon .	但 , 我去年挑選的長篇新聞是這個:水在月球上被發現 。
makes it a lot easier to put a colony up there .	讓蟻群很容易放上去 。
and if nasa doesn't do it , china might , or somebody in this room might write a big check .	如果美國太空總署不做 , 中國會 , 或在座某些人可能會寫大支票 。
my point is this: in the long run , some news stories are more important than others .	我的重點是:長遠來看 , 某些新聞故事比其他新聞更重要 。
planetary scientist carolyn porco shows images from the cassini voyage to saturn , focusing on its largest moon , titan , and on frozen enceladus , which seems to shoot jets of ice .	行星科學家carolynporco展示了從卡西尼航海到土星的影像 , 著重在它的最大衛星泰坦 , 和在結冰的土衛二上 , 它似乎是對冰的噴射流 。
nasa , design , exploration , science , space , technology , universe , visualizations	nasa , 設計 , 探索 , 科學 , 太空 , 科技 , 宇宙 , 視覺化的呈現 。
carolyn porco flies us to saturn	carolynporco為我們飛往土星
in the next 18 minutes , i'm going to take you on a journey .	在接下來的18分鐘裡 , 我將帶你們踏上一段旅程 ,
and it's a journey that you and i have been on for many years now , and it began some 50 years ago , when humans first stepped off our planet .	這段旅程是你和我已經踏上許多年的旅程 , 它開始於大約五十年前 , 人類第一次踏出我們的星球 。
and in those 50 years , not only did we literally , physically set foot on the moon , but we have dispatched robotic spacecraft to all the planets all eight of them and we have landed on asteroids , we have rendezvoused with comets , and , at this point in time , we have a spacecraft on its way to pluto , the body formerly known as a planet .	在這50年中 , 我們不僅在月球上 , 還裝了一艘太空船 , 我們在各個行星上都裝上了分散的機械太空船 , 我們在小行星上著陸 , 我們用彗星裝備著 , 在這個時點 , 我們有一艘太空船 , 正在它前往冥王星的路上 , 也就是我們所知的身體 。
and all of these robotic missions are part of a bigger human journey: a voyage to understand something , to get a sense of our cosmic place , to understand something of our origins , and how earth , our planet , and we , living on it , came to be .	所有這些機器人的任務 , 都是人類旅程的一部分:一個能了解事物的旅程 , 能理解我們的宇宙 , 理解我們的起源 , 了解我們的起源 , 地球 , 我們的星球 , 我們的生活方式 , 都是由它來的 。
and of all the places in the solar system that we might go to and search for answers to questions like this , there's saturn . and we have been to saturn before we visited saturn in the early 1980s but our investigations of saturn have become far more indepth in detail since the cassini spacecraft , traveling across interplanetary space for seven years , glided into orbit around saturn in the summer of 2004 , and became at that point the farthest robotic outpost that humanity had ever established around the sun .	在太陽系的所有地方中 , 我們可能去那裡尋找類似問題的答案 , 那裡是土星 。 在1980年代初 , 我們去過土星之前 , 我們去過土星 。 但是我們對於土星的調查從卡西尼號太空船開始更加深入 , 穿梭於星際空間中長達七年之久 , 在2004年夏天穿梭於土星的飛行軌道 , 成為當時人類最遠的機械裝置 , 就是地球地球 。
now , the saturn system is a rich planetary system .	現在 , 土星系是個豐富的行星系統 。
it offers mystery , scientific insight and obviously splendor beyond compare , and the investigation of this system has enormous cosmic reach .	它提供了神秘的、科學的洞見 , 以及明顯的光輝 , 相對之下 , 這個系統的調查有著巨大的宇宙性 。
in fact , just studying the rings alone , we stand to learn a lot about the discs of stars and gas that we call the spiral galaxies .	事實上 , 單單研究光環 , 我們就能瞭解很多恆星和氣體的圓盤 , 我們稱之為螺旋星系 。
and here's a beautiful picture of the andromeda nebula , which is our closest , largest spiral galaxy to the milky way .	這裡有一張仙女座星雲的美麗圖片 , 它是我們離銀河系最近 , 體積最大的螺旋星系 。
and then , here's a beautiful composite of the whirlpool galaxy , taken by the hubble space telescope .	這裡有個很漂亮的旋渦星系由哈勃太空望遠鏡所拍攝
so the journey back to saturn is really part of and is also a metaphor for a much larger human voyage to understand the interconnectedness of everything around us , and also how humans fit into that picture .	所以 , 回到土星的旅程其實是土星的一部分 , 也是人類更大的旅程 , 比喻著我們身邊一切事物的相互連結性 , 以及人類如何融入那張照片 。
and it pains me that i can't tell you all that we have learned with cassini .	我很痛苦 , 我無法告訴各位 , 我們已經學過卡西尼號 。
i can't show you all the beautiful pictures that we've taken in the last two and a half years , because i simply don't have the time .	我無法向你們展示我們在過去兩年半所拍攝的所有漂亮圖片 , 因為我沒有足夠的時間 。
so i'm going to concentrate on two of the most exciting stories that have emerged out of this major exploratory expedition that we are conducting around saturn , and have been for the past two and a half years .	所以 , 我要把焦點放在這次重大探索之旅中兩個最令人興奮的故事 , 就是我們要在土星周圍進行 , 且已經持續兩年半了 。
saturn is accompanied by a very large and diverse collection of moons .	土星伴隨著非常大且多樣的集合月球
they range in size from a few kilometers across to as big across as the u . s .	它們的大小從幾公里寬到美國這麼大 。
most of the beautiful pictures we've taken of saturn , in fact , show saturn in accompaniment with some of its moons . here's saturn with dione , and then , here's saturn showing the rings edgeon , showing you just how vertically thin they are , with the moon enceladus .	大部分我們拍攝土星的美麗照片 , 事實上 , 土星和它的一些衛星在一起 。 這是土星和土衛二 , 這是土星和土星 , 這是土星的光環 , 表明它們的垂直稀薄 。
now , two of the 47 moons that saturn has are standouts .	現在 , 土星47顆衛星中 , 有兩顆是立體 。
and those are titan and enceladus . titan is saturn's largest moon , and , until cassini had arrived there , was the largest single expanse of unexplored terrain that we had remaining in our solar system .	那些是土衛六泰坦和土衛二恩克拉多斯 。 泰坦是土星最大的衛星 , 並且 , 在卡西尼號到達之前 , 曾是太陽系中最大的一個未經探索的單一地帶 。
and it is a body that has long intrigued people who've watched the planets .	它是長期以來引人入勝的天體 , 觀看過行星的人 。
it has a very large , thick atmosphere , and in fact , its surface environment was believed to be more like the environment we have here on the earth , or at least had in the past , than any other body in the solar system .	它有很大很厚的大氣層 , 事實上 , 它的地表環境被認為更像是我們在地球上的環境 , 或者說至少在過去 , 比其它太陽系中的天體 。
its atmosphere is largely molecular nitrogen , like you are breathing here in this room , except that its atmosphere is suffused with simple organic materials like methane and propane and ethane .	它的大氣中有很大一部分是氮分子 , 就像你在這裡吸入的氮氣一樣 , 只不過它的大氣被甲烷和丙烷等簡單有機物質所混淆 。
and these molecules high up in the atmosphere of titan get broken down , and their products join together to make haze particles .	這些在土衛六的大氣層中分子被分解後 , 它們的產品結合成霧狀顆粒 。
this haze is ubiquitous . it's completely global and enveloping titan .	這個霧狀物無所不在 , 完全是全球性的 , 籠罩土衛六 。
and that's why you cannot see down to the surface with our eyes in the visible region of the spectrum .	這也是為什麼在可視範圍內 , 你無法在可見光中看到下面的表面 。
but these haze particles , it was surmised , before we got there with cassini , over billions and billions of years , gently drifted down to the surface and coated the surface in a thick organic sludge .	但這些霧狀顆粒 , 在我們到達卡西尼之前 , 在數十億年的時間 , 輕輕地漂流到水面上 , 將表面覆蓋在厚厚的有機廢物中 。
so like the equivalent , the titan equivalent , of tar , or oil , or what we didn't know what .	就像泰坦一樣 , 泰坦相當於焦油 , 或石油 , 我們不知道的是什麼 。
but this is what we suspected . and these molecules , especially methane and ethane , can be liquids at the surface temperatures of titan .	但這卻是我們懷疑的 。 而這些分子 , 尤其是甲烷和乙烷 , 在土衛六的表面溫度下 , 可以是液體 。
and so it turns out that methane is to titan what water is to the earth .	結果發現 , 甲烷是土衛六地上的水 。
it's a condensable in the atmosphere , and so recognizing this circumstance brought to the fore a whole world of bizarre possibilities . you can have methane clouds , ok , and above those clouds , you have this hundreds of kilometers of haze , which prevent any sunlight from getting to the surface .	它在大氣中是可以冷凝的 , 所以認知到這種情況 , 帶到一個奇怪的可能性世界 。 你可以有甲烷雲 , 在這些雲之上 , 你有數百公里的霧狀物 , 可以避免陽光照射到地表 。
the temperature at the surface is some 350 degrees below zero fahrenheit .	地表的溫度在華氏零下350度 。
but despite that cold , you could have rain falling down on the surface of titan .	但儘管那樣寒冷 , 你還是有可能在土衛六地表下雨 。
and doing on titan what rain does on the earth: it carves gullies ; it forms rivers and cataracts ; it can create canyons ; it can pool in large basins and craters .	在土衛六上下雨的地方 , 它會雕刻海鷗 ; 它會形成河流和白內障 , 能造出峽谷 ; 大型盆地和隕石 。
it can wash the sludge off high mountain peaks and hills , down into the lowlands . so stop and think for a minute .	它可以把泥巴從高山和山丘上沖到低窪地帶 。 所以停下來想一想 。
try to imagine what the surface of titan might look like .	試著想像土衛六的地表是甚麼樣子 。
it's dark . high noon on titan is as dark as deep earth twilight on the earth .	它很黑 。 土衛六上的中午和地球上所有深處的地球一樣黑 。
it's cold , it's eerie , it's misty , it might be raining , and you might be standing on the shores of lake michigan brimming with paint thinner .	那裡很冷 , 陰森森 , 陰森 , 迷霧重重 , 可能正在下雨 , 而你可能正站在密西根湖邊 , 和油漆稀疏的邊緣 。
that is the view that we had of the surface of titan before we got there with cassini , and i can tell you that what we have found on titan , though it is not the same in detail , is every bit as fascinating as that story is .	在卡西尼號到達之前 , 我們看到土衛六地表的景象 , 我可以告訴各位 , 我們在土衛六上發現的 , 雖然在細節裡 , 卻不盡相同 , 故事的精彩絕倫 。
and for us , it has been like the cassini people it has been like a jules verne adventure come true .	對我們來說 , 就像卡西尼號的人一樣--這就像是跳躍式的凡爾納冒險一樣 。
as i said , it has a thick , extensive atmosphere .	我說過 , 它有很厚、廣闊的大氣層 。
this is a picture of titan , backlit by the sun , with the rings as a beautiful backdrop .	這張是土衛六的照片 , 被太陽照的背光 , 光環是美麗的背景 。
and yet another moon there i don't even know which one it is . it's a very extensive atmosphere .	但另一顆衛星──我甚至不知道是哪一顆 。 它的大氣層非常廣闊 。
we have instruments on cassini which can see down to the surface through this atmosphere , and my camera system is one of them .	我們在卡西尼號上有可以透過大氣層看到海面的儀器我的相機系統就是其中之一
and we have taken pictures like this .	我們也拍了這樣的照片
and what you see is bright and dark regions , and that's about as far as it got for us .	而你所看到的是明亮、黑暗的區域 , 大概就是它為我們帶來的好處 。
it was so mystifying: we couldn't make out what we were seeing on titan .	這實在是太神秘了:我們無法辨別我們在土衛六上看到的東西 。
when you look closer at this region , you start to see things like sinuous channels we didn't know . you see a few round things .	當你看得更近這一區域你會開始看到一些東西 , 像是連續的管道我們不知道 。 你看到一些圓的東西
this , we later found out , is , in fact , a crater , but there are very few craters on the surface of titan , meaning it's a very young surface .	這個 , 後來我們發現 , 事實上是一個坑 , 但是土衛六表面的隕石坑數量很少 , 意味著土衛六的地表非常年輕 。
and there are features that look tectonic .	還有一些看起來像地殼構造的特徵 。
they look like they've been pulled apart .	看起來牠們被拉開了 。
whenever you see anything linear on a planet , it means there's been a fracture , like a fault .	每當你看到一個行星上的線性行星 , 就表示這裡有一個斷裂 , 像斷層一樣 。
and so it's been tectonically altered .	所以它已經在結構上有所改變 。
but we couldn't make sense of our images , until , six months after we got into orbit , an event occurred that many have regarded as the highlight of cassini's investigation of titan .	但我們無法理解我們的影像 , 直到我們進入軌道六個月後 , 一件事件發生了 , 許多人認為它是卡西尼號對於土衛六的重要發現 。
and that was the deployment of the huygens probe , the europeanbuilt huygens probe that cassini had carried for seven years across the solar system . we deployed it to the atmosphere of titan , it took two and a half hours to descend , and it landed on the surface .	那就是惠更斯號探測器的部署 , 歐洲建築的惠更斯號探測器 , 卡西尼號在整個太陽系中載了七年 。 我們將它部署到土衛六的大氣當中 , 它花了兩個半小時才下降 , 降到地表 。
and i just want to emphasize how significant an event this is .	我只想強調這個活動有多重大 。
this is a device of human making , and it landed in the outer solar system for the first time in human history .	這是人類製造的裝置 , 它在外太陽系的首次登陸 。
it is so significant that , in my mind , this was an event that should have been celebrated with ticker tape parades in every city across the u . s . and europe , and sadly , that wasn't the case .	意義重大 , 在我心目中 , 這事件本應為美國和歐洲各大城市的報紙遊行而歡慶 , 真是太不幸了 , 事實並非如此 。
it was significant for another reason . this is an international mission , and this event was celebrated in europe , in germany , and the celebratory presentations were given in english accents , and american accents , and german accents , and french and italian and dutch accents .	這很有意義 , 另一個原因 。 這是一個國際性的任務 , 這個活動在歐洲、德國受到讚頌 , 發表了許多情節 , 用英語口音 , 美國口音 , 德語 , 法語 , 意大利語和荷蘭口音 。
it was a moving demonstration of what the words " united nations " are supposed to mean: a true union of nations joined together in a colossal effort for good .	那是一個 「 聯合國 」 一詞的 「 移動示範 」 應該代表的意思:一個真正的國家團結一起努力地帶來正面的效果 。
and , in this case , it was a massive undertaking to explore a planet , and to come to understand a planetary system that , for all of human history , had been unreachable , and now humans had actually touched it .	在這個案例中 , 探索一個星球是很大的成果 , 並漸漸了解一個星球系統 , 這個系統在人類歷史上全都是不可接觸的 , 而現在人類才真正接觸到它 。
so it was i mean , i'm getting goose bumps just talking about it .	所以 , 我說的就是起雞皮疙瘩 。
it was a tremendously emotional event , and it's something that i will personally never forget , and you shouldn't either .	那是一個極度情緒化的事件 , 它是我個人永遠無法忘記的 , 你也不該如此 。
but anyway , the probe took measurements of the atmosphere on the way down , and it also took panoramic pictures .	但 , 總之 , 探測器在飛行途中對大氣進行了測量 , 同時也拍了全景照片 。
and i can't tell you what it was like to see the first pictures of titan's surface from the probe . and this is what we saw .	我無法告訴各位 , 從探測器上看到土衛六地表照片是什麼樣子 。 這就是我們所看到的 。
and it was a shocker , because it was everything we wanted those other pictures taken from orbit to be .	這真是震驚人心 , 因為那是我們希望其他照片從軌道上拍攝的一切 。
it was an unambiguous pattern , a geological pattern .	那是個很明確的模式 , 一種地質模式 。
it's a dendritic drainage pattern that can be formed only by the flow of liquids .	它是可由液體流動而形成的樹突狀體型 。
and you can follow these channels and you can see how they all converge .	你可以沿著這些管道 , 看到它們是如何匯合的 。
and they converge into this channel here , which drains into this region .	它們匯聚到這裡的通道中 , 流進這個區域 。
you are looking at a shoreline .	你看到的是一條海岸線 。
was this a shoreline of fluids ? we didn't know .	這是液體的海岸線嗎 ? 我們不知道 。
but this is somewhat of a shoreline .	但這是一條海岸線 。
this picture is taken at 16 kilometers .	這張照片是在16公里高的地方拍的 。
this is the picture taken at eight kilometers , ok ? again , the shoreline .	這是以8公里的高度所拍攝的照片 , 好嗎 ? 還是海岸線 。
okay , now , 16 kilometers , eight kilometers this is roughly an airline altitude .	好 , 現在 , 16公里 , 8公里--這大約是飛機的一個高度 。
if you were going to take an airplane trip across the u . s . , you would be flying at these altitudes .	如果你要飛機穿越美國 , 你就要飛到這些高度 。
so , this is the picture you would have at the window of titanian airlines as you fly across the surface of titan .	所以 , 這是在泰坦航空公司的窗口所放的照片 , 當你飛越泰坦的表面時 。
and then finally , the probe came to rest on the surface , and i'm going to show you , ladies and gentlemen , the first picture ever taken from the surface of a moon in the outer solar system .	最後 , 探測器在地表上安息 , 我要給大家看的是 , 女士們 , 先生們 , 外太陽系拍下的第一張衛星照片 。
and here is the horizon , ok ?	這裡是地平線 , 好嗎 ?
these are probably water ice pebbles , yes ?	這些可能是冰鵝卵石 , 對嗎 ?
and obviously , it landed in one of these flat , dark regions and it didn't sink out of sight . so it wasn't fluid that we landed in .	很顯然 , 它落在了其中一個平坦、黑暗的區域 , 且它沒有沉沒消失在視線之中 。 所以它不是流動的 , 我們落地了 。
what the probe came down in was basically the titan equivalent of a mud flat .	探測器基本上就是土衛六的平地 。
this is an unconsolidated ground that is suffused with liquid methane .	這是一個不固定的土地 , 裡頭充滿了液態甲烷 。
and it's probably the case that this material has washed off the highlands of titan through these channels that we saw , and has drained over billions of years to fill in lowlying basins .	這種材料可能已經沖走了土衛六的高地 , 通過我們看到的這些管道 , 流失了數十億年 , 可以填充到低窪地帶 。
and that is what the huygens probe landed in .	這就是惠更斯號探測器著陸的地方 。
but still , there was no sign in our images , or even in the huygens' images , of any large , open bodies of fluids .	但仍然沒有跡象顯示我們的影像 , 甚至惠更斯號的影像 , 都沒有大型液體開放的形體 。
where were they ? it got even more puzzling when we found dunes .	他們在哪裡 ? 當我們發現沙丘時 , 更讓人困惑了 。
ok , so this is our movie of the equatorial region of titan , showing these dunes . these are dunes that are 100 meters tall , separated by a few kilometers , and they go on for miles and miles and miles .	好 , 這是我們在土衛六赤道附近的電影 , 展現這些沙丘 。 這些沙丘有100公尺高 , 被幾公里遠的沙丘分隔開 , 然後再延伸好幾英里遠 。
there's hundreds , up to a 1 , 000 or 1 , 200 miles of dunes .	高達1000或1200英里的沙丘
this is the saharan desert of titan .	這是土衛六的撒哈拉沙漠 。
it's obviously a place which is very dry , or you wouldn't get dunes .	顯然是個非常乾燥的地方 , 否則就不會有沙丘 。
so again , it got puzzling that there were no bodies of fluid , until finally , we saw lakes in the polar regions .	所以 , 同樣的 , 讓人困惑的是 , 沒有液體的屍體 , 直到最後 , 我們看到了極地的湖泊 。
and there is a lake scene in the south polar region of titan .	土衛六的南極地區有一個湖 。
it's about the size of lake ontario .	和安大略湖差不多大 。
and then , only a week and a half ago , we flew over the north pole of titan and found , again , we found a feature here the size of the caspian sea .	然後 , 僅僅一個星期半前 , 我們飛過北極 , 發現了太平洋的大小 。
so it seems that the liquids , for some reason we don't understand , or during at least this season , are apparently at the poles of titan .	由於某些原因我們並不了解液體 , 或者在這一季 , 很明顯的 , 土衛六的極地 。
and i think you would agree that we have found titan is a remarkable , mystical place . it's exotic , it's alien , but yet strangely earthlike , and having earthlike geological formations and a tremendous geographical diversity , and is a fascinating world whose only rival in the solar system for complexity and richness is the earth itself .	我想你會同意我們發現土衛六是一個了不起、神秘的地方 。 它很奇特 , 它很奇特 , 但又很奇怪 , 像地球一樣 , 又有著像地球般的地質構造 , 又有著巨大的地理多樣性 , 也是一個迷人的世界 , 它在太陽系中 , 僅僅能以複雜度與豐富性的方式與地球相對應 。
and so now we go onto enceladus . enceladus is a small moon , it's about a tenth the size of titan . and you can see it here next to england , just to show you the size . this is not meant to be a threat .	所以現在我們來到土衛二看看 。 土衛二是一個小型衛星 , 尺寸大約是土衛六的十分之一 。 你可以看到它站在英國旁邊 , 只是想讓你們看看尺寸 。 這並不是指威脅 。
and enceladus is very white , it's very bright , and its surface is obviously wrecked with fractures .	而土衛二很白很明亮 , 它的表面明顯是碎裂的 。
it is a very geologically active body .	這是個非常地質活動的身體 。
but the mother lode of discoveries on enceladus was found at the south pole and we're looking at the south pole here where we found this system of fractures .	但土衛二上的發現之母就在南極 , 我們看到的是南極的地帶 , 我們發現了這個破裂的系統 。
and they're a different color because they're a different composition .	它們的顏色不同 , 因為它們是不同的編曲 。
they are coated . these fractures are coated with organic materials .	它們是覆蓋的 。 這些裂縫會覆蓋有機物質 。
moreover , this whole , entire region , the south polar region , has elevated temperatures . it's the hottest place on the planet , on the body .	此外 , 這整體 , 整個南極地區的溫度上升 , 是這個星球上最熱的地方 。
that's as bizarre as finding that the antarctic on the earth is hotter than the tropics .	這就和發現地球南極比熱帶地區還熱一樣奇怪 。
and then , when we took additional pictures , we discovered that from these fractures are issuing jets of fine , icy particles extending hundreds of miles into space .	接著 , 當我們拍攝額外的照片 , 我們發現從這些斷裂中 , 有精細的冰粒噴射出來 , 噴射範圍可以延伸數百英里 。
and when we colorcode this image , to bring out the faint light levels , we see that these jets feed a plume that , in fact , we see , in other images , goes thousands of miles into the space above enceladus .	當我們用顏色來分析這張影像 , 將微弱的光線分流出來時 , 我們可以看到 , 這些噴射流在土衛二的上空中流動數千英里 。
my team and i have examined images like this , and like this one , and have thought about the other results from cassini .	我和我的團隊對這些圖片進行了分析 , 像這張 , 並且思考了卡西尼號的其他成果 。
and we have arrived at the conclusion that these jets may be erupting from pockets of liquid water under the surface of enceladus .	我們的結論是 , 這些噴射現象可能是由土衛二地表下的液態水的口袋噴發而出 。
so we have , possibly , liquid water , organic materials and excess heat .	因此我們有 , 可能是液態水 , 有機物質和過剩的熱能 。
in other words , we have possibly stumbled upon the holy grail of modern day planetary exploration , or in other words , an environment that is potentially suitable for living organisms .	換句話說 , 我們可能偶然發現了現代行星探索的聖杯 , 或者說 , 一個可能適合生物生存的環境 。
and i don't think i need to tell you that the discovery of life elsewhere in our solar system , whether it be on enceladus or elsewhere , would have enormous cultural and scientific implications .	而我不認為我需要告訴你在太陽系其他地方生物的發現 , 不管是在土衛二或其它地方 , 都會有巨大的文化與科學的影響 。
because if we could demonstrate that genesis had occurred not once , but twice , independently , in our solar system , then that means , by inference , it has occurred a staggering number of times throughout the universe and its 13 . 7 billion year history .	因為如果我們能證明太陽系曾出現過不止一次 , 而是兩次 , 獨立於我們的太陽系 。 那就表示 , 按照推論 , 它在宇宙中已經發生了不少次 。 整個宇宙137億年的歷史都出現了 。
right now , earth is the only planet still that we know is teeming with life .	目前 , 地球仍然是唯一一個我們知道有生命的行星 。
it is precious , it is unique , it is still , so far , the only home we've ever known .	它很珍貴 , 它是獨一無二的 , 它依然是我們唯一知道的家園 。
and if any of you were alert and coherent during the 1960s and we'd forgive you , if you weren't , ok you would remember this very famous picture taken by the apollo 8 astronauts in 1968 .	如果在座有人在1960年代時有警覺和連貫性的話--我們會原諒你 , 如果你沒有 , 你可以記得1968年由阿波羅八號太空人拍攝的這張有名的照片 。
it was the first time that earth was imaged from space , and it had an enormous impact on our sense of place in the universe , and our sense of responsibility for the protection of our own planet .	那是第一次從太空拍攝地球的影像 , 並且對我們在宇宙中的位置產生了巨大的影響 , 以及我們對於保護地球的責任感 。
well , we on cassini have taken an equivalent first , a picture that no human eye has ever seen before .	我們在卡西尼號上拍攝了等同於人類眼睛的照片 。
it is a total eclipse of the sun , seen from the other side of saturn .	這是日全蝕 , 從土星的另一側看到的 。
and in this impossibly beautiful picture , you see the main rings backlit by the sun , you see the refracted image of the sun and you see this ring created , in fact , by the exhalations of enceladus .	在這張美麗的圖片裡 , 你看到背後的主光環 , 看到太陽折射的影像 , 看到這個光環事實上由土衛二的表面噴出 。
but as if that weren't brilliant enough , we can spot , in this beautiful image , sight of our own planet , cradled in the arms of saturn's rings .	但就好像這還不夠精彩 , 我們可以在這個美麗的圖像中發現 , 看到我們自己的星球 , 正如土星的光環一樣 。
now , there is something deeply moving about seeing ourselves from afar , and capturing the sight of our little , blueocean planet in the skies of other worlds .	現在 , 有種很深的動力 , 就是從遠處看我們自己 , 捕捉到我們在其他世界天空中那個小藍色的地球 。
and that , and the perspective of ourselves that we gain from that , may be , in the end , the finest reward that we earn from this journey of discovery that started half a century ago .	那 , 以及我們從中所獲得的觀點 , 可能 , 到頭來 , 我們從這次探索旅程所得到的最好的獎勵 , 一切都起源於半個世紀前 。
as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped . this slows the delivery of aid after a disaster and hides the economic potential of unused lands and unknown roads . in this short talk , google's lalitesh katragadda demos map maker , a group mapmaking tool that people around the globe are using to map their world .	截至2005年 , 世界上只有15%的地區被繪製出來 。 這使災難發生後的人們在災難後緩慢地傳遞 , 並隱藏未知的土地和未知的道路 。 在這簡短的簡短的演講中 , 谷歌的已故卡特拉達展示的地圖製造商 , 一個團體繪製出的工具 , 正使用在地圖上繪製他們的世界 。
collaboration , design , map , technology	合作、設計、地圖、科技、
lalitesh katragadda: making maps to fight disaster , build economies	拉利斯•卡特加達:製作地圖來對抗災難 , 建立經濟 。
in 2008 , cyclone nargis devastated myanmar .	在2008年 , 氣旋納基斯蹂躪了緬甸 。
millions of people were in severe need of help .	數百萬人嚴重需要協助 。
the u . n . wanted to rush people and supplies to the area .	聯合國想要把人民和物資趕到當地
but there were no maps , no maps of roads , no maps showing hospitals , no way for help to reach the cyclone victims .	但當時沒有地圖 , 沒有道路的地圖 , 沒有顯示醫院的地圖 , 沒有辦法協助接觸到氣旋受害者 。
when we look at a map of los angeles or london , it is hard to believe that as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped to a geocodable level of detail .	當我們看看洛杉磯或倫敦的地圖時 , 很難相信到2005年 , 世界上只有15%的地區 , 都有地理的細節 。
the u . n . ran headfirst into a problem that the majority of the world's populous faces: not having detailed maps .	聯合國反而把全球大部分的人口臉部問題都導向了這個問題:沒有詳細的地圖 。
but help was coming .	但 , 協助來了 。
at google , 40 volunteers used a new software to map 120 , 000 kilometers of roads , 3 , 000 hospitals , logistics and relief points .	在google有40位志願者使用了一套新軟體標註了12萬公里的道路3000間醫院 , 運送和救濟站
and it took them four days .	他們花了四天的時間
the new software they used ? google mapmaker .	他們用的新軟體 ? googlemapmaker
google mapmaker is a technology that empowers each of us to map what we know locally .	googlemapmaker是一個技術 , 它賦予我們每個人能力 , 繪製我們所知的地區地圖 。
people have used this software to map everything from roads to rivers , from schools to local businesses , and video stores to the corner store .	人們用這套軟體將一切畫在路上 , 從道路到河流 , 從學校到當地的企業然後錄影帶店到轉角的商店
nobel prize nominee hernando de soto recognized that the key to economic liftoff for most developing countries is to tap the vast amounts of uncapitalized land .	諾貝爾獎被提名人hernandodesto認可大部分發展中國家經濟的關鍵就是利用大量未經破壞的土地
for example , a trillion dollars of real estate remains uncapitalized in india alone .	舉例來說 , 光在印度就有一兆美金的房地產是被剝奪的
in the last year alone , thousands of users in 170 countries have mapped millions of pieces of information , and created a map of a level of detail never thought viable .	光在去年170個國家數以千計的使用者就標註了數以百萬計的資訊 , 並建立了一張從來沒想過能運作的程度的地圖 。
and this was made possible by the power of passionate users everywhere .	這項成果得以實現 , 靠著各地充滿激情的用戶的力量 。
let's look at some of the maps being created by users right now .	我們來看看目前使用者製作的一些地圖 。
so , as we speak , people are mapping the world in these 170 countries .	所以 , 在我們演說的同時 , 人們在這170個國家中為世界畫地圖 。
you can see bridget in africa who just mapped a road in senegal .	你可以看到在非洲的bridget剛為塞內加爾標註了一條道路
and , closer to home , chalua , an n . g . road in bangalore .	離家更近 , 夏露瓦 , 班加羅爾的一條n.g.路
this is the result of computational geometry , gesture recognition , and machine learning .	這是計算機幾何學動作識別和機器學習的結果
this is a victory of thousands of users , in hundreds of cities , one user , one edit at a time .	這是對數百個用戶的勝利 , 在數百個城市裡 , 一個用戶 , 一次編輯一筆 。
this is an invitation to the 70 percent of our unmapped planet .	這是個邀請 , 請我們那70%未開發的星球 。
welcome to the new world .	歡迎來到新世界 。
in 2003 , the palestinian village of budrus mounted a 10monthlong nonviolent protest to stop a barrier being built across their olive groves . did you hear about it ? didn't think so . brazilian filmmaker julia bacha asks why we only pay attention to violence in the israelpalestine conflict and not to the nonviolent leaders who may one day bring peace .	2003年 , 巴勒斯坦村落進行了一次長達十個月的非暴力抗議 , 阻止一座障礙在其橄欖草上被建造出來 。 你們聽說了嗎 ? 不這麼認為 ? 巴西製的電影人朱利亞•包夏問我們為什麼只注意以色列和平的暴力事件 , 而不是讓非暴力領導人有一天可能會帶來和平 。
arts , communication , compassion , entertainment , film , peace , violence , war	藝術、溝通、慈悲、娛樂、電影、和平、暴力、戰爭 。
julia bacha: pay attention to nonviolence	juliabacha:注意非暴力事件
for the last 8 years , i have dedicated my life to documenting the work of israelis and palestinians who are trying to end the conflict using peaceful means .	在過去八年間 , 我致力於記錄以色列人與巴勒斯坦人的作品他們試圖通過和平手段來終結衝突 。
when i travel with my work across europe and the united states , one question always comes up: where is the palestinian gandhi ?	當我在歐洲和美國旅行時 , 有一個問題總是出現:巴勒斯坦的甘地在哪裡 ?
why aren't palestinians using nonviolent resistance ?	為什麼巴勒斯坦人不用非暴力的方式抵抗 ?
the challenge i face when i hear this question is that often i have just returned from the middle east where i spent my time filming dozens of palestinians who are using nonviolence to defend their lands and water resources from israeli soldiers and settlers .	當我聽到這個問題時 , 我所面臨的挑戰通常是我才剛從中東回國 , 我在那裡度過時間拍攝了數十位巴勒斯坦人 , 他們用非暴力的方式來捍衛他們的土地和水資源 , 不受以色列士兵和移民者所苦 。
these leaders are trying to forge a massive national nonviolent movement to end the occupation and build peace in the region .	這些領導人試著要讓一場大規模的非暴力運動能夠終結該地區的佔領並建立和平 。
yet , most of you have probably never heard about them .	然而 , 大部分的人可能從未聽說過他們 。
this divide between what's happening on the ground and perceptions abroad is one of the key reasons why we don't have yet a palestinian peaceful resistance movement that has been successful .	這兩者間的分歧 , 介於國外發生的事和認知之間 , 正是我們還沒有成功地進行巴勒斯坦和平抗爭運動的關鍵原因之一 。
so i'm here today to talk about the power of attention , the power of your attention , and the emergence and development of nonviolent movements in the west bank , gaza and elsewhere but today , my case study is going to be palestine .	所以今天我在這裡要談關注的力量、關注的力量、關注的力量 , 以及非暴力運動在西岸、加薩及其他地方的出現和發展 , 但今天我的案例研究將會是巴勒斯坦 。
i believe that what's mostly missing for nonviolence to grow is not for palestinians to start adopting nonviolence , but for us to start paying attention to those who already are .	我相信 , 大多需要非暴力才能成長的原因不是要讓巴勒斯坦人開始採用非暴力手段而是要我們開始注意那些已經有的人們
allow me to illustrate this point by taking you to this village called budrus .	請允許我帶你到這個名為布德魯斯的村落說明這一點 。
about seven years ago , they faced extinction , because israel announced it would build a separation barrier , and part of this barrier would be built on top of the village .	大約七年前 , 他們面臨絕種 , 因為以色列宣佈要築起一道圍牆 , 這障礙的一部分會蓋在村落的上面 。
they would lose 40 percent of their land and be surrounded , so they would lose free access to the rest of the west bank .	他們會失去40%的土地並且被包圍住如此便無法自由往返約旦河西岸的其他地方
through inspired local leadership , they launched a peaceful resistance campaign to stop that from happening .	透過當地的領導 , 他們發動了和平抗爭活動來阻止這件事情發生 。
let me show you some brief clips , so you have a sense for what that actually looked like on the ground .	讓我給你們看一些簡短的短片 , 所以你們應該可以知道 , 地面上到底長什麼樣子 。
palestinian woman: we were told the wall would separate palestine from israel .	巴勒斯坦女性:我們被告知牆將分隔巴勒斯坦與以色列 。
here in budrus , we realized the wall would steal our land .	在布德鲁斯村我們意識到這道牆會偷走我們的土地
israeli man: the fence has , in fact , created a solution to terror .	以色列男子:圍籬實際上創造了一種解決方案
man: today you're invited to a peaceful march .	男:今天你被邀請去一場和平的遊行 。
you are joined by dozens of your israeli brothers and sisters .	你的加入有數十位你的以色列兄弟姐妹
israeli activist: nothing scares the army more than nonviolent opposition .	以色列社會運動人士:軍隊害怕的就是非暴力的反對 。
woman: we saw the men trying to push the soldiers , but none of them could do that .	女:我們看到男人試圖推開士兵 , 但沒有一個能那樣做 。
but i think the girls could do it .	但我認為女孩可以做到 。
fatah party member: we must empty our minds of traditional thinking .	法塔赫黨員:我們必須清空腦中的傳統思維 。
hamas party member: we were in complete harmony , and we wanted to spread it to all of palestine .	哈馬斯黨員:我們當時是完全和諧的 , 我們希望將它擴散到全巴勒斯坦 。
chanting: one united nation .	陳述一個聯合國
fatah , hamas and the popular front !	法塔赫、哈馬斯、人民陣線 !
news anchor: the clashes over the fence continue .	主播:籬笆的衝突持續著 。
reporter: israeli border police were sent to disperse the crowd .	記者:以色列邊境警察被派來驅散群眾
they were allowed to use any force necessary .	他們被允許使用任何必要的力量
man: these are live bullets .	男子:這些是實彈 ,
it's like fallujah . shooting everywhere .	這就像是wujah , 到處開槍
israeli activist: i was sure we were all going to die .	以色列活動家:我很確定我們都會死
but there were others around me who weren't even cowering .	但我身邊還有其他甚至不畏懼的人 。
israeli soldier: a nonviolent protest is not going to stop the [unclear] .	以色列士兵:非暴力抗爭是無法阻止這[不清楚]
protester: this is a peaceful march .	抗議人士:這是一個和平的遊行 。
there is no need to use violence .	不需要使用暴力 。
chanting: we can do it ! we can do it !	口號聲:我們辦得到 ! 我們辦得到 !
julia bacha: when i first heard about the story of budrus , i was surprised that the international media had failed to cover the extraordinary set of events that happened seven years ago , in 2003 .	朱莉亞•巴夏:當我第一次聽到布德鲁斯村的故事時 , 我很驚訝國際媒體竟然沒有報導這一組非凡的事件 , 七年前也發生在2003年 。
what was even more surprising was the fact that budrus was successful .	更令人驚訝的是布德鲁斯村成功了
the residents , after 10 months of peaceful resistance , convinced the israeli government to move the route of the barrier off their lands and to the green line , which is the internationally recognized boundary between israel and the palestinian territories .	居民抗爭十個月後說服了以色列政府將這道牆從他們的土地移開到綠線上也就是國際公認的以色列與巴勒斯坦領土的分界線
the resistance in budrus has since spread to villages across the west bank and to palestinian neighborhoods in jerusalem .	布德鲁斯村的抗爭自此傳遍全約旦河西岸的村莊以及耶路撒冷境內巴勒斯坦人附近的地區
yet the media remains mostly silent on these stories .	然而媒體仍然對這些故事保持沉默
this silence carries profound consequences for the likelihood that nonviolence can grow , or even survive , in palestine .	這種沉默帶給非暴力運動在巴勒斯坦可能生存的可能帶來深遠的影響 。
violent resistance and nonviolent resistance share one very important thing in common ; they are both a form of theater seeking an audience to their cause .	暴力抗爭和非暴力抗爭都有一個非常重要的共通點:它們都是劇院尋求觀眾的一種形式 。
if violent actors are the only ones constantly getting frontpage covers and attracting international attention to the palestinian issue , it becomes very hard for nonviolent leaders to make the case to their communities that civil disobedience is a viable option in addressing their plight .	如果只有使用暴力的人才能上頭版並引起國際媒體關注巴勒斯坦的議題非暴力領袖就很難向他們的社群證明公民不服從是個可行的選項來解決困境
the power of attention is probably going to come as no surprise to the parents in the room .	注意力的力量可能對在場的父母親一點也不意外 。
the surest way to make your child throw increasingly louder tantrums is by giving him attention the first time he throws a fit .	讓你的孩子越來越常吵鬧的最好方法 , 就是讓他第一次去注意他 。
the tantrum will become what childhood psychologists call a functional behavior , since the child has learned that he can get parental attention out of it .	脾臟就會變成兒童心理學家所謂的功能性行為 , 因為孩子們已經知道他能從中得到父母的注意力 。
parents can incentivize or disincentivize behavior simply by giving or withdrawing attention to their children .	父母可以透過給予孩童注意力 , 來鼓勵或抑制這樣的行為 。
but that's true for adults too .	但對成年人來說也是如此 。
in fact , the behavior of entire communities and countries can be influenced , depending on where the international community chooses to focus its attention .	事實上 , 整個社區和國家的行為可以被影響 , 取決於國際社會選擇將注意力放在哪裡 。
i believe that at the core of ending the conflict in the middle east and bringing peace is for us to transform nonviolence into a functional behavior by giving a lot more attention to the nonviolent leaders on the ground today .	我相信 , 終止中東地區衝突的核心 , 並帶來和平 , 就是我們要把非暴力行為轉變成一個功能性行為 , 通過給予當今非暴力領導人更多關注 。
in the course of taking my film to villages in the west bank , in gaza and in east jerusalem , i have seen the impact that even one documentary film can have in influencing the transformation .	在拍攝影片的過程中 , 西岸的村莊加薩及東耶路撒冷的村子我看到了連一部紀錄片都能影響整個轉變的過程
in a village called wallajeh , which sits very close to jerusalem , the community was facing a very similar plight to budrus .	在瓦拉杰村一個名為耶路撒冷的村子裡 , 這個社區面臨著與布德鲁斯村非常相似的困境 。
they were going to be surrounded , lose a lot of their lands and not have freedom of access , either to the west bank or jerusalem .	他們將被包圍 , 失去許多土地也失去往返約旦河西岸或耶路撒冷的自由
they had been using nonviolence for about two years but had grown disenchanted since nobody was paying attention .	他們已經使用非暴力手段大約兩年了 , 但自從沒人注意到他們之後 , 他們逐漸感到不安 。
so we organized a screening .	所以我們安排了一個篩選
a week later , they held the most wellattended and disciplined demonstration to date .	一個星期後 , 他們舉辦了目前為止最精彩且有紀律的展示會 。
the organizers say that the villagers , upon seeing the story of budrus documented in a film , felt that there were indeed people following what they were doing , that people cared .	籌辦人說村民見到布德鲁斯村的故事被記錄在一部電影裡 , 覺得確實有人會遵循他們所做的事情 , 人們會在乎 。
so they kept on going .	所以他們繼續向前 。
on the israeli side , there is a new peace movement called solidariot , which means solidarity in hebrew .	在以色列那邊則有新的和平運動 , 名叫索里德拉爾特 , 意思是希伯來語的團結 。
the leaders of this movement have been using budrus as one of their primary recruiting tools .	這項運動的領導者已經把布德鲁斯村當作主要的工具之一 。
they report that israelis who had never been active before , upon seeing the film , understand the power of nonviolence and start joining their activities .	他們報告說 , 過去從未參與過的以色列人看過影片 , 了解非暴力的力量然後開始加入他們的活動
the examples of wallajeh and the solidariot movement show that even a smallbudget independent film can play a role in transforming nonviolence into a functional behavior .	瓦拉杰村和索里德拉爾特的例子顯示即使小額預算的獨立製片也能在轉換非暴力行為時發揮作用
now imagine the power that big media players could have if they started covering the weekly nonviolent demonstrations happening in villages like bil'in , ni'lin , wallajeh , in jerusalem neighborhoods like sheikh jarrah and silwan the nonviolent leaders would become more visible , valued and effective in their work .	現在 , 想像一下大媒體球員能夠擁有的力量 , 如果他們開始報導周圍發生在村莊裡的那些非暴力示範 , 例如:比利、尼、瓦拉杰 , 在耶路撒冷的鄰里 , 像是謝克•傑拉 , 和絲瓦爾 , 非暴力領導人在他們的作品中變得更加明顯、更加有效 。
i believe that the most important thing is to understand that if we don't pay attention to these efforts , they are invisible , and it's as if they never happened .	我相信最重要的事情是要了解如果我們不注意這些努力 , 它們是看不見的 , 彷彿從來沒有發生過 。
but i have seen first hand that if we do , they will multiply .	但我親眼見到 , 如果我們做到了 , 他們會相乘 ,
if they multiply , their influence will grow in the overall israelipalestinian conflict .	如果他們能相乘 , 他們的影響會在以色列的整體衝突中成長 。
and theirs is the kind of influence that can finally unblock the situation .	而他們的影響力正是那種可以終於解開局面的影響力 。
these leaders have proven that nonviolence works in places like budrus .	這些領導人證實了非暴力是可行的在布德鲁斯村這樣的地方
let's give them attention so they can prove it works everywhere .	讓他們注意 , 這樣他們就能證明它在各地都行得通 。
simon sinek has a simple but powerful model for inspirational leadership all starting with a golden circle and the question " why ? " his examples include apple , martin luther king , and the wright brothers . . .	西蒙•辛克有一個簡單但強而有力的模式 , 鼓舞人心的領導力 , 都從黃金圈子開始 , 質疑為何 ? 他的例子包括蘋果、馬丁•路德•金 , 和萊特兄弟......
bullseye , business , entrepreneur , leadership , sales , selling , success	bullseye , 商業 , 企業家 , 領導者 , 銷售 , 銷售 , 成功
simon sinek: how great leaders inspire action	西蒙•辛克:偉大領袖如何激發行動 。
how do you explain when things don't go as we assume ?	你要怎麼解釋當事情不如我們所想的一般時 ?
or better , how do you explain when others are able to achieve things that seem to defy all of the assumptions ?	或者更好的 , 你如何解釋當其他人可以達成那些看來是違反所有假設的時 ?
for example: why is apple so innovative ?	比如:為什麼蘋果電腦這麼有創意 ?
year after year , after year , after year , they're more innovative than all their competition .	年復一年 , 日復一日他們比全部的競爭對手都要有創意
and yet , they're just a computer company .	然而 , 它們只是一家電腦公司 。
they're just like everyone else .	他們和其他人一樣 。
they have the same access to the same talent , the same agencies , the same consultants , the same media .	他們有相同的人才、相同的機構、同樣的顧問、同樣的媒體 。
then why is it that they seem to have something different ?	那為什麼他們似乎有些不同 ?
why is it that martin luther king led the civil rights movement ?	為什麼是馬丁•路德•金恩領導黑人民權運動 ?
he wasn't the only man who suffered in a precivil rights america , and he certainly wasn't the only great orator of the day .	他不是唯一一個在美國受到折磨的人他當然也不是當時唯一的偉大演說家
and why is it that the wright brothers were able to figure out controlled , powered man flight when there were certainly other teams who were better qualified , better funded . . .	為什麼萊特兄弟能夠想出有控制權、有動力飛行 , 如果有其他團隊更有資格、更好的資金......
and they didn't achieve powered man flight , and the wright brothers beat them to it .	他們沒有達成人力飛行 , 萊特兄弟打敗他們 。
there's something else at play here .	這裡還有其他的玩意兒 ,
about three and a half years ago i made a discovery .	大約三年半前 , 我有一個發現 。
and this discovery profoundly changed my view on how i thought the world worked , and it even profoundly changed the way in which i operate in it .	這個發現深深地改變了我對世界運作方式的看法 , 它甚至深深地改變了我在運作的方式 。
as it turns out , there's a pattern .	結果發現 , 有一種模式 ,
as it turns out , all the great and inspiring leaders and organizations in the world whether it's apple or martin luther king or the wright brothers they all think , act and communicate the exact same way .	結果發現 , 世界上所有偉大且鼓舞人心的領導人和組織不管是蘋果電腦 , 或馬丁路德金 , 或是萊特兄弟他們都認為 , 行動起來和溝通的方法都一樣 。
and it's the complete opposite to everyone else .	而且完全和其他人相反 。
all i did was codify it , and it's probably the world's simplest idea .	我所做的只是將它編碼 , 這可能是世界上最簡單的想法 。
i call it the golden circle .	我稱它做黃金圈 。
why ? how ? what ?	為什麼 ? 怎麼做 ? 什麼 ?
this little idea explains why some organizations and some leaders are able to inspire where others aren't .	這個小小的概念解釋了為什麼有些組織和有些領導人能夠激勵別人不去的地方 。
let me define the terms really quickly .	讓我很快地定義一下這個詞 。
every single person , every single organization on the planet knows what they do , 100 percent .	地球上的每一個人、每一個組織都知道他們在做什麼 , 百分之百肯定 。
some know how they do it , whether you call it your differentiated value proposition or your proprietary process or your usp .	有些人知道他們是如何辦到的 , 不論你怎麼稱呼你不同的價值主張或你的本體流程或你的usp 。
but very , very few people or organizations know why they do what they do .	但很少很少人或機構知道他們為什麼要做的事 。
and by " why " i don't mean " to make a profit . "	我說的 「 為什麼 」 不是指 「 創造利潤 」 。
that's a result . it's always a result .	那是結果 。 它永遠是結果 。
by " why , " i mean: what's your purpose ?	所謂 「 為什麼 」 , 我的意思是:你的目的是什麼 ?
what's your cause ? what's your belief ?	你的目的是什麼 ? 你的信念是什麼 ?
why does your organization exist ?	為什麼你的組織存在 ?
why do you get out of bed in the morning ?	為什麼你早上要起床 ?
and why should anyone care ?	而且為什麼有人要在乎 ?
well , as a result , the way we think , the way we act , the way we communicate is from the outside in .	嗯 , 結果呢 , 我們思考的方式 , 我們行動的方式 , 我們溝通的方式來自外部 。
it's obvious . we go from the clearest thing to the fuzziest thing .	這很明顯 。 我們從最清楚的地方 , 到最模糊不清的 。
but the inspired leaders and the inspired organizations regardless of their size , regardless of their industry all think , act and communicate from the inside out .	但鼓舞人心的領導者以及激勵人心的組織 , 不管它們的規模如何 , 不管它們的產業都會從內心深處思考、行動和溝通 。
let me give you an example .	讓我舉個例子 。
i use apple because they're easy to understand and everybody gets it .	我使用蘋果 , 因為它們很容易理解 , 且大家都懂 。
if apple were like everyone else , a marketing message from them might sound like this: " we make great computers .	如果蘋果電腦跟大家一樣 , 蘋果的行銷訊息可能聽起來像這樣: 「 我們製造很棒的電腦 。
they're beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	它們被設計得很漂亮 , 很簡單的使用 , 以及友善的使用者 。
want to buy one ? " " meh . "	想要買一台嗎 ? 「 啊 。 」
and that's how most of us communicate .	而這就是我們大多數人溝通的方式 。
that's how most marketing is done , that's how most sales is done and that's how most of us communicate interpersonally .	大部份的行銷都是這樣做的 , 大部份的銷售都是這樣做到的 , 而這正是我們多數人溝通交流的方式 。
we say what we do , we say how we're different or how we're better and we expect some sort of a behavior , a purchase , a vote , something like that .	我們說我們做了什麼 , 我們說我們如何不同或我們如何好 , 我們期待某種行為 , 購買、投票等等 。
here's our new law firm: we have the best lawyers with the biggest clients , we always perform for our clients who do business with us .	這是我們的新法律事務所:我們有最好的律師 , 最大客戶 , 我們總是為和我們做生意的客戶服務 。
here's our new car: it gets great gas mileage , it has leather seats , buy our car .	這是我們的新車:它有很好的油耗表現 , 它有皮革製的座椅 , 買我們的車 。
here's how apple actually communicates .	這裡有蘋果電腦實際上溝通的方式:
" everything we do , we believe in challenging the status quo .	「 我們所做的一切 , 我們相信挑戰現況 ,
we believe in thinking differently .	我們相信用不同的方式思考
the way we challenge the status quo is by making our products beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	我們挑戰現況的方式是使我們的產品有美好的設計、簡單的使用 , 以及友善的使用者 。
we just happen to make great computers .	我們只是恰巧製造了很棒的電腦 。
want to buy one ? "	想買一台嗎 ? "
totally different right ? you're ready to buy a computer from me .	完全不一樣吧 ? 你準備好要向我買一台電腦了 。
all i did was reverse the order of the information .	我所做的 , 只是逆轉資訊的順序 。
what it proves to us is that people don't buy what you do ; people buy why you do it .	它告訴我們 , 人們不會買你做什麼 ; 人們買你為什麼做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼做 。
this explains why every single person in this room is perfectly comfortable buying a computer from apple .	這解釋了為什麼在場的每個人都對買蘋果電腦感到完全的自在 。
but we're also perfectly comfortable buying an mp3 player from apple , or a phone from apple , or a dvr from apple .	但我們也很自在地買了蘋果電腦的mp3播放器 , 或蘋果電腦的電話 , 或蘋果電腦的dvr 。
but , as i said before , apple's just a computer company .	但是就像我之前說的 , 蘋果電腦只是一家電腦公司 。
there's nothing that distinguishes them structurally from any of their competitors .	結構上並沒有什麼能區別它們的競爭者 。
their competitors are all equally qualified to make all of these products .	他們的競爭者都有同樣資格製造所有這些產品 。
in fact , they tried .	事實上 , 他們試過
a few years ago , gateway came out with flat screen tvs .	幾年前 , gateway推出他們的平面電視
they're eminently qualified to make flat screen tvs .	他們很明顯夠資格製造平面電視 ,
they've been making flat screen monitors for years .	他們多年來一直在做平面螢幕監視器 。
dell came out with mp3 players and pdas , and they make great quality products , and they can make perfectly welldesigned products and nobody bought one .	戴爾電腦推出mp3播放器與pda , 他們製造了很棒的品質產品 , 他們可以做出完美設計 , 沒有人買一個 。
in fact , talking about it now , we can't even imagine buying an mp3 player from dell .	事實上 , 現在談它 , 我們甚至無法想像從戴爾電腦買一台mp3播放器 。
why would you buy an mp3 player from a computer company ?	為什麼你會從一家電腦公司買一台mp3播放器 ?
but we do it every day .	但我們每天都在做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼做 。
the goal is not to do business with everybody who needs what you have .	目標不是和每個需要你有什麼的人在做生意 。
the goal is to do business with people who believe what you believe .	目標是要和相信你所相信的人做生意 。
here's the best part: none of what i'm telling you is my opinion .	最棒的部分是:我所告訴你們的都不是我的意見 。
it's all grounded in the tenets of biology .	都以生物學的教義為基礎
not psychology , biology .	不是心理學 , 生物學
if you look at a crosssection of the human brain , looking from the top down , what you see is the human brain is actually broken into three major components that correlate perfectly with the golden circle .	如果你看人腦的橫切面 , 從上往下看 , 你會看到人腦其實是被分成三個主要部份 , 和黃金圈完美地相關 。
our newest brain , our homo sapien brain , our neocortex , corresponds with the " what " level .	我們最新的腦、我們的智人大腦、我們的新皮層 , 會對應到 「 什麼 」 的層次 。
the neocortex is responsible for all of our rational and analytical thought and language .	新皮層負責我們所有的理性、分析的想法和語言
the middle two sections make up our limbic brains , and our limbic brains are responsible for all of our feelings , like trust and loyalty .	中間兩個部分組成我們邊緣的腦 , 我們邊緣的腦負責我們所有的感覺 , 比如信任和忠誠 。
it's also responsible for all human behavior , all decisionmaking , and it has no capacity for language .	它也同時負責所有人類的行為所有的決策而它沒有語言的能力
in other words , when we communicate from the outside in , yes , people can understand vast amounts of complicated information like features and benefits and facts and figures .	換句話說 , 當我們從外而內地溝通時 , 是的 , 人們可以了解到大量的複雜資訊 , 像是特色、好處、事實與數字 。
it just doesn't drive behavior .	只是它不能驅動行為 。
when we can communicate from the inside out , we're talking directly to the part of the brain that controls behavior , and then we allow people to rationalize it with the tangible things we say and do .	當我們能由內而外溝通時我們就直接對著控制行為的大腦說話然後我們允許人們將它合理化用我們說的與做為的有形事物
this is where gut decisions come from .	這就是直覺決策的由來 。
you know , sometimes you can give somebody all the facts and figures , and they say , " i know what all the facts and details say , but it just doesn't feel right . "	你知道 , 有時候你能給某人所有的事實和數字 , 然後他們說: 「 我知道所有事實和細節說了什麼 , 但就是感覺不對勁 。 」
why would we use that verb , it doesn't " feel " right ?	為什麼我們要用那個動詞 , 它不會 「 感覺 」 對 ?
because the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking doesn't control language .	因為大腦控制決策的區塊無法控制語言
and the best we can muster up is , " i don't know . it just doesn't feel right . "	而我們最多能整理出的就是: 「 我不知道 。 那感覺不對 。 」
or sometimes you say you're leading with your heart , or you're leading with your soul .	或是有時你說你帶著內心的領導 , 或是你跟你的靈魂一同領導 。
well , i hate to break it to you , those aren't other body parts controlling your behavior .	嗯 , 我很不想對你說這些不是其他身體部位控制你的行為
it's all happening here in your limbic brain , the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking and not language .	都發生在你邊緣的大腦裡 , 大腦控制決策而非語言的區塊 。
but if you don't know why you do what you do , and people respond to why you do what you do , then how will you ever get people to vote for you , or buy something from you , or , more importantly , be loyal and want to be a part of what it is that you do .	但如果你不知道為什麼做你所做的事 , 人們會回應為什麼你做了什麼事 , 那麼 , 你如何才能讓人們投票給你 , 或者向你買東西 , 或者 , 更重要的是 , 要忠實而且想要成為你做的事的一部分 。
again , the goal is not just to sell to people who need what you have ; the goal is to sell to people who believe what you believe .	再次強調 , 目標不只是要賣給需要你所擁有的東西 ; 目標是要賣給那些相信你所相信的事的人 。
the goal is not just to hire people who need a job ; it's to hire people who believe what you believe .	目標不只是要雇用需要工作的人而是要雇用那些相信你所相信的事的人
i always say that , you know , if you hire people just because they can do a job , they'll work for your money , but if you hire people who believe what you believe , they'll work for you with blood and sweat and tears .	我總是這麼說 , 你知道嗎 , 如果你雇用人僅是因為他們可以做一份工作 , 他們將為你的錢工作 , 但如果你雇用那些相信你所相信的人們 , 他們將為你工作 , 帶著血汗和淚水 。
and nowhere else is there a better example of this than with the wright brothers .	除此之外沒有其他更好的例子了萊特兄弟
most people don't know about samuel pierpont langley .	大部分人都不知道samuelpierpontlangley
and back in the early 20th century , the pursuit of powered man flight was like the dot com of the day .	在20世紀初追尋人類飛翔就像當時的網路公司一樣
everybody was trying it .	所有人都在嘗試 。
and samuel pierpont langley had , what we assume , to be the recipe for success .	而samuelpierpontlangley曾經擁有的 , 我們假設的成功的秘訣
i mean , even now , you ask people , " why did your product or why did your company fail ? "	我的意思是 , 即使現在 , 你去問人們: 「 你的產品為何會失敗 ? 」
and people always give you the same permutation of the same three things: undercapitalized , the wrong people , bad market conditions .	人們總會給你相同的三個條件不足 , 不適合的人 , 不適合的市場條件
it's always the same three things , so let's explore that .	總是一樣的三樣東西 , 所以讓我們來探究一下 。
samuel pierpont langley was given 50 , 000 dollars by the war department to figure out this flying machine .	samuelpierpontlangley被戰爭部門用來想出這個飛行機器
money was no problem .	錢沒有問題 。
he held a seat at harvard and worked at the smithsonian and was extremely wellconnected ; he knew all the big minds of the day .	他在哈佛拿了一席之地 , 在史密森尼工作 , 他非常有連結性 , 他知道當時所有的大頭腦 。
he hired the best minds money could find and the market conditions were fantastic .	他雇用最好的頭腦資金 , 可以找到市場條件太棒了 。
the new york times followed him around everywhere , and everyone was rooting for langley .	紐約時報跟著他到處跑而且每個人都為langley加油
then how come we've never heard of samuel pierpont langley ?	那麼我們為什麼從未聽說過samuelpierpontlangley ?
a few hundred miles away in dayton ohio , orville and wilbur wright , they had none of what we consider to be the recipe for success .	在幾百英里外的dayton俄亥俄州和wilburwright他們都沒有我們認為的成功秘訣
they had no money ; they paid for their dream with the proceeds from their bicycle shop ; not a single person on the wright brothers' team had a college education , not even orville or wilbur ; and the new york times followed them around nowhere .	他們沒有資金 , 他們用他們腳踏車店裡的業績來支付夢想 ; 沒有在萊特兄弟的團隊 , 受過大學教育 , 甚至連歐維爾或威爾堡也沒有 。 紐約時報也跟著他們 。
the difference was , orville and wilbur were driven by a cause , by a purpose , by a belief .	不同的是 , 歐維爾和威爾伯是由一個理由 , 一個目的 , 一個信念 , 來驅動的 。
they believed that if they could figure out this flying machine , it'll change the course of the world .	他們相信如果他們能想出這架飛行機器這將改變世界的軌道
samuel pierpont langley was different .	samuelpierpontlangley不同
he wanted to be rich , and he wanted to be famous .	他想變得富有 , 他也想成名
he was in pursuit of the result .	他在追求結果 。
he was in pursuit of the riches .	他追求財富
and lo and behold , look what happened .	你瞧 , 看看發生了什麼事 。
the people who believed in the wright brothers' dream worked with them with blood and sweat and tears .	相信萊特兄弟的夢想的人用血汗與淚水和他們一起工作 。
the others just worked for the paycheck .	另一些人則只是為薪水而工作
and they tell stories of how every time the wright brothers went out , they would have to take five sets of parts , because that's how many times they would crash before they came in for supper .	他們說的故事是每次萊特兄弟出門他們都得帶上五套零件因為這是他們會墜機的次數在他們到供應商口前
and , eventually , on december 17th , 1903 , the wright brothers took flight , and no one was there to even experience it .	最後 , 1903年12月17日萊特兄弟起飛 , 沒有人在現場親身經歷
we found out about it a few days later .	我們在幾天後發現
and further proof that langley was motivated by the wrong thing: the day the wright brothers took flight , he quit .	更進一步證明langley因為錯誤的動機在萊特兄弟起飛的那天 , 他離職了
he could have said , " that's an amazing discovery , guys , and i will improve upon your technology , " but he didn't .	他可以說: 「 那真是很了不起的發現 , 各位 , 我會改善你的技術 。 」 但他沒有 。
he wasn't first , he didn't get rich , he didn't get famous so he quit .	他不是第一個 , 他沒有變有錢 , 他沒有變有名 , 所以他放棄了 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼做 。
and if you talk about what you believe , you will attract those who believe what you believe .	如果你談到你所相信的事 , 你會吸引那些相信你所相信的人們 。
but why is it important to attract those who believe what you believe ?	但為什麼吸引那些相信你所相信的人們很重要 ?
something called the law of diffusion of innovation , and if you don't know the law , you definitely know the terminology .	某樣東西叫做創意的散播法則 , 如果你不知道這個法則 , 你絕對知道它的術語 。
the first two and a half percent of our population are our innovators .	人口的前2.5%就是我們的創新者
the next 13 and a half percent of our population are our early adopters .	接下來的13.5%是早期我們採用的人 。
the next 34 percent are your early majority , your late majority and your laggards .	接下來的34%是早期的大多數晚期的大多數以及落後者
the only reason these people buy touch tone phones is because you can't buy rotary phones anymore .	這些人買觸控式手機的唯一理由 , 是因為你不能再買轉子電話了 。
we all sit at various places at various times on this scale , but what the law of diffusion of innovation tells us is that if you want massmarket success or massmarket acceptance of an idea , you cannot have it until you achieve this tipping point between 15 and 18 percent market penetration , and then the system tips .	我們都坐在這個尺度上不同的位置 , 但創意的散播法則告訴我們的是 , 如果你想要大眾市場成功或是大眾市場接受一個想法 , 你不可能擁有它 , 直到你達到了在15%到18%之間的市場滲透點 , 然後系統就會一面倒 。
and i love asking businesses , " what's your conversion on new business ? "	我很喜歡問企業: 「 你對新事業的轉變是什麼 ? 」
and they love to tell you , " oh , it's about 10 percent , " proudly .	他們很愛告訴你: 「 喔 , 大概是10%吧 ! 」 很驕傲地 ,
well , you can trip over 10 percent of the customers .	嗯 , 你可以讓超過10%的顧客出軌 。
we all have about 10 percent who just " get it . "	我們都有10%的 「 拿到 」
that's how we describe them , right ?	我們就是這樣描述它們的 , 對吧 ?
that's like that gut feeling , " oh , they just get it . "	那就像是那種直覺 , 感覺: 「 喔 , 他們就是懂了 。 」
the problem is: how do you find the ones that get it before you're doing business with them versus the ones who don't get it ?	問題是:你要怎麼找到那些在你做生意前獲得它的人 , 而不是那些沒有得到它的人呢 ?
so it's this here , this little gap that you have to close , as jeffrey moore calls it , " crossing the chasm " because , you see , the early majority will not try something until someone else has tried it first .	所以就是這個 , 這個小小的差距 , 就是你得填上它 , 如同jeffreymoore稱之為 " 跨越隔閡 " 因為 , 你看 , 早期大多不會嘗試 , 直到其他人先嘗試 。
and these guys , the innovators and the early adopters , they're comfortable making those gut decisions .	而這些人 , 這些發明家以及早期的採用者他們對做這些腸道的決定感到很自在
they're more comfortable making those intuitive decisions that are driven by what they believe about the world and not just what product is available .	他們更舒服地做這些直覺的決定 , 是由他們對世界的信念所驅使 , 而不僅是產品的可得性 。
these are the people who stood in line for six hours to buy an iphone when they first came out , when you could have just walked into the store the next week and bought one off the shelf .	這些是排隊排了六個小時買剛上市iphone的人 , 下星期剛剛出門走進商店時 , 再從架子上買了一支 。
these are the people who spent 40 , 000 dollars on flat screen tvs when they first came out , even though the technology was substandard .	這些人花四萬美元在平版電視剛上市 , 儘管科技已經問世了
and , by the way , they didn't do it because the technology was so great ; they did it for themselves .	順便一提 , 他們這麼做並不是因為這項科技太棒了 , 他們靠自己做到了 。
it's because they wanted to be first .	是因為他們想當第一個
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it and what you do simply proves what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼做 , 你做什麼就證明了你相信什麼 。
in fact , people will do the things that prove what they believe .	事實上 , 人們會去做那些證明他們所相信的事 。
the reason that person bought the iphone in the first six hours , stood in line for six hours , was because of what they believed about the world , and how they wanted everybody to see them: they were first .	那人之所以買iphone在最初的六個小時排隊排六個小時是因為他們所相信的世界以及他們希望每個人如何看待他們:他們是第一人
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼做 。
so let me give you a famous example , a famous failure and a famous success of the law of diffusion of innovation .	讓我給你一個有名的例子一個有名的失敗以及有名的成功關於創意的散播法則
first , the famous failure .	首先 , 著名的失敗
it's a commercial example .	這是個商業的例子 。
as we said before , a second ago , the recipe for success is money and the right people and the right market conditions , right ? you should have success then .	如同前面說過的 , 一秒鐘前成功的秘訣就是金錢、對的人、對的市場條件 , 對吧 ? 你們當時應該有成功的 。
from the time tivo came out about eight or nine years ago to this current day , they are the single highestquality product on the market , hands down , there is no dispute .	大約在八、九年前 , 當tivo上市時 , 到現在這一天 , 他們是市場上唯一的高品質產品 , 手下有手 , 沒有糾紛 。
they were extremely wellfunded .	他們極其受資助 。
market conditions were fantastic .	市場條件太棒了 。
i mean , we use tivo as verb .	我的意思是 , 我們把tivo當作動詞
i tivo stuff on my piece of junk time warner dvr all the time .	我tivo東西在我的垃圾時間vr上
but tivo's a commercial failure .	但tivo卻是種商業故障 。
they've never made money .	他們從來沒有賺到錢 。
and when they went ipo , their stock was at about 30 or 40 dollars and then plummeted , and it's never traded above 10 .	他們去ipo的時候他們的股票價值約30到40美元 , 然後就跌幅 , 從沒在10美元以上交易 。
in fact , i don't think it's even traded above six , except for a couple of little spikes .	事實上 , 我想它甚至比不上6 , 只不過幾次小漲幅 。
because you see , when tivo launched their product they told us all what they had .	因為你看 , 當tivo推出他們的產品他們告訴我們他們擁有的是什麼
they said , " we have a product that pauses live tv , skips commercials , rewinds live tv and memorizes your viewing habits without you even asking . "	他們說: 「 我們有一項產品可以暫停現場的電視節目 , 跳過廣告 , 讓現場電視節目重播 , 讓收視習慣連你都不問 。 」
and the cynical majority said , " we don't believe you .	那個憤世嫉俗的大多數說: 「 我們不相信你 。
we don't need it . we don't like it .	我們不需要它 , 我們不喜歡它
you're scaring us . "	你嚇著我們 。 」
what if they had said , " if you're the kind of person who likes to have total control over every aspect of your life , boy , do we have a product for you .	如果他們說: 「 若你是那種喜歡完全掌控生活的各個層面的人 , 那麼 , 我們有一項產品要給你嗎 ?
it pauses live tv , skips commercials , memorizes your viewing habits , etc . , etc . "	它可以暫停現場節目 , 跳過商業廣告 , 記下你的收視習慣等等 。 」
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it , and what you do simply serves as the proof of what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼而你做什麼僅僅是你相信什麼的證明
now let me give you a successful example of the law of diffusion of innovation .	現在讓我舉一個成功的例子 , 說明創意的散播法則 。
in the summer of 1963 , 250 , 000 people showed up on the mall in washington to hear dr . king speak .	1963年夏天 , 二十五萬人出現在華盛頓的商場上 , 聽金恩博士演說 。
they sent out no invitations , and there was no website to check the date .	他們沒有寄出任何一張邀請函而當時也沒有網站去查看日期
how do you do that ?	要怎麼做呢 ?
well , dr . king wasn't the only man in america who was a great orator .	金恩博士不是在美國唯一一個偉大的演說家
he wasn't the only man in america who suffered in a precivil rights america .	他不是在美國唯一一個受到其害的人在美國境內
in fact , some of his ideas were bad .	事實上 , 他的一些想法很壞 。
but he had a gift .	但他有一個禮物 。
he didn't go around telling people what needed to change in america .	他沒有到處告訴人們在美國什麼需要改變 。
he went around and told people what he believed .	他到處告訴人們他所相信的
" i believe , i believe , i believe , " he told people .	" 我相信 , 我相信 , 我相信 " 他告訴人們
and people who believed what he believed took his cause , and they made it their own , and they told people .	而那些相信他所相信的人們把他的成因拿走了他們讓它成為他們自己的 , 他們告訴人們
and some of those people created structures to get the word out to even more people .	有些人創造了結構 , 把字詞傳給更多人 。
and lo and behold , 250 , 000 people showed up on the right day at the right time to hear him speak .	然後你瞧 , 25萬人出現在對的日子裡聽著他說話 。
how many of them showed up for him ?	有多少人為了他而出現 ?
they showed up for themselves .	他們為自己出席
it's what they believed about america that got them to travel in a bus for eight hours to stand in the sun in washington in the middle of august .	正是他們所相信的美國使他們坐公車旅行八小時後站在華盛頓的陽光下八月中時
it's what they believed , and it wasn't about black versus white: 25 percent of the audience was white .	這是他們所相信的 , 這不是有關黑人與白人25%的觀眾是白人
dr . king believed that there are two types of laws in this world: those that are made by a higher authority and those that are made by man .	金恩博士相信在這個世界上有兩種定律那些由較高權威制定的人和那些由人類所制訂的法律
and not until all the laws that are made by man are consistent with the laws that are made by the higher authority will we live in a just world .	直到所有人類定律的定律都與高權威制定的法律一致-我們將會活在一個公正的世界 。
it just so happened that the civil rights movement was the perfect thing to help him bring his cause to life .	正是如此 , 民權運動幫助他把自己的理想帶到生活當中 。
we followed , not for him , but for ourselves .	我們追隨 , 不是為了他 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and , by the way , he gave the " i have a dream " speech , not the " i have a plan " speech .	順帶一提 , 他給了他 「 我有一個夢想 」 演講 , 而不是 「 我有一個計畫 」 的演講 。
listen to politicians now , with their comprehensive 12point plans .	現在聽政治人物用他們全心全意的12點計劃
they're not inspiring anybody .	他們沒有激勵任何人 。
because there are leaders and there are those who lead .	因為有領導者也有領導者 。
leaders hold a position of power or authority , but those who lead inspire us .	領導者持有權力或權威的地位 , 但是能啟發我們的人 。
whether they're individuals or organizations , we follow those who lead , not because we have to , but because we want to .	不論是個人或組織 , 我們跟隨那些領導的人 , 不是因為我們必須 , 而是因為我們想要 。
we follow those who lead , not for them , but for ourselves .	我們跟隨那些領導的人 , 不是為了他們而是為了我們自己
and it's those who start with " why " that have the ability to inspire those around them or find others who inspire them .	正是那些以 「 為什麼 」 開頭的人 , 有能力激發他們周圍的人 , 或找那些激勵他們的人 。
how do you remember where you parked your car ? how do you know if you're moving in the right direction ? neuroscientist neil burgess studies the neural mechanisms that map the space around us , and how they link to memory and imagination .	你怎麼記得你把車子停在哪裡 ? 你怎麼知道你是不是在往對的方向前進 ? 神經科學家尼爾伯特斯研究了我們周遭空間的神經機制 , 及他們如何連結記憶與想像力 。
brain , cognitive science , exploration , neuroscience , science	大腦、認知科學、探索、神經科學、科學 。
neil burgess: how your brain tells you where you are	尼爾伯斯:你的大腦如何告訴你你在哪裡 。
when we park in a big parking lot , how do we remember where we parked our car ?	當我們停在一個很大的停車場 , 我們怎麼記住我們停的車位 ?
here's the problem facing homer .	荷馬面臨的問題是
and we're going to try to understand what's happening in his brain .	而且我們會試著去了解他的大腦到底發生了什麼事 。
so we'll start with the hippocampus , shown in yellow , which is the organ of memory .	我們先從海馬體開始 , 圖中黃色部分是記憶的器官
if you have damage there , like in alzheimer's , you can't remember things including where you parked your car .	如果你的車因此受損 , 比如阿茲海默症 , 你就無法記住東西 , 包括你停車的地方 。
it's named after latin for " seahorse , " which it resembles .	它的名字取自拉丁文的 「 海馬 」 , 和海馬相似 。
and like the rest of the brain , it's made of neurons .	和大腦的其他部分一樣 , 它是由神經元所組成的 。
so the human brain has about a hundred billion neurons in it .	所以人腦大概有上千億的神經元在裡面
and the neurons communicate with each other by sending little pulses or spikes of electricity via connections to each other .	神經元會彼此溝通藉由脈衝或電的突波彼此連接
the hippocampus is formed of two sheets of cells , which are very densely interconnected .	海馬體是由兩片細胞彼此非常緊密的連結組成
and scientists have begun to understand how spatial memory works by recording from individual neurons in rats or mice while they forage or explore an environment looking for food .	科學家們開始了解空間的記憶是如何運作的 , 藉由記錄老鼠在覓食或探索環境時 , 觀察出老鼠個別的神經元如何運作 。
so we're going to imagine we're recording from a single neuron in the hippocampus of this rat here .	所以 , 我們要想像我們紀錄的是一隻單一神經元在這隻老鼠的海馬體上 。
and when it fires a little spike of electricity , there's going to be a red dot and a click .	而當它發出了點電流 , 就會有一個紅點和一個點 。
so what we see is that this neuron knows whenever the rat has gone into one particular place in its environment .	我們可以看到這個神經元知道每當老鼠進入某一特定的環境時
and it signals to the rest of the brain by sending a little electrical spike .	並藉由電的突波向大腦其他部位發出訊號 。
so we could show the firing rate of that neuron as a function of the animal's location .	所以我們可以把那神經元的發射率表現為動物所在位置的功能 。
and if we record from lots of different neurons , we'll see that different neurons fire when the animal goes in different parts of its environment , like in this square box shown here .	如果我們從很多不同的神經中紀錄 , 我們會看到當動物走進不同的環境時 , 神經元會發出訊號 , 就像這個方框所顯示的 。
so together they form a map for the rest of the brain , telling the brain continually , " where am i now within my environment ? "	所以 , 它們一起形成了地圖 , 為大腦的其他部分建構出地圖 , 持續告訴大腦: 「 我現在在我的環境中的哪裡 ? 」
place cells are also being recorded in humans .	人類身上的位置細胞也會被記錄下來 。
so epilepsy patients sometimes need the electrical activity in their brain monitoring .	所以癲癇患者有時需要他們大腦裡的電活動來監測
and some of these patients played a video game where they drive around a small town .	有些病患會玩一個電玩遊戲讓他們在一個小鎮上開車
and place cells in their hippocampi would fire , become active , start sending electrical impulses whenever they drove through a particular location in that town .	海馬體中的 " 位置細胞 " 會被激發 , 開始發射電子脈衝當它們行駛於那個小鎮的一個特定位置
so how does a place cell know where the rat or person is within its environment ?	所以 , 位置細胞要如何知道老鼠或人在環境中的位置 ?
well these two cells here show us that the boundaries of the environment are particularly important .	這兩個細胞告訴我們環境的界線是特別重要的
so the one on the top likes to fire sort of midway between the walls of the box that their rat's in .	上方的那一隻喜歡在自己老鼠的箱子中間發出一些火花
and when you expand the box , the firing location expands .	而當你將箱子擴大時 , 激發的位置也會跟著變大 。
the one below likes to fire whenever there's a wall close by to the south .	下面的那面 , 則是每當南方靠近一面牆的時候 , 都喜歡被激發 。
and if you put another wall inside the box , then the cell fires in both place wherever there's a wall to the south as the animal explores around in its box .	如果你在盒子裡放置另一道牆那細胞在這兩個地方都會被激發每當動物在盒子裡在南方有一面牆的時候都會一面向南 。
so this predicts that sensing the distances and directions of boundaries around you extended buildings and so on is particularly important for the hippocampus .	所以 , 這預測到 , 在你周遭的範圍內 , 會感應到邊界的距離和方向 , 且會延伸到建築物等等 , 對海馬迴特別重要 。
and indeed , on the inputs to the hippocampus , cells are found which project into the hippocampus , which do respond exactly to detecting boundaries or edges at particular distances and directions from the rat or mouse as it's exploring around .	的確 , 接收到海馬體的輸入後 , 細胞就會在海馬體中找到哪些項目 , 會針對老鼠的身體或邊緣作出回應 , 尤其是從老鼠或其他地方 , 來偵測周圍的界線和邊緣 。
so the cell on the left , you can see , it fires whenever the animal gets near to a wall or a boundary to the east , whether it's the edge or the wall of a square box or the circular wall of the circular box or even the drop at the edge of a table , which the animals are running around .	所以左邊的細胞 , 你們可以看到 , 當動物接近一面牆 , 或一條向東邊的界線時 , 會被激發 , 不論是方形盒子的邊緣 , 或是圓形外牆 , 甚至是桌邊的邊緣 , 這些動物跑來跑去 。
and the cell on the right there fires whenever there's a boundary to the south , whether it's the drop at the edge of the table or a wall or even the gap between two tables that are pulled apart .	右邊的細胞會當南方的界線被激發 , 不論是桌子的邊緣還是牆壁 , 甚至是兩張桌子之間的落差 。
so that's one way in which we think place cells determine where the animal is as it's exploring around .	所以我們認為位置細胞可以決定動物在四周探索的位置
we can also test where we think objects are , like this goal flag , in simple environments or indeed , where your car would be .	我們也能測試我們認為物品的位置 , 像是這個目標旗 , 在簡單的環境中或是你的車會放在哪裡 。
so we can have people explore an environment and see the location they have to remember .	所以 , 我們可以讓人們去探索一個環境 , 並觀察他們需要記住的位置 。
and then , if we put them back in the environment , generally they're quite good at putting a marker down where they thought that flag or their car was .	接著 , 如果我們把它們放回環境中 , 一般來說 , 它們很能放下標記 , 讓它們以為是旗幟或車輛的地方 。
but on some trials , we could change the shape and size of the environment like we did with the place cell .	但在一些試驗中 , 我們可以像我們使用位置細胞一樣改變環境的形狀和大小 。
in that case , we can see how where they think the flag had been changes as a function of how you change the shape and size of the environment .	在那樣的情況下 , 我們可以看到他們認為旗幟位置的改變是如何改變環境的形狀和大小 。
and what you see , for example , if the flag was where that cross was in a small square environment , and then if you ask people where it was , but you've made the environment bigger , where they think the flag had been stretches out in exactly the same way that the place cell firing stretched out .	你可以看到 , 舉例來說 , 如果旗子在小方形的環境中那個交叉點的地方 , 然後如果你去問人在哪裡 , 但是你讓環境變大了 , 他們認為旗幟的位置和位置細胞激發的位置完全相同 ,
it's as if you remember where the flag was by storing the pattern of firing across all of your place cells at that location , and then you can get back to that location by moving around so that you best match the current pattern of firing of your place cells with that stored pattern .	這就好像你還記得旗子在那個位置的各個位置細胞被激發時的樣子 , 然後你就可以藉由四處移動回到那個位置 , 這樣你就可以最好地去匹配目前位置細胞被激發的模式以那種儲存模式 。
that guides you back to the location that you want to remember .	那會引導你回到你想要記住的位置 。
but we also know where we are through movement .	但我們也知道我們透過動作的位置 。
so if we take some outbound path perhaps we park and we wander off we know because our own movements , which we can integrate over this path roughly what the heading direction is to go back .	所以如果我們採取一些有限的路徑──也許我們會停車 , 閒逛──我們會了解因為我們自己的動作 , 我們可以整合這條路 , 大致上就是要回頭的方向 。
and place cells also get this kind of path integration input from a kind of cell called a grid cell .	位置細胞也會從一種叫做網格細胞的細胞得到這種路徑融合 。
now grid cells are found , again , on the inputs to the hippocampus , and they're a bit like place cells .	目前網格細胞同樣也在海馬體的輸入上找到它們有點像位置細胞
but now as the rat explores around , each individual cell fires in a whole array of different locations which are laid out across the environment in an amazingly regular triangular grid .	但當老鼠四處探索時每個細胞會激發一系列不同位置的不同位置並在一個奇妙的三角形網格中標出
and if you record from several grid cells shown here in different colors each one has a gridlike firing pattern across the environment , and each cell's gridlike firing pattern is shifted slightly relative to the other cells .	如果從這邊以不同顏色標出的數個網格細胞記錄下 , 每個細胞的網格雷射激發模式 , 相對於其他細胞 , 會稍微改變 。
so the red one fires on this grid and the green one on this one and the blue on on this one .	紅色的會在這個網格上發射 , 而綠色的會在這個上面 , 藍色的會在上面 。
so together , it's as if the rat can put a virtual grid of firing locations across its environment a bit like the latitude and longitude lines that you'd find on a map , but using triangles .	綜合起來 , 就好像老鼠可以在周遭的環境中放置一個虛擬的網格 。 有點像你在地圖上找到的緯度和長度線 , 但用的是三角形 。
and as it moves around , the electrical activity can pass from one of these cells to the next cell to keep track of where it is , so that it can use its own movements to know where it is in its environment .	當它到處移動時 , 電流會從其中一個細胞傳遞到下一個細胞 , 讓它能追蹤到它的所在位置 , 讓它可以用它自己的動作 , 知道它在環境中的位置 。
do people have grid cells ?	人們有格子細胞嗎 ?
well because all of the gridlike firing patterns have the same axes of symmetry , the same orientations of grid , shown in orange here , it means that the net activity of all of the grid cells in a particular part of the brain should change according to whether we're running along these six directions or running along one of the six directions in between .	嗯 , 因為所有網格雷射激發的圖案都有相同的對稱軸 , 在這裡都是同一個網格 , 以橘色顯示 , 表示所有網格細胞的淨活動在大腦特定的某一個部位應該會根據我們在這六個方向中間的移動而改變 , 還是沿著六個方向在運行 。
so we can put people in an mri scanner and have them do a little video game like the one i showed you and look for this signal .	所以我們可以把人放進核磁共振掃描儀 , 讓他們做一個小小的電玩遊戲 , 就像我剛剛給你們看的那種 , 然後去找這個訊號 。
and indeed , you do see it in the human entorhinal cortex , which is the same part of the brain that you see grid cells in rats .	的確 , 你在人類的腦皮層也看到了 , 老鼠的格狀細胞也一樣 。
so back to homer .	回到荷馬 。
he's probably remembering where his car was in terms of the distances and directions to extended buildings and boundaries around the location where he parked .	他可能還記得他的車子的位置 , 在他停車的位置和方向上 , 將建築物和邊界往外延伸 。
and that would be represented by the firing of boundarydetecting cells .	可以用邊界偵測細胞來表示 。
he's also remembering the path he took out of the car park , which would be represented in the firing of grid cells .	他也想起了他走出停車場的路徑 , 這會在發射網格細胞時呈現出來 。
now both of these kinds of cells can make the place cells fire .	這兩種細胞都可以使位置細胞被激發
and he can return to the location where he parked by moving so as to find where it is that best matches the firing pattern of the place cells in his brain currently with the stored pattern where he parked his car .	他可以藉由移動 , 回到他停車的位置找到目前位置為止 , 位置與他正在他大腦中被激發的位置細胞圖案 , 與他停車的地方一樣 。
and that guides him back to that location irrespective of visual cues like whether his car's actually there .	那會引導他回到那個位置 , 不考慮用視覺提示的方式 , 比如他的車是否真的在 。
maybe it's been towed .	或許已經是高塔上了 。
but he knows where it was , so he knows to go and get it .	但他知道它在哪裡 , 所以他知道要去抓它 。
so beyond spatial memory , if we look for this gridlike firing pattern throughout the whole brain , we see it in a whole series of locations which are always active when we do all kinds of autobiographical memory tasks , like remembering the last time you went to a wedding , for example .	所以除了空間記憶之外 , 如果我們從整個大腦中尋找這種網格狀的發射模式 , 我們看到一系列的位置 , 總是在我們進行各種自傳記憶任務時活躍起來 , 像是回憶你上次參加婚禮時的反應 。
so it may be that the neural mechanisms for representing the space around us are also used for generating visual imagery so that we can recreate the spatial scene , at least , of the events that have happened to us when we want to imagine them .	所以 , 可能就是代表我們周圍空間的神經機制也被用來產生視覺影像 , 讓我們能夠重現現現有的空間場景 , 至少 , 當我們想要想像這些事件時 , 已經發生在我們身上的那些事件 。
so if this was happening , your memories could start by place cells activating each other via these dense interconnections and then reactivating boundary cells to create the spatial structure of the scene around your viewpoint .	所以 , 如果這正在發生 , 你的記憶可以從位置細胞開始互相啟動 , 通過這些緊密的相互連結 , 接著重新啟動邊界細胞 , 來創造出你觀點周圍的空間結構 。
and grid cells could move this viewpoint through that space .	網格細胞可以透過這個空間移動這個視野 。
another kind of cell , head direction cells , which i didn't mention yet , they fire like a compass according to which way you're facing .	另一種我還沒提到的細胞頭部方向細胞 , 它們就像是指南針一樣 , 根據你所面對的方向來激發 。
they could define the viewing direction from which you want to generate an image for your visual imagery , so you can imagine what happened when you were at this wedding , for example .	他們可以定義一個你想要為你的視覺影像產生的方向 , 所以你可以想像當你在這場婚禮時發生了什麼事 , 舉例來說 。
so this is just one example of a new era really in cognitive neuroscience where we're beginning to understand psychological processes like how you remember or imagine or even think in terms of the actions of the billions of individual neurons that make up our brains .	所以 , 這只是在認知神經科學中的一個新時代的一個例子 , 我們開始了解心理的過程 , 比如你如何記住、想像 , 甚至思考數十億個獨立的神經元所採取的行動 。
thank you very much .	非常感謝 。
imagine a global security driven by collaboration among agencies , government , the private sector and the public . that's not just the distant hope of opensource fans , it's the vision of james stavridis , the supreme commander of nato , who shares vivid moments from recent military history to explain why security of the future should be built with bridges rather than walls .	想像一個全球安全的驅使 , 由政府部門 , 私營機構和公眾所推動的 , 不只是開放原始碼的粉絲 , 也是詹姆士斯•史特里迪里斯所帶領的遠景 , 北約最高總統也在近期歷史上分享鮮明的時刻來解釋 , 為什麼未來的安全應該要用橋來建造 , 而不是用牆 。
collaboration , global issues , opensource , peace , politics , social media , violence , war	合作、全球議題、開放資源、和平、政治、社交媒體、暴力、戰爭、戰爭 。
james stavridis: how nato's supreme commander thinks about global security	詹姆斯•斯塔維里得斯:北約的最高指揮官對全球安全的看法如何 。
i'm gonna talk a little bit about opensource security , because we've got to get better at security in this 21st century .	我要講一些開放原始碼的安全性 , 因為在21世紀 , 我們必須在安全方面做得更好 。
let me start by saying , let's look back to the 20th century , and kind of get a sense of how that style of security worked for us .	讓我先回顧一下二十世紀 , 有點像是了解安全風格對我們來說是如何運作的 。
this is verdun , a battlefield in france just north of the nato headquarters in belgium .	這是verdun , 一個法國的戰場 , 就在北約在比利時總部的北邊 。
at verdun , in 1916 , over a 300day period , 700 , 000 people were killed , so about 2 , 000 a day .	在1916年的verdun , 超過三百天 , 七十萬人被殺 , 所以大約二千人一天 。
if you roll it forward 20thcentury security into the second world war , you see the battle of stalingrad , 300 days , 2 million people killed .	如果再向前推進二十世紀的安全 , 進入第二次世界大戰 , 你看到在斯大林格勒的戰役 , 300天內有兩千萬人死亡 。
we go into the cold war , and we continue to try and build walls .	我們進入冷戰 , 繼續建造圍牆 。
we go from the trench warfare of the first world war to the maginot line of the second world war , and then we go into the cold war , the iron curtain , the berlin wall .	我們從一戰的壕溝 , 到二戰的馬基線 , 再到冷戰中的鐵幕 , 柏林牆 。
my thesis for us today is , instead of building walls to create security , we need to build bridges .	我今天的主題是 , 我們不需要建造牆壁來創造安全 , 我們需要建造橋樑 。
this is a famous bridge in europe .	這是歐洲一座著名的橋
it's the bridge over the drina river , the subject of a novel by ivo andrić , and it talks about how , in that very troubled part of europe and the balkans , over time there's been enormous building of walls .	它是draina河的橋梁 , 由ivoandrigo設計的小說的主題 , 它談到如何在歐洲和巴爾幹地區非常麻煩的部分 , 經過一段時間又建了巨大的牆 。
more recently , in the last decade , we begin to see these communities start , hesitatingly , to come together .	更近期 , 在過去十年 , 我們開始看到這些社區開始 , 盡管有些猶豫不決 , 要團結起來 。
